* **Associated Passages:** MAT 8:19
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 8:20 (id: 22250)

Following Jesus is not easy; it involves more than intellectual mastery. Following Jesus entails being willing to forgo life’s normal comforts.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 8:20
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 8:21 (id: 22251)

Another of his disciples: This statement suggests that the teacher of [8:19](https://ref.ly/Matt8:19) was a disciple as well. Lord suggests a stronger commitment to Jesus. • bury my father: This was one of the highest religious duties in Judaism, but Jesus requires total commitment to him.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 8:21
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 8:22 (id: 22252)

Let the spiritually dead bury their own dead: Jesus’ opponents would have misconstrued this instruction as blatant disregard for the fifth commandment to honor one’s parents ([Exod 20:12](https://ref.ly/Exod20:12)), but in essence it is a restatement of the first commandment ([Exod 20:1–3](https://ref.ly/Exod20:1-Exod20:3)). It was warranted by Jesus’ messianic authority and the impact of the Kingdom upon normal human life, including family ties and commitments (see [Matt 10:34–39](https://ref.ly/Matt10:34-Matt10:39); [12:46–50](https://ref.ly/Matt12:46-Matt12:50); [19:29](https://ref.ly/Matt19:29); [Zech 13:3](https://ref.ly/Zech13:3); [Luke 14:26–27](https://ref.ly/Luke14:26-Luke14:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 8:22
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 8:23–27 (id: 22253)

The episode at sea extends the theme of what true discipleship involves. The storm challenged the disciples to entrust their very lives to Jesus for protection and deliverance. Jesus even has authority over dangerous weather and the sea (see [Job 38:8–11](https://ref.ly/Job38:8-Job38:11); [Pss 29](https://ref.ly/Ps29:1-Ps29:11); [65:1–13](https://ref.ly/Ps65:1-Ps65:13); [89:9](https://ref.ly/Ps89:9); [107:23–32](https://ref.ly/Ps107:23-Ps107:32)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 8:23–MAT 8:27
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 8:24 (id: 22254)

a fierce storm struck the lake: Sudden squalls are common on the Sea of Galilee, which is among mountains.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 8:24
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 8:27 (id: 22255)

Who is this man? Salvation requires a proper answer to this question and active faith in him. Jesus’ disciples had still failed to understand.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 8:27
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 8:28 (id: 22257)

possessed by demons … so violent: Demon\-possession was often accompanied by violence, revulsion at the presence of the Son of God ([8:29](https://ref.ly/Matt8:29)), inability to speak ([9:32](https://ref.ly/Matt9:32); [12:22](https://ref.ly/Matt12:22)), blindness ([12:22](https://ref.ly/Matt12:22)), seizures ([17:15](https://ref.ly/Matt17:15)), and self\-destructive behavior ([17:15](https://ref.ly/Matt17:15)). With Jesus’ exorcisms, the power of the Kingdom broke into human history ([12:28](https://ref.ly/Matt12:28)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 8:28
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 8:28–34 (id: 22256)

This episode focuses on Jesus’ authority as well as on the cost of following him; those who walk by faith will, like the Messiah, also experience opposition.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 8:28–MAT 8:34
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 8:29 (id: 22258)

Those controlled by Satan immediately recognized Jesus’ true identity as the Son of God (see [Mark 1:24](https://ref.ly/Mark1:24)) and answered the question asked by Jesus’ disciples when he had calmed the storm ([Matt 8:27](https://ref.ly/Matt8:27)). Elsewhere, Jesus’ true nature and identity are acknowledged by the Father ([3:17](https://ref.ly/Matt3:17); [17:5](https://ref.ly/Matt17:5)), Satan ([4:3](https://ref.ly/Matt4:3), [6](https://ref.ly/Matt4:6)), humans ([14:33](https://ref.ly/Matt14:33); [16:16](https://ref.ly/Matt16:16); [27:54](https://ref.ly/Matt27:54)), and Christ himself ([11:27](https://ref.ly/Matt11:27); [24:36](https://ref.ly/Matt24:36); [28:19](https://ref.ly/Matt28:19)). • God’s appointed time is the final, eternal damnation of all who oppose God (see [Jude 1:6](https://ref.ly/Jude1:6); [Rev 20:10](https://ref.ly/Rev20:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 8:29
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 8:31 (id: 22260)

The demons were no match for Jesus’ authority; they desperately begged to avoid imminent doom.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 8:31
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 8:32 (id: 22261)

Jesus’ word had sufficient authority to expel demons. • drowned: Jesus had begun to defeat the enemy ([12:28](https://ref.ly/Matt12:28); [Luke 10:17–20](https://ref.ly/Luke10:17-Luke10:20); [Rom 16:20](https://ref.ly/Rom16:20); [Col 2:15](https://ref.ly/Col2:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 8:32
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 8:34 (id: 22262)

The tragedy of the incident is that those who witnessed the Son of God’s power to give salvation feared having their world upset, so they rejected him.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 8:34
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:1 (id: 22277)

His own town was Capernaum ([Mark 2:1](https://ref.ly/Mark2:1)), where he apparently relocated from Nazareth after being rejected there ([Matt 4:13](https://ref.ly/Matt4:13); [Luke 4:16–31](https://ref.ly/Luke4:16-Luke4:31)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:1
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:1–17 (id: 22269)

Controversy ensued among Jesus’ opponents, the teachers of religious law and Pharisees ([9:1–13](https://ref.ly/Matt9:1-Matt9:13)), and among the disciples of John the Baptist ([9:14–17](https://ref.ly/Matt9:14-Matt9:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:1–MAT 9:17
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:3 (id: 22290)

Does he think he’s God? God alone could forgive sins ([Ps 103:3](https://ref.ly/Ps103:3); [Isa 43:25](https://ref.ly/Isa43:25); [Jer 50:20](https://ref.ly/Jer50:20)). The teachers of religious law failed to comprehend Jesus’ mission as God’s incarnate Son ([Matt 3:17](https://ref.ly/Matt3:17); [11:25–27](https://ref.ly/Matt11:25-Matt11:27)). As God’s Messiah ([1:1](https://ref.ly/Matt1:1); [11:2–6](https://ref.ly/Matt11:2-Matt11:6)), he was saving mankind ([8:17](https://ref.ly/Matt8:17); [26:26–28](https://ref.ly/Matt26:26-Matt26:28)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:3
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:5 (id: 22291)

It is easier for Jesus to pronounce forgiveness, since that might have no verifiable effects; it is harder to enable a paralytic to walk. The miracle, visible to all, corroborates Jesus’ authority to forgive sins and forces all who witness it to decide about Jesus.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:5
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:6 (id: 22292)

So I will prove: Jesus performed the miracle to reveal his authority and identity as God’s Messiah (see [11:2–6](https://ref.ly/Matt11:2-Matt11:6); [12:28](https://ref.ly/Matt12:28)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:6
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:8 (id: 22293)

The crowd responded with fear and admiration because they realized a powerful truth about Jesus. He is truly the Son of God with the authority to forgive sins on earth ([9:6](https://ref.ly/Matt9:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:8
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:9 (id: 22295)

Another name for the apostle Matthew was "Levi" ([Mark 2:14](https://ref.ly/Mark2:14)). He might have had two names, or Jesus might have given him a new name.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:9
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:9–13 (id: 22294)

Jesus, as Lord and Messiah, tore down the barriers that prevented righteous Jews from intermingling with those who were unclean or sinful.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:9–MAT 9:13
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:10 (id: 22270)

The Jewish people despised Jewish tax collectors ([5:46–47](https://ref.ly/Matt5:46-Matt5:47); [18:15–20](https://ref.ly/Matt18:15-Matt18:20)), who cooperated with Roman oppressors and were considered betrayers of the Israelite nation. Many also considered them unclean because of their frequent contact with Gentiles and because of the idolatrous images on Roman coins. Tax\-collection was a private enterprise. In each district, Rome granted the right to collect taxes to the highest bidder (cp. [Luke 19:1–10](https://ref.ly/Luke19:1-Luke19:10)). Anything collected above the bid was profit for the collectors, who, driven by greed, often used extortion.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:10
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:13 (id: 22271)

I want you to show mercy, not offer sacrifices: God’s desire is applied to the question of table fellowship with sinners; Jesus’ mercy in eating with sinners contrasts with the Pharisees’ separation from sinners (symbolized as sacrifices). • Jesus revealed the true spiritual condition of the Pharisees, who think they are righteous*;* they failed to recognize that they were in fact unrighteous and in need of the Messiah’s salvation. See [7:1–5](https://ref.ly/Matt7:1-Matt7:5); [8:11–12](https://ref.ly/Matt8:11-Matt8:12); [19:30](https://ref.ly/Matt19:30); [20:16](https://ref.ly/Matt20:16); [21:43](https://ref.ly/Matt21:43).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:13
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:14 (id: 22272)

fast: Fasting expressed personal humility and repentance ([2 Sam 12:16–23](https://ref.ly/2Sam12:16-2Sam12:23); [Dan 9:3](https://ref.ly/Dan9:3)). It called attention to the national need for repentance ([Lev 16:29–31](https://ref.ly/Lev16:29-Lev16:31); [Neh 9:1](https://ref.ly/Neh9:1)) and probably sought to hasten the arrival of the Messiah through purification. The fact that Jesus and his disciples did not fast ([Matt 11:18–19](https://ref.ly/Matt11:18-Matt11:19)) subtly proclaimed that the Messiah had already arrived (see also [6:16](https://ref.ly/Matt6:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:14
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:15 (id: 22273)

wedding guests … groom: John the Baptist had also described the Messiah and his disciples in this way ([John 3:29](https://ref.ly/John3:29)), drawing on Old Testament imagery to reveal Jesus’ status (see [Matt 25:1–13](https://ref.ly/Matt25:1-Matt25:13); [Isa 54:5–6](https://ref.ly/Isa54:5-Isa54:6)). • taken away: This is Jesus’ first prediction of his violent death (see [Matt 16:21](https://ref.ly/Matt16:21); [17:12](https://ref.ly/Matt17:12), [22–23](https://ref.ly/Matt17:22-Matt17:23); [20:18–19](https://ref.ly/Matt20:18-Matt20:19); [26:2](https://ref.ly/Matt26:2), [26–35](https://ref.ly/Matt26:26-Matt26:35); [Isa 53:8](https://ref.ly/Isa53:8)). • then they will fast: Jesus may be referring to the disciples’ sorrow immediately after his crucifixion, or to the disciples’ lifestyle after his death and resurrection (see [Acts 9:9](https://ref.ly/Acts9:9); [13:2–3](https://ref.ly/Acts13:2-Acts13:3); [14:23](https://ref.ly/Acts14:23); [27:9](https://ref.ly/Acts27:9), [33](https://ref.ly/Acts27:33)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:15
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:16–17 (id: 22274)

These riddle\-like parables contrast the new covenant that Jesus has established ([26:26–29](https://ref.ly/Matt26:26-Matt26:29)) with the old covenant, especially in relation to such rituals as fasting. Jesus consummates, but does not abolish, the law ([5:17–20](https://ref.ly/Matt5:17-Matt5:20); see [Gal 2:21](https://ref.ly/Gal2:21); [5:4](https://ref.ly/Gal5:4)). Yet the new covenant requires new practices.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:16–MAT 9:17
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:18 (id: 22276)

lay your hand on her: The laying\-on of hands is a visible symbol of prayer for God’s power to flow into someone, often resulting in new life or ministries ([19:13](https://ref.ly/Matt19:13); [Num 27:18–23](https://ref.ly/Num27:18-Num27:23); [Deut 34:9](https://ref.ly/Deut34:9)). • The man believed that Jesus had the power to raise the dead (cp. [1 Kgs 17:8–24](https://ref.ly/1Kgs17:8-1Kgs17:24); [2 Kgs 4:18–37](https://ref.ly/2Kgs4:18-2Kgs4:37)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:18
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:18–34 (id: 22275)

Jesus is the Messiah whose power knows no boundaries. He calls people to have faith in him.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:18–MAT 9:34
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:20 (id: 22278)

The woman’s constant bleeding rendered her always ceremonially unclean and made whoever she touched unclean as well ([Lev 15:25–30](https://ref.ly/Lev15:25-Lev15:30)). But instead of rendering Jesus unclean, her touching him made her clean, a stunning reversal that illustrates Jesus’ power to redeem and sanctify (see [Matt 14:36](https://ref.ly/Matt14:36); [Mark 3:10](https://ref.ly/Mark3:10)). • fringe: The tassels at the bottom of a tunic ([Matt 23:5](https://ref.ly/Matt23:5); [Num 15:37–41](https://ref.ly/Num15:37-Num15:41)) reminded Jews to live in accord with God’s law.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:20
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:22 (id: 22279)

Your faith has made you well (literally *has saved you)*: Physical healing demonstrated her spiritual salvation (see [8:17](https://ref.ly/Matt8:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:22
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:23 (id: 22280)

*the flute players and the noisy crowd*: people publicly expressed their sorrow over a family member's death. This happened with music and laments by professional mourners. “Even the poorest in Israel should hire at least two flutes and one wailing woman” (*Mishnah Ketubbot* 4:4\).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:23
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:24 (id: 22281)

Though she was physically dead, from Jesus’ perspective the girl was just asleep—she would soon be raised back to life (see [Isa 26:19](https://ref.ly/Isa26:19); [John 11:11–14](https://ref.ly/John11:11-John11:14), [25](https://ref.ly/John11:25); [1 Thes 4:14](https://ref.ly/1Thess4:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:24
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:27 (id: 22282)

Eye diseases were common in the ancient world. Blindness was often considered to be divine punishment (see [Exod 4:11](https://ref.ly/Exod4:11); [Deut 28:28](https://ref.ly/Deut28:28); [2 Kgs 6:18](https://ref.ly/2Kgs6:18); [John 9:2–3](https://ref.ly/John9:2-John9:3)). The Old Testament predicts that the Messiah’s coming would bring restoration of sight for the blind ([Matt 11:4–5](https://ref.ly/Matt11:4-Matt11:5); [Isa 29:18–19](https://ref.ly/Isa29:18-Isa29:19); [35:5–6](https://ref.ly/Isa35:5-Isa35:6)). • Son of David is a messianic title particularly associated with miraculous healings (see [Matt 1:1](https://ref.ly/Matt1:1); [12:23](https://ref.ly/Matt12:23); [15:22](https://ref.ly/Matt15:22); [20:30–31](https://ref.ly/Matt20:30-Matt20:31); [2 Sam 7:12–16](https://ref.ly/2Sam7:12-2Sam7:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:27
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:28 (id: 22283)

Jesus intended his question to elicit confessions of faith from the two men.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:28
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:32 (id: 22285)

Enabling the deaf to hear and the mute to speak is a sign of the Kingdom of God ([11:4–5](https://ref.ly/Matt11:4-Matt11:5); [Isa 35:5–6](https://ref.ly/Isa35:5-Isa35:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:32
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:32–34 (id: 22284)

The Messiah’s acts invoke faith, astonishment, and derisive rejection.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:32–MAT 9:34
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:35 (id: 22287)

This verse connects with the section begun at [4:23](https://ref.ly/Matt4:23). Matthew has presented Jesus to his readers as the Messiah who teaches, preaches, heals, casts out demons, and calls for a decisive response of faith.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:35
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:35–11.1 (id: 22286)

Jesus here extends his ministry (shown in [4:23–9:34](https://ref.ly/Matt4:23-Matt9:34)) to others within Israel through his disciples ([10:5–6](https://ref.ly/Matt10:5-Matt10:6)). Jesus’ instructions to his disciples ([10:5–42](https://ref.ly/Matt10:5-Matt10:42)) focus on missionary activity and its consequent opposition and hardship.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:35–MAT 11:1
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:36 (id: 22288)

like sheep without a shepherd: Jesus lamented the Pharisees’ pastoral negligence (see [12:11–12](https://ref.ly/Matt12:11-Matt12:12); [18:12](https://ref.ly/Matt18:12)). Their attacks against Jesus were a clear indication of their hard\-hearted rejection of God. The crowds languished due to pastoral neglect and mistreatment ([10:5–6](https://ref.ly/Matt10:5-Matt10:6); [15:12–14](https://ref.ly/Matt15:12-Matt15:14); [23:4](https://ref.ly/Matt23:4); [Zech 11:16](https://ref.ly/Zech11:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:36
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 9:37–38 (id: 22289)

Harvest refers to the multitudes (see also [13:24–30](https://ref.ly/Matt13:24-Matt13:30), [36–43](https://ref.ly/Matt13:36-Matt13:43); [Mark 4:26–29](https://ref.ly/Mark4:26-Mark4:29); [John 4:35–38](https://ref.ly/John4:35-John4:38); [Rev 14:15–20](https://ref.ly/Rev14:15-Rev14:20)). • the Lord who is in charge of the harvest: All ministries are ultimately under God’s call (see [Matt 23:8–10](https://ref.ly/Matt23:8-Matt23:10), [13](https://ref.ly/Matt23:13)), so Jesus urges his disciples to pray for God himself to call more workers.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 9:37–MAT 9:38
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:1 (id: 21662)

Jesus called his twelve disciples as workers in the harvest ([9:37–38](https://ref.ly/Matt9:37-Matt9:38)). The choice of twelve is not accidental—it recalls the twelve tribes of Israel. Jesus was appointing new leaders for the new people of God under his reign as Messiah ([16:18–19](https://ref.ly/Matt16:18-Matt16:19); [18:18](https://ref.ly/Matt18:18); [19:28](https://ref.ly/Matt19:28); [21:43](https://ref.ly/Matt21:43)). • gave them authority ([9:6–8](https://ref.ly/Matt9:6-Matt9:8); [28:18](https://ref.ly/Matt28:18)): Jesus enabled the Twelve to perform ministries that the Jewish leaders could not accomplish ([9:32–34](https://ref.ly/Matt9:32-Matt9:34); [10:5–8](https://ref.ly/Matt10:5-Matt10:8)). The authority to cast out evil spirits ([8:28](https://ref.ly/Matt8:28)) and to heal are ascribed to Jesus ([4:23](https://ref.ly/Matt4:23); [8:1–9:35](https://ref.ly/Matt8:1-Matt9:35)) in similar terms.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:1
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:2 (id: 21669)

The apostles are ambassadors or messengers, authorized and sent by an authority to represent and accomplish prescribed tasks (see [10:1–8](https://ref.ly/Matt10:1-Matt10:8), [40](https://ref.ly/Matt10:40); [28:16–20](https://ref.ly/Matt28:16-Matt28:20)). The term is also used for Paul ([Gal 1:1](https://ref.ly/Gal1:1)). • first, Simon (also called Peter): Peter had priority in time ([Matt 4:18–22](https://ref.ly/Matt4:18-Matt4:22); [16:17–19](https://ref.ly/Matt16:17-Matt16:19)) and position as the representative leader of the apostles (see [19:27](https://ref.ly/Matt19:27); [26:33](https://ref.ly/Matt26:33); [Acts 2:14](https://ref.ly/Acts2:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:2
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:2–4 (id: 21663)

The four lists of the apostles (see also [Mark 3:16–19](https://ref.ly/Mark3:16-Mark3:19); [Luke 6:14–16](https://ref.ly/Luke6:14-Luke6:16); [Acts 1:13](https://ref.ly/Acts1:13)) are all different, although the differences are minimal. The order within each list varies slightly, but only the names Thaddaeus ([10:3](https://ref.ly/Matt10:3); [Mark 3:18](https://ref.ly/Mark3:18)) and Judas son of James ([Luke 6:16](https://ref.ly/Luke6:16); [Acts 1:13](https://ref.ly/Acts1:13)) differ. They might be two names for the same man.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:2–MAT 10:4
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:3 (id: 21674)

Matthew (the tax collector) (see [9:9](https://ref.ly/Matt9:9)) is also called Levi ([Mark 2:14](https://ref.ly/Mark2:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:3
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:4 (id: 21677)

the zealot: Zealots were militant Jews who thought violence and war were capable of accomplishing the will of God. As a Jewish nationalist, Simon was probably zealous for the law ([Acts 22:3–5](https://ref.ly/Acts22:3-Acts22:5); [Gal 1:14](https://ref.ly/Gal1:14); [Phil 3:6](https://ref.ly/Phil3:6)). Josephus blamed the Zealot party for the great war with Rome in AD 66–70\. • Iscariot might refer to someone from Kerioth in southern Judea ([Josh 15:25](https://ref.ly/Josh15:25)) or from Kerioth in Perea ([Jer 48:24](https://ref.ly/Jer48:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:4
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:5 (id: 21678)

* *Do not go onto the road of the Gentiles*: At this time, Jesus' mission was limited to the Jews ([Matthew 15:24](https://ref.ly/Matt15:24)). God would reach gentiles (non\-Jewish people) through the Jews ([Isaiah 2:2–4](https://ref.ly/Isa2:2-Isa2:4); [42:6–7](https://ref.ly/Isa42:6-Isa42:7); [49:6](https://ref.ly/Isa49:6); [60:3](https://ref.ly/Isa60:3)).
* Jews saw *Samaritans* as impure Jews ([Luke 17:18](https://ref.ly/Luke17:18)) because they married gentiles during and after the Assyrian and Babylonian exiles ([2 Kings 17:24–41](https://ref.ly/2Kgs17:24-2Kgs17:41)). The tension between Jews and Samaritans grew worse in 128 BC when John Hyrcanus, a Jewish leader, destroyed the Samaritan temple on Mount Gerizim (Josephus, *Antiquities* 13\.9\.1\).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:5
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:6 (id: 21679)

They are *lost* because their shepherds (leaders) neglected them ([9:36](https://ref.ly/Matt9:36); [15:24](https://ref.ly/Matt15:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:6
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:7–8 (id: 21680)

By doing these things in the name and authority of Jesus, the apostles showed that Jesus is the Messiah (see [11:2–6](https://ref.ly/Matt11:2-Matt11:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:7–MAT 10:8
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:8 (id: 21681)

*Freely you have received; freely give:* While payment is not wrong ([1 Corinthians 9:3–19](https://ref.ly/1Cor9:3-1Cor9:19); [Galatians 6:6](https://ref.ly/Gal6:6); [1 Timothy 5:17](https://ref.ly/1Tim5:17)), Jesus encouraged the apostles to avoid appearing greedy (see [Acts 8:20](https://ref.ly/Acts8:20); [20:33](https://ref.ly/Acts20:33)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:8
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:9–10 (id: 21682)

Jesus' disciples should trust God to provide ([6:11](https://ref.ly/Matt6:11), [25–34](https://ref.ly/Matt6:25-Matt6:34); [7:7–11](https://ref.ly/Matt7:7-Matt7:11)). They should avoid greed, which could harm God's reputation. They should also encourage new communities to provide what their leaders need (see [1 Corinthians 9:3–19](https://ref.ly/1Cor9:3-1Cor9:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:9–MAT 10:10
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:12 (id: 21656)

*greet its occupants*: Greetings meant more than just saying "hello." They often included a blessing for the person receiving it (see [Ruth 2:4](https://ref.ly/Ruth2:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:12
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:13 (id: 21657)

* A *worthy home* would accept the message about Jesus and the kingdom of heaven ([10:37–38](https://ref.ly/Matt10:37-Matt10:38); [22:8](https://ref.ly/Matt22:8)).
* The disciples’ blessing was an offer of salvation. Taking back the blessing was a sign of judgment as the offer was removed.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:13
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:14 (id: 21658)

shake its dust from your feet: This prophet\-like gesture is explained by the Israelite custom of expressing displeasure with ungodliness by shaking off Gentile dust whenever crossing the border into Israel. The gesture signifies the disciples’ rejection of those who oppose God’s work (see [Acts 18:6](https://ref.ly/Acts18:6)). Pronouncing judgment on those who reject the message is part of proclaiming the Good News about the Kingdom (see [Matt 11:20–24](https://ref.ly/Matt11:20-Matt11:24); [13:10–15](https://ref.ly/Matt13:10-Matt13:15); [23:37–39](https://ref.ly/Matt23:37-Matt23:39); [24:1–36](https://ref.ly/Matt24:1-Matt24:36)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:14
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:15 (id: 21659)

God destroyed Sodom and Gomorrah for their wickedness ([Gen 18:16–19:29](https://ref.ly/Gen18:16-Gen19:29)). Now, with a more complete revelation in Jesus Christ, a town that rejected the disciples’ preaching would receive a more complete judgment. • such a town: An entire village or city is culpable when a significant majority rejects the message (see [Acts 13:45–47](https://ref.ly/Acts13:45-Acts13:47), [50–51](https://ref.ly/Acts13:50-Acts13:51); [14:1–7](https://ref.ly/Acts14:1-Acts14:7)). However, individuals who respond in faith are saved (e.g., Lot; see [Gen 19:1–29](https://ref.ly/Gen19:1-Gen19:29); [2 Pet 2:6–9](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:6-2Pet2:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:15
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:16 (id: 21660)

False leaders who prey upon people’s spiritual vulnerability rather than exercise appropriate pastoral care are often called wolves ([Ezek 22:27](https://ref.ly/Ezek22:27); [Zeph 3:3](https://ref.ly/Zeph3:3); cp. [Prov 28:15](https://ref.ly/Prov28:15)). • be as shrewd as snakes and harmless as doves: The proverb calls for being astute but not deceitful.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:16
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:19–20 (id: 21661)

As God gave Moses a spokesman in Aaron ([Exod 4:10–17](https://ref.ly/Exod4:10-Exod4:17)), so God would give Jesus’ disciples the right words at the right time through the Spirit ([John 14:26](https://ref.ly/John14:26); [Acts 4:8](https://ref.ly/Acts4:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:19–MAT 10:20
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:21–22 (id: 21664)

Jews regularly associated family strife with the last times (see [24:9–10](https://ref.ly/Matt24:9-Matt24:10)). Jesus experienced such conflicts as well ([12:46–50](https://ref.ly/Matt12:46-Matt12:50)). • Everyone who endures to the end refers to those who remain faithful to Jesus, to the point of death or until his return ([10:23](https://ref.ly/Matt10:23)). • will be saved: Though some have taken this phrase to mean temporal deliverance from persecution (such as release from prison), the idea here is eternal salvation for those who remain faithful.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:21–MAT 10:22
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:23 (id: 21665)

will return: Scholars are divided as to whether this refers to the second coming of Christ for his church or an earlier coming in judgment—namely, the destruction of Jerusalem in AD 70 (see [16:28](https://ref.ly/Matt16:28)). • before you have reached: Jesus meant either “before you have *fled* through all the towns” or “before you have *evangelized* all the towns.” The focus on persecution in the context (see [10:17–39](https://ref.ly/Matt10:17-Matt10:39)) favors the former, suggesting that the towns were like cities of refuge ([Num 35:9–32](https://ref.ly/Num35:9-Num35:32)). The emphasis is on how widespread the rejection of the message will be—i.e., “not until the whole nation has run you out of town.”

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:23
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:25 (id: 21666)

In Jesus’ day, Satan was often called prince of demons. The Greek term is *Beelzeboul,* from the name of an Old Testament pagan deity, Baal\-zebul (“lord, the prince”). The Latin version reads Beelzebub, which is a transliteration of a Hebrew phrase meaning “lord of flies,” which was most likely a Jewish insult of Baal\-zebul (see [2 Kgs 1:2](https://ref.ly/2Kgs1:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:25
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:28 (id: 21667)

Jesus’ disciples are to fear only God by obeying him and testifying of him; in contrast to human authorities, God’s authority and judgment are unlimited. • hell: See study note on 5:29.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:28
* **Associated Articles:** Matthew 5:29 (ID: 22185)

## Matthew 10:29–31 (id: 21668)

Because God cares about every sparrow, and because Jesus’ disciples are much more valuable, certainly the disciples need not fear—God will providentially care for them.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:29–MAT 10:31
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:32–33 (id: 21670)

God accepts the one who acknowledges Jesus publicly in the context of trial and persecution ([10:16–25](https://ref.ly/Matt10:16-Matt10:25)). These verses pertain to a person’s pattern of life (see [7:13–27](https://ref.ly/Matt7:13-Matt7:27)) and not to a single confession or a single denial. For example, Judas acknowledged Jesus in individual instances yet was damned ([26:23–24](https://ref.ly/Matt26:23-Matt26:24)), whereas Peter denied Jesus (see [26:69–75](https://ref.ly/Matt26:69-Matt26:75)) yet was saved.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:32–MAT 10:33
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:34 (id: 21672)

Jesus did bring peace ([John 14:27](https://ref.ly/John14:27)), but not of a social and political kind. Instead, Jesus calls humans to make a decision about him, which brings a sword—i.e., division (see [Matt 8:21–22](https://ref.ly/Matt8:21-Matt8:22); [12:46–50](https://ref.ly/Matt12:46-Matt12:50); [Luke 12:51](https://ref.ly/Luke12:51)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:34
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:34–39 (id: 21671)

Allegiance to Jesus has priority over allegiance to family.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:34–MAT 10:39
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:37–39 (id: 21673)

The cross was a Roman instrument of torture and execution ([27:27–55](https://ref.ly/Matt27:27-Matt27:55)). To take up your cross and follow Jesus involves loving him above all other things and being willing to follow him regardless of the physical or social consequences.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:37–MAT 10:39
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:41 (id: 21675)

The same reward as a prophet (literally *A prophet’s reward*) means either the same reward a prophet would receive or the benefit of the prophet’s ministry. • Righteous people are those who conform their behavior to God’s law as taught by both John the Baptist ([21:32](https://ref.ly/Matt21:32)) and Jesus (see [3:15](https://ref.ly/Matt3:15)), and therefore are approved by God ([13:43](https://ref.ly/Matt13:43), [49](https://ref.ly/Matt13:49); [25:37–46](https://ref.ly/Matt25:37-Matt25:46)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:41
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 10:42 (id: 21676)

The least of my followers probably refers to the low social standing of most of Jesus’ followers (cp. [5:3](https://ref.ly/Matt5:3); [18:1–5](https://ref.ly/Matt18:1-Matt18:5) and [6:5](https://ref.ly/Matt6:5); [23:5–12](https://ref.ly/Matt23:5-Matt23:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 10:42
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:2 (id: 21698)

John was arrested ([4:12](https://ref.ly/Matt4:12)) by Herod Antipas because he had denounced Herod’s immoral relationship with Herodias, his half\-brother’s wife ([14:1–12](https://ref.ly/Matt14:1-Matt14:12)). • the things the Messiah was doing: These actions demonstrated that he is the Messiah ([8:1–9:34](https://ref.ly/Matt8:1-Matt9:34)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:2
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:2–19 (id: 21688)

This section begins with John the Baptist’s doubt, but it ends by exalting his faith and ministry ([11:7–19](https://ref.ly/Matt11:7-Matt11:19)). The people’s rejection of John ([11:16–19](https://ref.ly/Matt11:16-Matt11:19)) foreshadows their later rejection of Jesus.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:2–MAT 11:19
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:2–20.34 (id: 21689)

This section highlights the two primary responses to Jesus: acceptance and rejection. The first section ([11:2–12:50](https://ref.ly/Matt11:2-Matt12:50)) features the rejection of Jesus by Jewish leaders while his disciples were learning to understand and accept him.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:2
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:5 (id: 21699)

Jesus’ miracles of compassion inaugurated the Kingdom of God ([12:28](https://ref.ly/Matt12:28); see [Isa 29:18–19](https://ref.ly/Isa29:18-Isa29:19); [35:5–6](https://ref.ly/Isa35:5-Isa35:6); [61:1](https://ref.ly/Isa61:1)). Jesus expected John to understand that he was fulfilling Old Testament expectations.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:5
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:6 (id: 21700)

who do not fall away because of me: The works listed in [11:5](https://ref.ly/Matt11:5) were intended to drive John and his disciples to a decision regarding Jesus. Jesus was aware, however, that certain unexpected elements of his ministry would cause some to reject him.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:6
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:7 (id: 21701)

a weak reed, swayed by every breath of wind: An unstable person. The implied answer to Jesus’ rhetorical question is no.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:7
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:11 (id: 21683)

John the Baptist was the greatest person ever to have lived. Yet the least of Jesus’ followers are greater than John because they live in the new covenant of salvation through Jesus (see [4:17](https://ref.ly/Matt4:17)). The new covenant refers to God's new agreement with people that came through Jesus. Salvation (being saved from sin and its consequences) comes through Jesus' death and resurrection.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:11
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:12 (id: 21684)

the Kingdom of Heaven has been forcefully advancing: Or *the Kingdom of Heaven has suffered from violence.* These alternatives reflect either a positive or negative nuance of the Greek verb. In [Luke 16:16](https://ref.ly/Luke16:16), a different verb (“preached”) makes it a clearly positive statement. • violent people are attacking it: This phrase may also have a positive or negative sense. If negative, it might refer to those who imprisoned John (see [Matt 11:2](https://ref.ly/Matt11:2); [14:1–12](https://ref.ly/Matt14:1-Matt14:12)), and *attacking* might mean either that they were trying to attack the Kingdom but were unable to thwart God’s sovereign plans, or that they were attacking it by persecuting its members. In [Luke 16:16](https://ref.ly/Luke16:16) this statement has the positive sense that they were “eager to get in” and were forcefully laying claim to the Kingdom through radical trust and obedience.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:12
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:14–15 (id: 21685)

Elijah, the one the prophets said would come: John is the fulfillment of Old Testament expectations of Elijah’s return ([17:10–13](https://ref.ly/Matt17:10-Matt17:13); see [Mal 4:5](https://ref.ly/Mal4:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:14–MAT 11:15
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:16–19 (id: 21686)

John’s prophetic message is represented by funeral songs—he didn’t drink wine and he often fasted ([11:18](https://ref.ly/Matt11:18); see [3:4](https://ref.ly/Matt3:4)). Jesus’ message is seen in wedding songs and in feasts and drinks (see [9:9–17](https://ref.ly/Matt9:9-Matt9:17)). In both cases, this generation responds to God’s messenger with indifference and rejection.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:16–MAT 11:19
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:18–19 (id: 21687)

Here Jesus describes the specific ways in which John and Jesus offended the present generation. John, who stayed in the wilderness and ate locusts and honey ([3:1](https://ref.ly/Matt3:1), [4](https://ref.ly/Matt3:4)), was accused of being possessed by a demon*;* while Jesus, who ate and drank freely, was accused of being a rebellious son (see [Deut 21:18–21](https://ref.ly/Deut21:18-Deut21:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:18–MAT 11:19
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:20–24 (id: 21690)

The miracles Jesus performed confirmed him as Messiah ([11:5–6](https://ref.ly/Matt11:5-Matt11:6)) and demanded repentance ([11:20](https://ref.ly/Matt11:20)). Rejecting the Messiah would result in terrible judgment because the evidence of Jesus’ identity was clear.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:20–MAT 11:24
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:21–24 (id: 21691)

As Jesus moved through the villages of Galilee—from Korazin to Bethsaida to Capernaum—he gave the people a greater revelation of himself, with a correspondingly more severe judgment when they refused to listen. The severity is indicated by comparison with the pagan cities of Tyre ([Isa 23](https://ref.ly/Isa23:1-Isa23:18); [Ezek 26:1–28:19](https://ref.ly/Ezek26:1-Ezek28:19)), Sidon ([Ezek 28:20–23](https://ref.ly/Ezek28:20-Ezek28:23)), and Sodom ([Gen 18:22–19:29](https://ref.ly/Gen18:22-Gen19:29)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:21–MAT 11:24
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:23 (id: 21692)

the place of the dead: Greek *Hades,* which corresponds to the Hebrew term Sheol (see study note on Ps 6:5).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:23
* **Associated Articles:** Psalms 6:5 (ID: 24688)

## Matthew 11:25 (id: 21694)

those who think themselves wise and clever: The Pharisees and teachers of religious law thought their access to God was guaranteed through their knowledge and practice of the law. Jesus’ disciples were more childlike (see [21:15–16](https://ref.ly/Matt21:15-Matt21:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:25
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:25–30 (id: 21693)

This passage focuses on the remnant who, despite the present generation’s overall rejection of the Messiah, willingly embrace him and follow his teachings.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:25–MAT 11:30
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:27 (id: 21695)

Jesus was revealing his intimate relationship to the Father. Everything he said and did was rooted in this Father–Son unity (see [John 10:14–15](https://ref.ly/John10:14-John10:15); [14:6–7](https://ref.ly/John14:6-John14:7); [15:23–24](https://ref.ly/John15:23-John15:24); [16:15](https://ref.ly/John16:15); [17:25–26](https://ref.ly/John17:25-John17:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:27
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:28 (id: 21696)

The heavy burdens were likely caused by the legal requirements of the teachers of religious law and Pharisees (see [23:4](https://ref.ly/Matt23:4)). • rest: Spiritual refreshment in either a present or a future sense (cp. [1:21](https://ref.ly/Matt1:21); [Heb 4:8–11](https://ref.ly/Heb4:8-Heb4:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:28
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 11:29–30 (id: 21697)

A yoke, which forms a harness between two animals, is a metaphor for the demands of discipleship. In contrast to the “yoke” of the religious leaders, Jesus’ yoke is easy and light, not because it is less demanding (see [7:13–14](https://ref.ly/Matt7:13-Matt7:14)), but because the power of the Messiah (by the Holy Spirit) makes it possible (see [Acts 15:10](https://ref.ly/Acts15:10); [1 Jn 5:3](https://ref.ly/1John5:3)). The religious demands of Israel’s spiritual leaders ([Matt 23:4](https://ref.ly/Matt23:4); [Acts 15:10](https://ref.ly/Acts15:10)) included 613 Old Testament commands and their expansion through tradition. Jesus urged those who were suffering from the burdens of the Pharisees’ stipulations to come to him ([Matt 11:28](https://ref.ly/Matt11:28)) in order to find the salvation their hearts desired. It is a call to salvation involving a life of obedience to Jesus’ new teachings. People are invited to enter a relationship with a humble and gentle teacher.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 11:29–MAT 11:30
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:1 (id: 21708)

The Sabbath*,* the seventh day of the week, was to be a day of complete rest according to Old Testament laws ([Gen 2:2–3](https://ref.ly/Gen2:2-Gen2:3); [Exod 20:8–11](https://ref.ly/Exod20:8-Exod20:11)). The Sabbath is fulfilled in Christ (cp. [Heb 4:1–11](https://ref.ly/Heb4:1-Heb4:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:1
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:1–8 (id: 21703)

This exchange highlights the Pharisees’ lack of compassion as they imposed a burdensome yoke ([11:29–30](https://ref.ly/Matt11:29-Matt11:30)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:1–MAT 12:8
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:1–14 (id: 21702)

Matthew places Jesus’ offer of rest ([11:28–30](https://ref.ly/Matt11:28-Matt11:30)) in close connection with a discussion of the Sabbath. Jesus’ rest liberates people from human traditions concerning the Sabbath (cp. [Heb 4:1–11](https://ref.ly/Heb4:1-Heb4:11)). The Pharisees rejected Jesus because of their commitment to tradition.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:1–MAT 12:14
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:3–4 (id: 21717)

Ritual laws were at times rightly suspended for particular people or circumstances ([1 Sam 21:1–6](https://ref.ly/1Sam21:1-1Sam21:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:3–MAT 12:4
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:3–7 (id: 21718)

The Pharisees did not understand that the Sabbath was designed to benefit people. Their view of the Sabbath placed onerous burdens on people.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:3–MAT 12:7
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:5–6 (id: 21730)

Priests worked on the Sabbath ([Lev 24:8–9](https://ref.ly/Lev24:8-Lev24:9); [Num 28:9–10](https://ref.ly/Num28:9-Num28:10)), and this was not offensive to Pharisees. If the priests’ work for the Temple on the Sabbath is allowed, then certainly Jesus can do the same because he is greater than the Temple (see [Matt 4:23](https://ref.ly/Matt4:23); [9:35](https://ref.ly/Matt9:35); [11:2–6](https://ref.ly/Matt11:2-Matt11:6), [20–30](https://ref.ly/Matt11:20-Matt11:30)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:5–MAT 12:6
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:7 (id: 21731)

The Pharisees’ view of the Sabbath was unscriptural since it broke the deeper principle of mercy.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:7
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:8 (id: 21732)

Jesus is superior to David, the priests, and the Temple. He reigns even over the Sabbath.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:8
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:9 (id: 21734)

their synagogue: A disunion was developing between Jesus and Judaism (also [4:23](https://ref.ly/Matt4:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:9
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:9–14 (id: 21733)

This second Sabbath controversy castigates the Pharisees for elevating regulations over human needs (see [12:7](https://ref.ly/Matt12:7), [11–12](https://ref.ly/Matt12:11-Matt12:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:9–MAT 12:14
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:10 (id: 21704)

Does the law permit: Rabbinic tradition permitted healing on the Sabbath only if life was in danger. Since life was not in jeopardy, the Pharisees thought healing was not permitted.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:10
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:11–12 (id: 21705)

Their practice of rescuing animals but neglecting fellow humans was inconsistent.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:11–MAT 12:12
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:15–21 (id: 21706)

This summary of Jesus’ ministry clarifies Jesus’ nature as the Messiah, the Servant of God who will bring salvation to the nations (see [Isa 42:1–4](https://ref.ly/Isa42:1-Isa42:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:15–MAT 12:21
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:18 (id: 21707)

This quotation parallels Jesus’ baptism ([3:13–17](https://ref.ly/Matt3:13-Matt3:17)). • Justice (or *judgment*) can have positive or negative implications; the context here favors a positive meaning ([12:20](https://ref.ly/Matt12:20); cp. [23:23](https://ref.ly/Matt23:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:18
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:20 (id: 21709)

Instead of increasing people’s spiritual burden, Jesus offers compassionate forgiveness and sustenance (see [11:28–30](https://ref.ly/Matt11:28-Matt11:30); [12:1–14](https://ref.ly/Matt12:1-Matt12:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:20
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:22–45 (id: 21710)

The Messiah was rejected by the Pharisees, the teachers of religious law, and his own generation.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:22–MAT 12:45
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:23 (id: 21711)

Amazement was a common response to Jesus’ miracles ([Mark 2:12](https://ref.ly/Mark2:12); [6:51](https://ref.ly/Mark6:51); [Luke 2:47](https://ref.ly/Luke2:47); [8:56](https://ref.ly/Luke8:56); [24:22](https://ref.ly/Luke24:22)). • Could it be: The question expected a negative answer: Jesus did not fit their expectations for the Messiah, but his miracles did prompt the question.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:23
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:24 (id: 21712)

Satan: Greek *Beelzeboul;* see study note on 10:25.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:24
* **Associated Articles:** Matthew 10:25 (ID: 21666)

## Matthew 12:26 (id: 21713)

Jesus argued, in essence, “If I cast out demons under the influence of Satan, then Satan is dividing his camp, which obviously would be a foolish thing for Satan to do.”

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:26
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:27 (id: 21714)

what about your own exorcists (literally *your sons*): Jesus forced them to think consistently. If demons are cast out under Satan’s influence, then their disciples were equally guilty (see [Acts 19:13–16](https://ref.ly/Acts19:13-Acts19:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:27
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:28 (id: 21715)

The Pharisees were being confronted with and were rejecting the Kingdom of God itself (see [Luke 17:20–21](https://ref.ly/Luke17:20-Luke17:21); [1 Jn 3:8](https://ref.ly/1John3:8)). Jesus’ miracles brought the power of the Kingdom into the present reality; its ultimate consummation awaits Christ’s second coming.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:28
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:29 (id: 21716)

This parable forced the Pharisees to answer a simple question: Can anyone cast out demons without first binding Satan’s powers and thus opposing him (see [Isa 49:24–26](https://ref.ly/Isa49:24-Isa49:26); [53:12](https://ref.ly/Isa53:12))? • tie him up: Jesus overcame Satan first at his temptation ([Matt 4:1–11](https://ref.ly/Matt4:1-Matt4:11)), then throughout his ministry (see [Luke 10:17–20](https://ref.ly/Luke10:17-Luke10:20)), and ultimately on the cross (see [Col 2:14–15](https://ref.ly/Col2:14-Col2:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:29
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:31 (id: 21719)

In the face of the Pharisees’ accusations of Satanic influence, Jesus had just argued that he, the Messiah, cast out demons through the power of the Holy Spirit. In this context, blasphemy against the Holy Spirit can only mean attributing the ministry and exorcisms of Jesus to Satan’s power.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:31
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:32 (id: 21720)

God can forgive people who are confused about Jesus calling himself the "Son of Man." But, God will not forgive a person that says the Holy Spirit's work comes from Satan. Today, this is like completely rejecting the conviction of the Holy Spirit about Jesus. This refers to when an unbeliever ultimately rejects the good news about Jesus (see [Hebrews 6:4–6](https://ref.ly/Heb6:4-Heb6:6); [1 John 5:16–21](https://ref.ly/1John5:16-1John5:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:32
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:33–37 (id: 21721)

Jesus addressed the main issue. The Pharisees did not accept him or believe his work came from God because they were wicked (see [7:15–27](https://ref.ly/Matt7:15-Matt7:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:33–MAT 12:37
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:36–37 (id: 21722)

* The *careless word*, in this context, was the claim that demons empowered Jesus.
* What a person says will either free or condemn them on the day of judgment. What people say shows the true state of their hearts.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:36–MAT 12:37
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:38 (id: 21723)

a miraculous sign to prove: A popular expectation of the Messiah, probably fueled by biblical accounts about Moses ([Exod 4:1–9](https://ref.ly/Exod4:1-Exod4:9); see also [Isa 7:11](https://ref.ly/Isa7:11), [14](https://ref.ly/Isa7:14); [38:7–8](https://ref.ly/Isa38:7-Isa38:8)), was that the Messiah would display spectacular miracles on command (see [Matt 16:1–4](https://ref.ly/Matt16:1-Matt16:4); [Luke 23:8](https://ref.ly/Luke23:8); [John 2:18](https://ref.ly/John2:18); [4:48](https://ref.ly/John4:48); [6:30](https://ref.ly/John6:30); [7:31](https://ref.ly/John7:31); [9:16](https://ref.ly/John9:16); [11:47](https://ref.ly/John11:47); [1 Cor 1:22](https://ref.ly/1Cor1:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:38
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:39–40 (id: 21724)

To demand a sign demonstrates a lack of faith. • The sign of the prophet Jonah consisted of Jonah’s “resurrection” from the large fish after three days and three nights as well as his preaching ([12:41](https://ref.ly/Matt12:41); [Luke 11:32](https://ref.ly/Luke11:32)); it was analogous to Jesus’ burial and resurrection and his preaching. Jesus was drawing a parallel between Jonah’s experience and what he himself would experience. He was not predicting an exact chronology of his death and resurrection. • Heart of the earth is a euphemism for the grave.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:39–MAT 12:40
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:41–42 (id: 21725)

someone greater: Jesus is greater than the Temple ([12:6](https://ref.ly/Matt12:6)), a prophet (Jonah), and a king (Solomon); therefore, rejection of him entails greater judgment on this “evil, adulterous generation” ([12:39](https://ref.ly/Matt12:39)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:41–MAT 12:42
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:42 (id: 21726)

The queen of Sheba: See [1 Kgs 10:1–13](https://ref.ly/1Kgs10:1-1Kgs10:13).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:42
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:43 (id: 21728)

Demons were thought to prefer the arid desert (see [Rev 18:2](https://ref.ly/Rev18:2); cp. [Isa 13:21](https://ref.ly/Isa13:21); [34:14](https://ref.ly/Isa34:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:43
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:43–45 (id: 21727)

The Messiah came in victory over demonic powers, but instead of repenting, the nation as a whole rejected the Messiah. Just as an exorcised demon will return if the house is not properly prepared against it, so judgment would come to this evil generation for rejecting the Messiah.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:43–MAT 12:45
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 12:48–50 (id: 21729)

Those who are true members in Jesus’ family do the will of the Father*,* as expressed in the commands of Jesus (see [7:21](https://ref.ly/Matt7:21)). Obedience does not earn entrance into this family, but one cannot be considered a member if he or she is not obedient (see [3:15](https://ref.ly/Matt3:15); [5:17–48](https://ref.ly/Matt5:17-Matt5:48); [6:10](https://ref.ly/Matt6:10), [12](https://ref.ly/Matt6:12); [7:13–27](https://ref.ly/Matt7:13-Matt7:27); [21:31](https://ref.ly/Matt21:31)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 12:48–MAT 12:50
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:1–53 (id: 21735)

In the third major discourse recorded by Matthew (see study note on Matt 5:1–7:29), Jesus here recognized the separation of his followers from others ([13:14](https://ref.ly/Matt13:14),[16](https://ref.ly/Matt13:16)) and began to reveal the secrets of the Kingdom privately to them through parables.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:1–MAT 13:53
* **Associated Articles:** Matthew 5:1-7.29 (ID: 22169)

## Matthew 13:3–9 (id: 21749)

This parable (interpreted in [13:18–23](https://ref.ly/Matt13:18-Matt13:23)) addresses the mostly negative responses of the Jewish nation to Jesus and his message. • Parables (Greek parabolē) are stories that usually express an analogy between a common aspect of life and a spiritual truth. To understand a parable, it is necessary to locate the central analogy and understand it in its historical context and in the context of the Gospel text; then the central message can be understood. Speculative allegorical meanings that were not intended should not be found in every element of a parable.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:3–MAT 13:9
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:10 (id: 21736)

From this point on, Jesus rarely taught the general public. Instead, he focused on teaching those who had committed themselves to him ([13:1–20:34](https://ref.ly/Matt13:1-Matt20:34)), though he would once again confront Israel ([21:1–23:39](https://ref.ly/Matt21:1-Matt23:39)). • The people were the unbelieving opponents mentioned again in [13:11](https://ref.ly/Matt13:11) (“others”) and [13:12](https://ref.ly/Matt13:12) (“those who are not listening”).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:10
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:11 (id: 21738)

You are permitted to understand: God had enabled the disciples to comprehend Jesus’ significance and to respond to his message of the Kingdom in faith and obedience (see [13:19](https://ref.ly/Matt13:19), [23](https://ref.ly/Matt13:23)). • the secrets of the Kingdom of Heaven: Namely, that salvation is available to them in Jesus as the fulfillment of Old Testament promises.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:11
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:11–15 (id: 21737)

Jesus’ answer to the disciples’ question ([13:10](https://ref.ly/Matt13:10)) was essentially that the people’s stubborn unbelief and rejection of Jesus had brought God’s condemnation.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:11–MAT 13:15
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:13 (id: 21739)

Jesus told parables*,* and those who believed understood while those who had rejected Jesus found that his parables intensified their unbelief. • they don’t really see … listen or understand: They lacked the faith that perceives the truth ([13:19](https://ref.ly/Matt13:19), [23](https://ref.ly/Matt13:23)) and acts upon it ([Mark 8:18](https://ref.ly/Mark8:18); [John 12:40](https://ref.ly/John12:40); see also [Jer 5:21](https://ref.ly/Jer5:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:13
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:14–15 (id: 21740)

Like that of Isaiah, Jesus’ message has a dual effect: It judges people for unbelief and disobedience, and it creates a remnant of faithful ones who accomplish the Lord’s will ([21:43](https://ref.ly/Matt21:43)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:14–MAT 13:15
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:16–17 (id: 21741)

Jesus brought into reality what the prophets and Old Testament saints desired to see and hear*,* that is, the fulfillment of Old Testament promises (see [Isa 52:15](https://ref.ly/Isa52:15); [John 8:56](https://ref.ly/John8:56); [1 Pet 1:10](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:16–MAT 13:17
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:19 (id: 21742)

don’t understand it: Responding to the message of the Kingdom is directly related to discerning its significance.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:19
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:20–21 (id: 21743)

don’t have deep roots … don’t last long: The problem is a lack of persevering faith and obedience (see [7:13–27](https://ref.ly/Matt7:13-Matt7:27); [10:22](https://ref.ly/Matt10:22)), particularly when persecution arises.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:20–MAT 13:21
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:22 (id: 21744)

Jesus spoke of competing demands in life, (see also [8:18–22](https://ref.ly/Matt8:18-Matt8:22)). The worries of this life can become so great that they divert one from the path of faithful obedience (see [6:19–34](https://ref.ly/Matt6:19-Matt6:34)). The lure of wealth*,* particularly in its ability to deceive, appears often in Matthew (e.g., [4:8–10](https://ref.ly/Matt4:8-Matt4:10); [6:24](https://ref.ly/Matt6:24); [13:44–45](https://ref.ly/Matt13:44-Matt13:45)). God does not desire that his people have wealth as much as that they have faith, obey him, and willingly help those in need (e.g., [19:21](https://ref.ly/Matt19:21); [25:31–46](https://ref.ly/Matt25:31-Matt25:46)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:22
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:23 (id: 21745)

produce a harvest: Probably a general reference to faithful obedience to Jesus’ commands (e.g., [5:1–7:27](https://ref.ly/Matt5:1-Matt7:27); [28:20](https://ref.ly/Matt28:20)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:23
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:24–30 (id: 21746)

This story is explained in [13:36–43](https://ref.ly/Matt13:36-Matt13:43).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:24–MAT 13:30
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:25 (id: 21747)

Weeds (or *tares*, bearded darnel) are almost indistinguishable from wheat and so were left until growth revealed their true nature. Malevolent contamination of crops in this manner was punishable by law.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:25
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:28–30 (id: 21748)

Just as Jesus rebuked the sons of Zebedee for wanting to destroy unbelieving villages ([Luke 9:54–55](https://ref.ly/Luke9:54-Luke9:55)), he prohibited his followers from retaliating against enemies. Judgment is God’s work (see [Matt 7:1–5](https://ref.ly/Matt7:1-Matt7:5)). Jesus urges his followers to wait patiently for God’s righteous judgment (the harvest; see [Luke 13:6–9](https://ref.ly/Luke13:6-Luke13:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:28–MAT 13:30
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:31–33 (id: 21750)

Jesus used surprising, evocative imagery in these parables, either to emphasize the inevitable growth of the Kingdom through proclamation of the gospel or, more probably, to emphasize the contrast between insignificant beginnings and glorious consummation, and to exhort the disciples to patience (see also [16:24–17:13](https://ref.ly/Matt16:24-Matt17:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:31–MAT 13:33
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:33 (id: 21751)

Normally yeast refers to the influence of evil (e.g., [16:6](https://ref.ly/Matt16:6); [1 Cor 5:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:6); [Gal 5:9](https://ref.ly/Gal5:9)); here, however, it is positive, speaking of the all\-pervasive influence of the Kingdom.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:33
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:34–35 (id: 21752)

Even Jesus’ manner of teaching fulfilled Old Testament predictions. [Psalm 78:2–3](https://ref.ly/Ps78:2-Ps78:3) speaks of passing down the history of God’s revelation to children of the next generation. Jesus’ revelation is the climax of that history ([Matt 13:10–17](https://ref.ly/Matt13:10-Matt13:17); [1 Cor 2:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor2:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:34–MAT 13:35
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:36 (id: 21754)

They went into the house (see [13:1](https://ref.ly/Matt13:1)). Jesus taught in parables publicly, but the interpretations were reserved for his disciples in private. • Please explain: Though the disciples were privileged to know the mysteries of the Kingdom ([13:11–17](https://ref.ly/Matt13:11-Matt13:17)), they did not understand the parables until Jesus explained them.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:36
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:36–43 (id: 21753)

These verses are the interpretation of the parable told in [13:24–30](https://ref.ly/Matt13:24-Matt13:30). The people of the Kingdom (wheat) coexist with nonmembers (weeds) in the world (field) until the end of history. The mystery of the Kingdom is that it is present in the world without weeding out the wicked in judgment; Jesus’ disciples must learn patience.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:36–MAT 13:43
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:38 (id: 21755)

The field is the world: The Kingdom includes all nations ([28:16–20](https://ref.ly/Matt28:16-Matt28:20)). • The people of the Kingdom are those who follow Jesus ([13:11–17](https://ref.ly/Matt13:11-Matt13:17), [23](https://ref.ly/Matt13:23); [21:43](https://ref.ly/Matt21:43)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:38
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:40–42 (id: 21756)

The harvest of judgment, which began with the first coming of the Son of Man ([3:12](https://ref.ly/Matt3:12)), will be completed when he returns ([Rev 14:14–16](https://ref.ly/Rev14:14-Rev14:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:40–MAT 13:42
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:41 (id: 21757)

his Kingdom: Not until the “end of the world” ([13:40](https://ref.ly/Matt13:40)) will the rule of the Son of Man be visible over all things.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:41
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:43 (id: 21758)

The righteous do the will of God as revealed by Jesus, in contrast to those “who do evil” ([13:41](https://ref.ly/Matt13:41)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:43
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:44 (id: 21760)

treasure … hidden in a field: Treasures were buried for protection against thieves and military enemies ([25:25](https://ref.ly/Matt25:25)). • In his excitement: Those who discover the Kingdom find greater joy in it than can be found in any temporal pleasure (see [1 Pet 1:8](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:44
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:44–46 (id: 21759)

Another mystery of the kingdom of heaven ([13:11](https://ref.ly/Matt13:11)) is that it is more valuable than any treasure. So, a person should give up everything to get it (see [19:21](https://ref.ly/Matt19:21), [29](https://ref.ly/Matt19:29); [Philippians 3:7](https://ref.ly/Phil3:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:44–MAT 13:46
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:47–50 (id: 21761)

This parable refers to God’s judgment at the last day ([25:31–46](https://ref.ly/Matt25:31-Matt25:46)), which will eternally separate the wicked from the righteous. This note of warning reinforces the urgency of the previous two calls to decision.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:47–MAT 13:50
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:49 (id: 21762)

The wicked are those who do not do the will of God as revealed in Jesus, and the righteous are those who do (see [5:21–48](https://ref.ly/Matt5:21-Matt5:48); [6:1](https://ref.ly/Matt6:1), [33](https://ref.ly/Matt6:33); [7:13–27](https://ref.ly/Matt7:13-Matt7:27); [12:33–37](https://ref.ly/Matt12:33-Matt12:37); [16:27](https://ref.ly/Matt16:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:49
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:51 (id: 21763)

The ability to understand the mysteries of the Kingdom is a gift from God ([13:10–17](https://ref.ly/Matt13:10-Matt13:17), [23](https://ref.ly/Matt13:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:51
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:52 (id: 21764)

A teacher of religious law who becomes a disciple in the Kingdom has had his allegiance radically altered toward Jesus as the way of salvation. • new gems of truth as well as old: The sequence reflects the preeminence of the new covenant inaugurated in Jesus ([5:17–20](https://ref.ly/Matt5:17-Matt5:20); [19:16–22](https://ref.ly/Matt19:16-Matt19:22)) over the old covenant administered under Abraham and Moses.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:52
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:54–58 (id: 21765)

That Jesus was rejected at home is part of the ongoing theme of the Messiah’s rejection by his own people (see ch [12](https://ref.ly/Matt12:1-Matt12:50); [15:1–20](https://ref.ly/Matt15:1-Matt15:20); [16:1–12](https://ref.ly/Matt16:1-Matt16:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:54–MAT 13:58
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:55–56 (id: 21766)

carpenter’s son: A carpenter (literally *craftsman*) worked with his hands, whether in wood, metal, or stone.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:55–MAT 13:56
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:57 (id: 21767)

They were deeply offended. Dwelling on Jesus’ all\-too\-common heritage ([John 6:42](https://ref.ly/John6:42)), they could not see his uncommon significance.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:57
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 13:58 (id: 21768)

Faith is required both to understand Jesus’ message ([13:10–17](https://ref.ly/Matt13:10-Matt13:17)) and to experience his miracles.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 13:58
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 14:1 (id: 21770)

Herod Antipas’s official title was *tetrarch* (ruler of a fourth part of a kingdom) of Galilee and Perea (4 BC—AD 39; see [2:19–22](https://ref.ly/Matt2:19-Matt2:22)). Jesus referred to Antipas as “that fox” ([Luke 13:32](https://ref.ly/Luke13:32)), and John the Baptist justly condemned him for adultery ([Matt 14:3–12](https://ref.ly/Matt14:3-Matt14:12); [Luke 3:19–20](https://ref.ly/Luke3:19-Luke3:20)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 14:1
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 14:2 (id: 21777)

There was a rumor that John had been resurrected (see [16:14](https://ref.ly/Matt16:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 14:2
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 14:3–12 (id: 21778)

The popular appeal of John’s message posed a political threat (see Josephus, *Antiquities* 18\.5\.2\). Years after John’s execution, the Jews viewed Herod’s military defeat at the hands of Aretas (AD 36\) as a just recompense for putting an innocent man to death.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 14:3–MAT 14:12
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 14:4 (id: 21780)

John had continually warned Herod of his sin (see [Lev 18:6](https://ref.ly/Lev18:6); [20:21](https://ref.ly/Lev20:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 14:4
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 14:6 (id: 21781)

Herodias’s daughter was probably Salome, a daughter from Herodias’s previous marriage to Philip. Sexually provocative dances such as this were a regular occurrence for depraved royalty.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 14:6
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 14:7 (id: 21782)

Such an extravagant, foolish oath was consistent with Herod Antipas’s character.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 14:7
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 14:8 (id: 21783)

In ancient times, presenting a head on a tray was a known practice (see Josephus, *Antiquities* 13\.4\.8; 14\.15\.13; 18\.5\.1; 20\.5\.1\).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 14:8
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 14:13–21 (id: 21769)

Jesus’ actions consistently fulfilled Old Testament promises regarding the Kingdom and the Messiah ([11:5–6](https://ref.ly/Matt11:5-Matt11:6); [12:28](https://ref.ly/Matt12:28)). Here Jesus evoked the memory of God’s provision of manna for the Israelites ([Exod 16](https://ref.ly/Exod16:1-Exod16:36); see [John 6:32](https://ref.ly/John6:32)), demonstrating that he is the promised end\-time prophet (see [Deut 18:15–16](https://ref.ly/Deut18:15-Deut18:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 14:13–MAT 14:21
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 14:21 (id: 21771)

5,000 men … in addition to all the women and children: The count was of families, denoted by heads of households, rather than individuals.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 14:21
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 14:22 (id: 21773)

After the miraculous feeding, the crowds sought to make Jesus king ([John 6:15](https://ref.ly/John6:15)), prompting his withdrawal because it was not the appropriate time.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 14:22
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 14:22–33 (id: 21772)

Jesus’ power over nature presented the disciples with the opportunity to trust in him as the Son of God ([14:33](https://ref.ly/Matt14:33); see also [8:23–27](https://ref.ly/Matt8:23-Matt8:27); [Ps 8:6](https://ref.ly/Ps8:6); [Heb 2:8–9](https://ref.ly/Heb2:8-Heb2:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 14:22–MAT 14:33
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 14:23 (id: 21774)

Jesus often sought solitude in order to pray*,* particularly in conjunction with important events in his life and ministry ([26:36–46](https://ref.ly/Matt26:36-Matt26:46); [Mark 1:35](https://ref.ly/Mark1:35); [Luke 5:16](https://ref.ly/Luke5:16); [6:12](https://ref.ly/Luke6:12); [9:28](https://ref.ly/Luke9:28)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 14:23
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 14:25 (id: 21775)

About three o’clock in the morning: Literally *In the fourth watch of the night.* This was approximately 3:00–6:00 am by Roman reckoning. • The fact that Jesus came … walking on the water demonstrates God’s sovereign reign over the stormy waters (see [Job 9:8](https://ref.ly/Job9:8); [Ps 77:19](https://ref.ly/Ps77:19); [Isa 43:16](https://ref.ly/Isa43:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 14:25
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 14:27 (id: 21776)

I am here: Literally *I am.* This declaration is associated with the appearance of God himself (see also [John 8:24](https://ref.ly/John8:24); [18:5–6](https://ref.ly/John18:5-John18:6); cp. [Exod 3:14](https://ref.ly/Exod3:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 14:27
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 14:34–36 (id: 21779)

On the purpose of Jesus’ miracles, see study notes on Matt 11:5; 12:28.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 14:34–MAT 14:36
* **Associated Articles:** Matthew 11:5 (ID: 21699); Matthew 12:28 (ID: 21715)

## Matthew 15:1 (id: 21787)

Jerusalem was the location of the Temple and thus the seat of authority in Judaism; this gave the ambassadors greater leverage in their arguments with Jesus.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 15:1
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 15:1–20 (id: 21784)

Jesus indicted the Pharisees for disobeying God’s law in their zeal to preserve traditions.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 15:1–MAT 15:20
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 15:2 (id: 21793)

The Jewish teachers’ age\-old tradition sought to apply the written Torah to common circumstances in the ordinary course of life. This tradition was memorized and passed on orally from teacher to student (cp. [1 Cor 11:23](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:23); [15:1–5](https://ref.ly/1Cor15:1-1Cor15:5)). • To ignore the tradition of … hand washing (see [Mark 7:2–4](https://ref.ly/Mark7:2-Mark7:4); [Luke 11:38](https://ref.ly/Luke11:38)) was considered disobedient to the Torah and unfaithful to God’s will for Israel (cp. [Matt 23:25–26](https://ref.ly/Matt23:25-Matt23:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 15:2
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 15:5 (id: 21796)

vowed to give to God: Such a gift was likely donated at the Temple (see [Mark 7:11](https://ref.ly/Mark7:11); see also [Prov 28:24](https://ref.ly/Prov28:24)) but functioned as a way to dodge financial responsibility for one’s parents.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 15:5
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 15:6 (id: 21797)

cancel: Because of a greater commitment to their traditions, the Pharisees in effect rendered God’s law nonbinding, turning their piety into sinful disregard for the word of God.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 15:6
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 15:7 (id: 21798)

You hypocrites! See study note on Matt 23:13.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 15:7
* **Associated Articles:** Matthew 23:13 (ID: 21965)

## Matthew 15:11 (id: 21785)

what goes into your mouth: Jesus was speaking here either of foods that were not permitted (e.g., pork or shellfish) or of food contaminated by unclean hands ([15:20](https://ref.ly/Matt15:20)). • That which defiles makes a person unfit for communion with God. Jesus pressed the matter beyond ceremonial purity to true inner purity (see [15:18–19](https://ref.ly/Matt15:18-Matt15:19); [23:25–26](https://ref.ly/Matt23:25-Matt23:26); [Acts 10:1–48](https://ref.ly/Acts10:1-Acts10:48); [Rom 14:14](https://ref.ly/Rom14:14)). • One’s words are a measure of one’s character (see [Matt 15:18–20](https://ref.ly/Matt15:18-Matt15:20); [Jas 3:1–12](https://ref.ly/Jas3:1-Jas3:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 15:11
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 15:13 (id: 21786)

not planted by my heavenly Father: These Pharisees did not belong to the true people of God (see [3:9–12](https://ref.ly/Matt3:9-Matt3:12); [Isa 5:1–7](https://ref.ly/Isa5:1-Isa5:7); [Jer 45:4](https://ref.ly/Jer45:4)). They will be uprooted at the final judgment (see [Matt 3:10](https://ref.ly/Matt3:10); [8:12](https://ref.ly/Matt8:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 15:13
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 15:21–28 (id: 21788)

This encounter highlights another controversial issue: Gentile participation in the Kingdom of the Messiah (see [8:11](https://ref.ly/Matt8:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 15:21–MAT 15:28
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 15:22 (id: 21789)

Gentile woman: Literally *Canaanite woman.* Matthew uses this archaic Old Testament expression to describe the woman as a pagan. • Lord, Son of David: The woman apparently perceived that Jesus was the Messiah (see [1:1](https://ref.ly/Matt1:1); [9:27](https://ref.ly/Matt9:27); [17:15](https://ref.ly/Matt17:15); [20:30](https://ref.ly/Matt20:30)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 15:22
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 15:23 (id: 21790)

no reply: Jesus’ silence was a test of the woman’s faith ([15:28](https://ref.ly/Matt15:28); cp. [8:24](https://ref.ly/Matt8:24); [14:16](https://ref.ly/Matt14:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 15:23
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 15:26 (id: 21791)

Jews often referred to pagans as dogs*,* which are ceremonially unclean ([Lev 11:27](https://ref.ly/Lev11:27)). Jesus was speaking to the woman of her spiritual condition as a Gentile—as unclean and separated from God (cp. [Matt 7:6](https://ref.ly/Matt7:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 15:26
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 15:29–31 (id: 21792)

Jesus returned to a predominantly Gentile area and performed many miracles. Though Jesus was sent primarily for Israel’s sake ([15:21–28](https://ref.ly/Matt15:21-Matt15:28)), the new era that he inaugurated is also the beginning of Gentile salvation ([1:3](https://ref.ly/Matt1:3), [5–6](https://ref.ly/Matt1:5-Matt1:6); [2:1–12](https://ref.ly/Matt2:1-Matt2:12); [4:12–16](https://ref.ly/Matt4:12-Matt4:16); [8:5–13](https://ref.ly/Matt8:5-Matt8:13); [15:21–28](https://ref.ly/Matt15:21-Matt15:28); [28:16–20](https://ref.ly/Matt28:16-Matt28:20)). • Such healings are signs that the Kingdom has broken into history through Jesus’ ministry ([8:1–9:34](https://ref.ly/Matt8:1-Matt9:34); [11:5–6](https://ref.ly/Matt11:5-Matt11:6); [12:28](https://ref.ly/Matt12:28)). • the God of Israel: This phrase suggests that the crowd ([15:30](https://ref.ly/Matt15:30)) was predominantly Gentile.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 15:29–MAT 15:31
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 15:32–39 (id: 21794)

The previous feeding miracle (see [14:13–21](https://ref.ly/Matt14:13-Matt14:21)) was for Jews, whereas this one extended to Gentiles; it thus develops the theme of [15:27](https://ref.ly/Matt15:27). Through this miracle Jesus demonstrated that he is the true bread of life (see [16:5–12](https://ref.ly/Matt16:5-Matt16:12); [John 6](https://ref.ly/John6:1-John6:71)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 15:32–MAT 15:39
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 15:39 (id: 21795)

Magadan is an unknown site, perhaps *Magdala* (as in some Greek manuscripts; see also [Mark 8:10](https://ref.ly/Mark8:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 15:39
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:1–12 (id: 21799)

Having been warmly received in the Gentile world, Jesus returned to his fellow countrymen only to encounter further rejection.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:1–MAT 16:12
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:2–3 (id: 21807)

Jesus made a deliberate play on their words when they sought a “sign from heaven” ([16:1](https://ref.ly/Matt16:1)). They were able to read the weather in the sky (Greek ouranos, the same word translated “heaven”), but they failed to discern the Messiah despite the many signs already given (see [11:1–6](https://ref.ly/Matt11:1-Matt11:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:2–MAT 16:3
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:3 (id: 21817)

The signs of the times were Jesus himself ([16:4](https://ref.ly/Matt16:4)) and the various miracles that he performed (cp. [11:2–6](https://ref.ly/Matt11:2-Matt11:6); [12:28](https://ref.ly/Matt12:28)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:3
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:9–10 (id: 21818)

Jesus had shown his disciples that he is the true "bread of life" ([15:32–39](https://ref.ly/Matt15:32-Matt15:39); [John 6:35](https://ref.ly/John6:35), [48](https://ref.ly/John6:48)). In contrast, the Jewish leaders taught things that were wrong. Their false teaching spread everywhere, like yeast (or leaven) spreads through bread dough (see study note on Matt 16:11–12).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:9–MAT 16:10
* **Associated Articles:** Matthew 16:11-12 (ID: 21800)

## Matthew 16:11–12 (id: 21800)

*Leaven* (or yeast) often symbolizes sin and evil (see [Exodus 12:8](https://ref.ly/Exod12:8), [15](https://ref.ly/Exod12:15); [Leviticus 6:16–17](https://ref.ly/Lev6:16-Lev6:17); [Galatians 5:9](https://ref.ly/Gal5:9)). Here, it represents how deceptive teaching spreads.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:11–MAT 16:12
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:13 (id: 21801)

*Caesarea Philippi* was about forty kilometers (twenty\-five miles) north of Capernaum. It had many shrines (holy places) dedicated to Pan, the Roman god of nature.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:13
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:14 (id: 21802)

Some*,* such as Herod Antipas ([14:1–2](https://ref.ly/Matt14:1-Matt14:2)), thought Jesus was John the Baptist resurrected. • Elijah was expected as a forerunner to the Messiah ([11:14](https://ref.ly/Matt11:14); [17:10–12](https://ref.ly/Matt17:10-Matt17:12); [Mal 3:1](https://ref.ly/Mal3:1); [4:5–6](https://ref.ly/Mal4:5-Mal4:6)). • Jeremiah or one of the other prophets: Some Jews expected Jeremiah to be raised (see *2 Maccabees* 15:13–16\). Jesus’ strong stand on sensitive matters ([Matt 5:17](https://ref.ly/Matt5:17); [15:1–20](https://ref.ly/Matt15:1-Matt15:20)) may have led some to think Jesus was Jeremiah. Jesus was not yet understood as God’s Messiah.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:14
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:16 (id: 21803)

Peter’s acknowledgment of Jesus as the Messiah, the Son of the living God ([3:17](https://ref.ly/Matt3:17)) shows that his eyes had been opened by faith (see [11:25–27](https://ref.ly/Matt11:25-Matt11:27); [14:33](https://ref.ly/Matt14:33); [27:54](https://ref.ly/Matt27:54)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:16
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:17 (id: 21804)

God revealed to Peter his plan of salvation in Jesus, the Messiah. This moment of revelation was a high point in the unfolding of God’s will for humanity (cp. [Gal 1:16](https://ref.ly/Gal1:16); [3:23](https://ref.ly/Gal3:23); [Eph 3:5](https://ref.ly/Eph3:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:17
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:18 (id: 21805)

The phrase upon this rock is a pun on Peter’s name. Peter was the foundational rock in that he was the first confessor and leader of the apostles—he was the “founding member” of the church (see [Eph 2:20–22](https://ref.ly/Eph2:20-Eph2:22); [Rev 21:14](https://ref.ly/Rev21:14)). Some scholars have suggested that Jesus was referring to himself when he said this rock*,* but it seems clear that Jesus was referring either to Peter or to his confession. However, it is clearly Jesus’ church (my church), not Peter’s, and Jesus himself will build it.
