So it is not necessary to conclude that later church leaders must derive their authority from Peter. • Matthew is the only Gospel writer who uses the term church (also [Matt 18:17](https://ref.ly/Matt18:17)). The idea here is more *the community of God’s people* than an ecclesiastical institution. • will not conquer it: The church will not be defeated by the attacks of Satan (see [11:12](https://ref.ly/Matt11:12); [13:24–30](https://ref.ly/Matt13:24-Matt13:30), [36–43](https://ref.ly/Matt13:36-Matt13:43)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:18
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:19 (id: 21806)

Keys are an image for access to privileged knowledge that gives one authority (see [13:16–17](https://ref.ly/Matt13:16-Matt13:17); [23:13](https://ref.ly/Matt23:13); [Isa 22:22](https://ref.ly/Isa22:22); [Rev 3:7](https://ref.ly/Rev3:7)). • forbid … permit: Jesus granted to Peter (and later to the rest of the Twelve, [Matt 18:18](https://ref.ly/Matt18:18)) the authority to teach the will of God as revealed in Jesus Christ ([13:52](https://ref.ly/Matt13:52); [18:15–20](https://ref.ly/Matt18:15-Matt18:20); [23:2–12](https://ref.ly/Matt23:2-Matt23:12); [28:16–20](https://ref.ly/Matt28:16-Matt28:20)). • will be: This could be translated *will have been*, emphasizing that God’s sovereign decision comes first.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:19
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:21 (id: 21809)

This is the first of three predictions of Jesus’ *passion*—his suffering through betrayal, crucifixion, and death (see also [17:22–23](https://ref.ly/Matt17:22-Matt17:23); [20:18–19](https://ref.ly/Matt20:18-Matt20:19)). Each prediction gives a lesson on the cost of discipleship ([16:24–27](https://ref.ly/Matt16:24-Matt16:27); [20:20–28](https://ref.ly/Matt20:20-Matt20:28)). • That he would suffer was God’s sovereign and necessary purpose for the Messiah (see [17:12](https://ref.ly/Matt17:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:21
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:21–28 (id: 21808)

Jesus, now officially recognized by his disciples as the Messiah, begins to reveal a startling aspect of his mission: He must suffer before entering his glory ([16:21–23](https://ref.ly/Matt16:21-Matt16:23)), and those who follow him will meet a similar fate ([16:24–28](https://ref.ly/Matt16:24-Matt16:28)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:21–MAT 16:28
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:22 (id: 21810)

began to reprimand him: Though Peter accurately perceived Jesus’ identity as God’s Messiah, he did not understand that the Messiah must suffer.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:22
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:23 (id: 21811)

As when Satan tempted Jesus to assume royal privileges without first enduring the cross (see [4:8–10](https://ref.ly/Matt4:8-Matt4:10)), so now Jesus perceived Peter’s suggestion as incited by satanic forces. • dangerous trap: Literally *stumbling block*.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:23
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:24 (id: 21812)

give … take … follow: These three imperatives use different images to speak of the same radical commitment of confessing one’s sinfulness before God in humility, surrendering one’s personal ambition to God, and living according to his will (see also [5:20](https://ref.ly/Matt5:20); [10:34–39](https://ref.ly/Matt10:34-Matt10:39); [18:1–5](https://ref.ly/Matt18:1-Matt18:5); [20:20–28](https://ref.ly/Matt20:20-Matt20:28)). • Take up your cross is a metaphor for devotion (see [Luke 9:23](https://ref.ly/Luke9:23)) rather than a call to martyrdom, although martyrdom is an ever\-present possibility for Jesus’ disciples ([Matt 5:10–12](https://ref.ly/Matt5:10-Matt5:12); [10:21](https://ref.ly/Matt10:21)). • In Matthew, follow is used both literally ([9:19](https://ref.ly/Matt9:19); [26:58](https://ref.ly/Matt26:58)) and metaphorically. Metaphorically, it indicates interest in a teacher ([4:25](https://ref.ly/Matt4:25); [8:1](https://ref.ly/Matt8:1), [10](https://ref.ly/Matt8:10); [12:15](https://ref.ly/Matt12:15); [14:13](https://ref.ly/Matt14:13); [19:2](https://ref.ly/Matt19:2); [20:29](https://ref.ly/Matt20:29); [21:9](https://ref.ly/Matt21:9)) or personal allegiance to Jesus involving a call, a commitment, and great ongoing costs ([4:20](https://ref.ly/Matt4:20), [22](https://ref.ly/Matt4:22); [8:19](https://ref.ly/Matt8:19), [22–23](https://ref.ly/Matt8:22-Matt8:23); [9:9](https://ref.ly/Matt9:9); [10:38](https://ref.ly/Matt10:38); [16:24](https://ref.ly/Matt16:24); [19:21](https://ref.ly/Matt19:21), [27](https://ref.ly/Matt19:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:24
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:25 (id: 21813)

Jesus’ disciples must relinquish control of their lives, even to the point of being willing to suffer and die for Christ. Jesus promised that those who follow him with such radical abandon, though they may suffer now, will be vindicated at the final judgment (see [1 Pet 2:23](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:25
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:26 (id: 21814)

your own soul? “Soul” and “life” ([16:25](https://ref.ly/Matt16:25)) both translate the same Greek term (psuchē) and refer to the essence of a person—the self.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:26
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:27 (id: 21815)

The exhortation to deny oneself and follow Jesus is rooted in the fact that Jesus will return to judge all people according to their deeds (see [19:28](https://ref.ly/Matt19:28); [24:29–31](https://ref.ly/Matt24:29-Matt24:31); [25:31](https://ref.ly/Matt25:31); [Ps 62:12](https://ref.ly/Ps62:12); [Prov 24:12](https://ref.ly/Prov24:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:27
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 16:28 (id: 21816)

This saying has been taken to refer either to (1\) the transfiguration that follows ([17:1–13](https://ref.ly/Matt17:1-Matt17:13)); (2\) the death and resurrection of Jesus Christ ([27:50–53](https://ref.ly/Matt27:50-Matt27:53); [28:1–10](https://ref.ly/Matt28:1-Matt28:10)); (3\) Pentecost ([Acts 2:1–47](https://ref.ly/Acts2:1-Acts2:47)); (4\) the destruction of Jerusalem in AD 70 ([Matt 24:1–31](https://ref.ly/Matt24:1-Matt24:31)); (5\) the second coming of Christ in the future ([24:29–31](https://ref.ly/Matt24:29-Matt24:31)); or (6\) an unfolding revelation of God’s Kingdom in various ways, including the evangelism of the world. In the fourth view, coming would mean “coming in judgment” upon sinful Israel. • The expression Son of Man ([16:27–28](https://ref.ly/Matt16:27-Matt16:28)) forms an *inclusio* (bracketing expression) with [16:13](https://ref.ly/Matt16:13), unifying [16:13–28](https://ref.ly/Matt16:13-Matt16:28) around the theme of the identity of the Son of Man. He is the Messiah who would suffer and then be exalted by God and return as Judge.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 16:28
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 17:1 (id: 21821)

Peter … James and John later accompanied Jesus at Gethsemane ([26:37](https://ref.ly/Matt26:37); [2 Pet 1:16–19](https://ref.ly/2Pet1:16-2Pet1:19)). • It is impossible to determine the exact location of this high mountain. The traditional site, Mount Tabor, is only about 1,900 feet (580 meters) high and is out of the way for a trip from Caesarea Philippi ([Matt 16:13](https://ref.ly/Matt16:13)) to Capernaum ([17:24](https://ref.ly/Matt17:24)). Mount Hermon, another possibility, is about 9,200 feet (2,800 meters) high and located in Syria, forty miles north of Capernaum. It is unlikely, however, that “teachers of religious law” ([Mark 9:14](https://ref.ly/Mark9:14)) would have congregated at the foot of a mountain in Gentile territory. A strong candidate is Mount Meron, about 4,000 feet (1,220 meters) high and situated between Caesarea Philippi and Capernaum.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 17:1
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 17:2 (id: 21826)

Jesus’ appearance was transformed: Jesus’ inner, divine nature, previously veiled, was now disclosed so that the three caught a glimpse of his glory (see [Exod 34:29–35](https://ref.ly/Exod34:29-Exod34:35); [Ps 104:2](https://ref.ly/Ps104:2); [2 Cor 3:12–18](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:12-2Cor3:18); [Rev 1:16](https://ref.ly/Rev1:16)). Jesus’ followers will one day share in this glory ([Matt 13:43](https://ref.ly/Matt13:43)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 17:2
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 17:3 (id: 21827)

Moses symbolizes the law and Elijah the prophets. They appeared as witnesses to Christ, to demonstrate that Jesus, God’s Son, is the fulfillment of everything written in the Law and the Prophets (see [5:17–20](https://ref.ly/Matt5:17-Matt5:20); [11:2–6](https://ref.ly/Matt11:2-Matt11:6); [12:28](https://ref.ly/Matt12:28)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 17:3
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 17:4 (id: 21828)

three shelters as memorials: Peter probably thought that the Kingdom was about to be ushered in with full glory (cp. [Acts 1:6](https://ref.ly/Acts1:6)), and he desired to memorialize the moment.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 17:4
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 17:5 (id: 21829)

a bright cloud overshadowed them: Such an occurrence accompanied God’s presence among the ancient Israelites during Moses’ ministry (see [Exod 24:15–18](https://ref.ly/Exod24:15-Exod24:18); [25:8](https://ref.ly/Exod25:8); [29:45–46](https://ref.ly/Exod29:45-Exod29:46); [40:34–38](https://ref.ly/Exod40:34-Exod40:38)). • my dearly loved Son: The Father was confirming what Peter had previously affirmed ([Matt 16:16–17](https://ref.ly/Matt16:16-Matt16:17)). • They should listen to him because Jesus is God’s Son, who, as a prophet, reveals God’s will ([11:27](https://ref.ly/Matt11:27); see [Deut 18:15](https://ref.ly/Deut18:15), [18](https://ref.ly/Deut18:18); [Acts 3:22–23](https://ref.ly/Acts3:22-Acts3:23); [7:37](https://ref.ly/Acts7:37)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 17:5
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 17:6–7 (id: 21830)

Such a response is typical for encounters with God’s glory (e.g., [Isa 6:5](https://ref.ly/Isa6:5); [Dan 8:17](https://ref.ly/Dan8:17); [10:9](https://ref.ly/Dan10:9), [15–19](https://ref.ly/Dan10:15-Dan10:19); [Rev 1:17](https://ref.ly/Rev1:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 17:6–MAT 17:7
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 17:9 (id: 21831)

Jesus could not be fully understood until all of his work was accomplished, particularly his death and resurrection.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 17:9
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 17:10–13 (id: 21819)

Elijah’s presence at the transfiguration prompted a question about the view that Elijah must return before the Messiah comes (see [Mal 4:5–6](https://ref.ly/Mal4:5-Mal4:6)). In pointing to John the Baptist*,* Jesus reinforced the unexpected idea that the Messiah must suffer*,* even as his precursor had suffered ([Matt 14:3–12](https://ref.ly/Matt14:3-Matt14:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 17:10–MAT 17:13
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 17:17 (id: 21820)

faithless and corrupt people: The expression is often used for moral depravity (see [Deut 32:5](https://ref.ly/Deut32:5), [19–22](https://ref.ly/Deut32:19-Deut32:22)). Normally, this exclamation of Jesus was directed at the unbelieving Jewish crowds or leaders who refuse to acknowledge God’s presence in him (see [Matt 12:39](https://ref.ly/Matt12:39)). Here, however, it was a sharp criticism of his disciples’ failure to trust Jesus and his saving, healing power.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 17:17
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 17:20 (id: 21822)

Here, the expression don’t have enough faith is virtually synonymous with *no faith*. • faith even as small as a mustard seed: This could mean that if the disciples had even very little faith they would be able to accomplish great things ([21:21](https://ref.ly/Matt21:21); cp. [1 Cor 13:2](https://ref.ly/1Cor13:2)). It could also mean that if they would allow their faith to grow (see [Matt 13:31–32](https://ref.ly/Matt13:31-Matt13:32)), they could act with courageous belief. • Moving mountains is an adage for overcoming obstacles and fulfilling God’s purposes ([Isa 40:4](https://ref.ly/Isa40:4); [49:11](https://ref.ly/Isa49:11); [54:10](https://ref.ly/Isa54:10); [1 Cor 13:2](https://ref.ly/1Cor13:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 17:20
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 17:22 (id: 21823)

betrayed: See [Matt 20:18](https://ref.ly/Matt20:18); [26:14–16](https://ref.ly/Matt26:14-Matt26:16), [45–49](https://ref.ly/Matt26:45-Matt26:49) for the fulfillment of this prediction.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 17:22
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 17:24 (id: 21824)

Every adult citizen of Israel was required to pay the Temple tax of one\-half shekel. In Jesus’ day, priests and some rabbis did not pay the tax. • Peter was the spokesman for the Twelve (see [10:2](https://ref.ly/Matt10:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 17:24
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 17:25–26 (id: 21825)

As an obedient Jew, Jesus would have paid the tax annually, and he did pay it. Jesus’ point was that as God’s Son, he is greater than the Temple ([12:5–6](https://ref.ly/Matt12:5-Matt12:6)), and he makes a decisive break with it (see [16:18–19](https://ref.ly/Matt16:18-Matt16:19); [21:33–46](https://ref.ly/Matt21:33-Matt21:46)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 17:25–MAT 17:26
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:1 (id: 21844)

About that time: Matthew connects the disciples’ questions with the previous discussion concerning the Temple. The disciples began to assume that their new freedom in relation to Jewish authority entitled them to authority of their own. In addition, talk of special revelations ([11:25–27](https://ref.ly/Matt11:25-Matt11:27); [13:11–17](https://ref.ly/Matt13:11-Matt13:17)) and roles of leadership ([10:2–4](https://ref.ly/Matt10:2-Matt10:4); [19:28](https://ref.ly/Matt19:28)) probably gave rise to jealous comparisons and petty desires for power among the disciples, perhaps revolving around the apparent privilege of Peter ([17:25](https://ref.ly/Matt17:25)) or Peter, James, and John ([17:1–3](https://ref.ly/Matt17:1-Matt17:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:1
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:1–35 (id: 21832)

This fourth major discourse in Matthew (see study note on Matt 5:1–7:29) focuses on responses to the Messiah—acceptance by the disciples and rejection by the Jewish leaders and most of the populace. In light of this growing polarization, Jesus began to instruct his followers on the nature of community life. For a community to live according to Jesus’ standards, it must live with humility ([18:1–5](https://ref.ly/Matt18:1-Matt18:5)), sensitivity ([18:6–9](https://ref.ly/Matt18:6-Matt18:9)), compassion ([18:10–14](https://ref.ly/Matt18:10-Matt18:14)), discipline ([18:15–18](https://ref.ly/Matt18:15-Matt18:18)), and forgiveness ([18:21–35](https://ref.ly/Matt18:21-Matt18:35)). As with the other discourses, a concluding formula ([19:1–2](https://ref.ly/Matt19:1-Matt19:2)) bridges to the next section.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:1–MAT 18:35
* **Associated Articles:** Matthew 5:1-7.29 (ID: 22169)

## Matthew 18:3 (id: 21853)

Like little children means to be humble ([18:4](https://ref.ly/Matt18:4)). The disciples had been intent on status and ambition.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:3
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:5 (id: 21854)

Jesus moved the discussion toward solidarity within the community; to welcome a humble follower of Jesus is to welcome Jesus himself (see [10:40–42](https://ref.ly/Matt10:40-Matt10:42)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:5
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:6 (id: 21855)

To cause one … to fall into sin is to lead believing children (or possibly believing adults who become “like children”; see [18:3](https://ref.ly/Matt18:3)) to reject Christ and abandon the faith. • The designation little ones emphasizes their humility ([5:3–12](https://ref.ly/Matt5:3-Matt5:12); [18:4](https://ref.ly/Matt18:4); [19:13–15](https://ref.ly/Matt19:13-Matt19:15)). • Though the thought of being drowned with a large millstone around the neck is frightful, Jesus warned that causing another to fall away will bring far greater misery ([18:7](https://ref.ly/Matt18:7); [26:24](https://ref.ly/Matt26:24); [Rev 18:21](https://ref.ly/Rev18:21); see [Matt 22:13](https://ref.ly/Matt22:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:6
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:8–9 (id: 21856)

Concern shifts to the individual: Get rid of whatever causes you to sin (see [5:29–30](https://ref.ly/Matt5:29-Matt5:30); [Col 3:5–17](https://ref.ly/Col3:5-Col3:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:8–MAT 18:9
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:10 (id: 21833)

Don’t look down on them, either by refusing to receive them ([18:5–6](https://ref.ly/Matt18:5-Matt18:6)) or by refusing to give pastoral care when needed ([18:12–14](https://ref.ly/Matt18:12-Matt18:14); see [19:13–15](https://ref.ly/Matt19:13-Matt19:15)). • their angels: See [4:5–7](https://ref.ly/Matt4:5-Matt4:7); [Heb 1:14](https://ref.ly/Heb1:14).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:10
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:12 (id: 21834)

Just as a shepherd will work to recover a lost sheep*,* the “little ones” ([18:6](https://ref.ly/Matt18:6)) must not be despised or neglected.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:12
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:14 (id: 21835)

The shepherd’s joy is also the joy of the Father; the purpose of pastoral care is so God will not lose any of his sheep.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:14
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:15 (id: 21838)

If another believer sins*,* love requires us to go privately and point out the offense ([Lev 19:17](https://ref.ly/Lev19:17); [Luke 17:3](https://ref.ly/Luke17:3); [Gal 6:1](https://ref.ly/Gal6:1); [1 Tim 5:20](https://ref.ly/1Tim5:20); [Titus 3:10](https://ref.ly/Titus3:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:15
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:15–20 (id: 21836)

Restoration begins privately and should be made public only as a last resort.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:15–MAT 18:20
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:15–35 (id: 21837)

The believing community must not be fractured into rival parties and unreconciled relationships. Its members are to pursue reconciliation ([18:15–20](https://ref.ly/Matt18:15-Matt18:20)) and forgive willingly ([18:21–35](https://ref.ly/Matt18:21-Matt18:35)). At times, however, stern discipline may be necessary ([18:17](https://ref.ly/Matt18:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:15–MAT 18:35
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:16 (id: 21839)

By requiring the presence of one or two others*,* Jesus prevented slanderous, unsubstantiated accusations from being presented to the congregation (see [John 8:17](https://ref.ly/John8:17); [2 Cor 13:1](https://ref.ly/2Cor13:1); [1 Tim 5:19](https://ref.ly/1Tim5:19); [Heb 10:28](https://ref.ly/Heb10:28)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:16
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:17 (id: 21840)

The church is the local Christian community. • The unrepentant person is to be considered a pagan or a corrupt tax collector, a wicked transgressor of the law. Church discipline by exclusion (excommunication; see [Acts 5:1–6](https://ref.ly/Acts5:1-Acts5:6); [Rom 16:17](https://ref.ly/Rom16:17); [1 Cor 5:1–13](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:1-1Cor5:13); [2 Cor 6:14–18](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:14-2Cor6:18); [Gal 5:7–12](https://ref.ly/Gal5:7-Gal5:12); [2 Thes 3:14–15](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:14-2Thess3:15)) is rooted in the conviction that God’s people are to be holy and that sin corrupts fellowship, both between people and between the people and God. The goal is neither vindictive retribution nor a public display of power, but restoration of the wayward to holiness and fellowship ([Matt 18:10–15](https://ref.ly/Matt18:10-Matt18:15); [Gal 6:1](https://ref.ly/Gal6:1); [Jas 5:19–20](https://ref.ly/Jas5:19-Jas5:20)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:17
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:18 (id: 21842)

forbid … permit: The privilege and authority granted to Peter ([16:19](https://ref.ly/Matt16:19)) are here granted to the church (or possibly to the twelve apostles, [18:1](https://ref.ly/Matt18:1)). The decisions of the community, when in accord with God’s will, are eternally binding.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:18
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:18–20 (id: 21841)

These sayings provide the basis for a process of discipline and restoration in the community of disciples.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:18–MAT 18:20
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:19 (id: 21843)

anything you ask: In the context of church discipline ([18:15–17](https://ref.ly/Matt18:15-Matt18:17)), this suggests that discipline must be done in prayer.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:19
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:20 (id: 21845)

Christ is present in the process of discipline, so the process is a ratification of God’s decision.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:20
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:21–35 (id: 21846)

Peter’s suggestion of seven times was generous, so Jesus’ answer was startling. The disciple’s willingness to forgive should be like God’s forgiving grace, limitless and free (see [18:10–14](https://ref.ly/Matt18:10-Matt18:14)). Those who do not forgive in this way cannot themselves have experienced God’s forgiveness ([18:35](https://ref.ly/Matt18:35); see [6:12](https://ref.ly/Matt6:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:21–MAT 18:35
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:22 (id: 21847)

seventy times seven: Or *seventy\-seven times*; either way, Jesus prescribes limitless readiness to forgive from the heart ([18:35](https://ref.ly/Matt18:35); cp. [Gen 4:23–24](https://ref.ly/Gen4:23-Gen4:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:22
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:24 (id: 21848)

millions of dollars (Greek *10,000 talents*): The talent was the highest unit of currency, but its value fluctuated. The debt was clearly impossible to pay—this amount exceeded the tax revenue of all Galilee.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:24
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:26 (id: 21849)

I will pay it all: The exaggerated debt and the slave’s promise amplify the greatness of the king’s mercy and the slave’s unforgiving attitude ([18:29–30](https://ref.ly/Matt18:29-Matt18:30)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:26
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:28 (id: 21850)

a few thousand dollars: The first servant’s debt was about one million times greater than this sum owed to him.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:28
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:34 (id: 21851)

This is how God responds ([18:35](https://ref.ly/Matt18:35)) to anyone unwilling to forgive. • until he had paid his entire debt: I.e., permanently, because he could never repay.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:34
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 18:35 (id: 21852)

That’s what my heavenly Father will do to you: Prison and torture ([18:34](https://ref.ly/Matt18:34)) is thus a metaphor for hell (see [5:22](https://ref.ly/Matt5:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 18:35
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 19:1–20.34 (id: 21857)

Jesus was now on the move toward Jerusalem ([19:1](https://ref.ly/Matt19:1); [20:29](https://ref.ly/Matt20:29); [21:1](https://ref.ly/Matt21:1)), with a further opportunity for instructing the disciples on various aspects of discipleship.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 19:1–MAT 20:19
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 19:3 (id: 21867)

There were two divergent views on when one was allowed to divorce one’s wife. One group of Pharisees, following Rabbi Shammai, argued that divorce was allowed only in the case of adultery or other grave sin, while the other group, following Rabbi Hillel, contended that a man could divorce his wife for any reason, such as if she burned his dinner.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 19:3
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 19:4–5 (id: 21868)

The Pharisees were not considering *all* of God’s word. The Creator had made marriage as a permanent union (see [Gen 2:18–25](https://ref.ly/Gen2:18-Gen2:25); see also [1 Cor 7:10–16](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:10-1Cor7:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 19:4–MAT 19:5
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 19:6 (id: 21869)

Since God made marriage a union, humans do not have the right to break that union. Jesus affirmed the indissolubility of marriage.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 19:6
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 19:7–8 (id: 21870)

why did Moses say (literally *command*): The Pharisees thought Jesus had contradicted a command of the law (see [Deut 24:1–4](https://ref.ly/Deut24:1-Deut24:4)), but Moses permitted divorce only as a concession to their hard hearts. Jesus introduced the revolutionary principle that God’s permission is not necessarily his desire (see [1 Cor 6:12](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:12)). Divorce is never God’s desire ([Mal 2:14–16](https://ref.ly/Mal2:14-Mal2:16)); it is an expression of human sin.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 19:7–MAT 19:8
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 19:9 (id: 21871)

Jesus permits only one legitimate reason for a man to divorce: if his wife has been unfaithful (see [5:32](https://ref.ly/Matt5:32)). In the face of those who thought divorce could be taken lightly, Jesus affirms God’s created order: Marriage was designed to be permanent (see [Mark 10:11–12](https://ref.ly/Mark10:11-Mark10:12)). • commits adultery: This speaks only of the man who divorces his wife unlawfully. In such a case, his remarriage is adulterous. Jesus’ motivation is to reestablish the permanency of marriage.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 19:9
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 19:11 (id: 21858)

This statement refers to the disciples’ comment ([19:10](https://ref.ly/Matt19:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 19:11
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 19:12 (id: 21859)

Eunuchs are males castrated either by a birth defect or by a surgical operation. Jesus also uses the term metaphorically for those who choose not to marry (see [Luke 14:26](https://ref.ly/Luke14:26); [18:29](https://ref.ly/Luke18:29); [1 Cor 7:7–8](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:7-1Cor7:8)). • for the sake of the Kingdom: Jesus was not denigrating marriage; he was simply indicating that the unmarried often have greater potential for ministry (see [1 Cor 7:25–35](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:25-1Cor7:35)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 19:12
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 19:13 (id: 21860)

Jesus would lay his hands on others to bless them (see [Luke 4:40](https://ref.ly/Luke4:40); [13:13](https://ref.ly/Luke13:13); see also [Gen 48:14–15](https://ref.ly/Gen48:14-Gen48:15); [Acts 19:6](https://ref.ly/Acts19:6)). • The disciples*,* motivated to protect Jesus, scolded the parents*,* demonstrating a wrong attitude toward children (see [Matt 18:5–6](https://ref.ly/Matt18:5-Matt18:6), [10](https://ref.ly/Matt18:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 19:13
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 19:17 (id: 21861)

Why ask me? The man, as a Jew, should have known that God’s standard of goodness is clearly reflected in his commandments. The man’s questions (also [19:20](https://ref.ly/Matt19:20)) show that he was not trusting in the adequacy of God’s revealed will. • only One … is good: The man may have believed he could act with perfect goodness on his own, whereas only God is truly good and thus the source of all goodness. • keep the commandments: Jesus has in mind either leading the man to see his sinfulness by asking him to do the impossible, or more probably, restating that good works are a telling gauge of the truthfulness of a person’s faith (see [7:13–27](https://ref.ly/Matt7:13-Matt7:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 19:17
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 19:21–22 (id: 21862)

By calling the man to go and sell and come, follow me*,* Jesus revealed that the man had not in fact kept the first of the ten commandments ([Exod 20:3](https://ref.ly/Exod20:3)). His possessions—his wealth and security—had become his god (see [Matt 6:20](https://ref.ly/Matt6:20), [24](https://ref.ly/Matt6:24); [13:44–46](https://ref.ly/Matt13:44-Matt13:46)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 19:21–MAT 19:22
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 19:23 (id: 21863)

Jesus draws a lesson for discipleship from the rich man’s tragic denial. It is hard for the rich to humble themselves, admit their need, and trust in God (see [5:3](https://ref.ly/Matt5:3); [Luke 6:24](https://ref.ly/Luke6:24); [1 Tim 6:9–10](https://ref.ly/1Tim6:9-1Tim6:10)). • Kingdom of Heaven is equivalent here to *eternal life* ([Matt 19:16–17](https://ref.ly/Matt19:16-Matt19:17), [29](https://ref.ly/Matt19:29)) or to *salvation* as the result of God’s regenerating work ([19:25–26](https://ref.ly/Matt19:25-Matt19:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 19:23
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 19:24 (id: 21864)

easier for a camel: This analogy reinforces the difficulty that wealthy people face in entering the Kingdom. A few manuscripts have a Greek word meaning *rope* (Greek kamilos) instead of *camel* (Greek kamēlos), a difference of only one letter. • to go through the eye of a needle: The image makes the wealthy entering the Kingdom an impossibility. The situation is not utterly hopeless, however ([19:26–27](https://ref.ly/Matt19:26-Matt19:27)). See study note on Mark 10:25.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 19:24
* **Associated Articles:** Mark 10:25 (ID: 21237)

## Matthew 19:26 (id: 21865)

God’s regenerating grace is absolutely essential before the wealthy are able to repent from their idolatry, abandon their possessions if called to do so, and follow Jesus ([19:21](https://ref.ly/Matt19:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 19:26
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 19:28 (id: 21866)

you … will also sit on twelve thrones: The disciples’ part in judging is a reversal—those who are wealthy and powerful now will be judged by those who are humble and poor (see [19:30](https://ref.ly/Matt19:30)). • Judging can mean both ruling and condemning (see [Rev 20:4](https://ref.ly/Rev20:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 19:28
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 20:1–16 (id: 21888)

This parable is similar to the parable of the Lost Son ([Luke 15:11–32](https://ref.ly/Luke15:11-Luke15:32)). In both, God’s grace is shown to two parties while one grumbles about unjust treatment.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 20:1–MAT 20:16
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 20:8 (id: 21900)

Payment followed the day’s work ([Deut 24:14–15](https://ref.ly/Deut24:14-Deut24:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 20:8
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 20:16 (id: 21889)

See [Matt 5:19](https://ref.ly/Matt5:19); [8:11–12](https://ref.ly/Matt8:11-Matt8:12).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 20:16
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 20:20–21 (id: 21890)

This mother’s question appears to have been inspired by her sons, since Jesus responded to the sons rather than to the mother (cp. [Mark 10:35–37](https://ref.ly/Mark10:35-Mark10:37)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 20:20–MAT 20:21
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 20:20–28 (id: 21891)

Each prediction of Jesus’ suffering in Matthew is connected to instruction on the nature of discipleship in light of that suffering (see [16:24–28](https://ref.ly/Matt16:24-Matt16:28); [17:24–18:5](https://ref.ly/Matt17:24-Matt18:5)). This teaching called the Messiah’s disciples to follow his example of service and sacrifice.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 20:20–MAT 20:28
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 20:21 (id: 21892)

The promise of sitting in positions of authority in God’s Kingdom had already been given ([19:28](https://ref.ly/Matt19:28)); the brothers’ request seems to have been motivated out of selfish desire for prominence, with no regard for the suffering the Messiah would soon undergo (see [Matt 23:6](https://ref.ly/Matt23:6); [Luke 14:7–11](https://ref.ly/Luke14:7-Luke14:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 20:21
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 20:22 (id: 21893)

The cup refers to Jesus’ duty, calling, and destiny (see [26:39](https://ref.ly/Matt26:39); [John 18:11](https://ref.ly/John18:11); see also [Ps 75:8](https://ref.ly/Ps75:8); [Isa 51:17](https://ref.ly/Isa51:17), [22](https://ref.ly/Isa51:22); [Rev 16:19](https://ref.ly/Rev16:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 20:22
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 20:23 (id: 21894)

You will indeed: James was eventually martyred ([Acts 12:2](https://ref.ly/Acts12:2)), and John suffered significant persecution ([Acts 4:3](https://ref.ly/Acts4:3); [5:40](https://ref.ly/Acts5:40); [Rev 1:9](https://ref.ly/Rev1:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 20:23
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 20:24 (id: 21895)

The other disciples … were indignant: Selfish ambition was apparently not unique to James and John (see also [21:15](https://ref.ly/Matt21:15); [26:8](https://ref.ly/Matt26:8); [Luke 13:14](https://ref.ly/Luke13:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 20:24
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 20:25–28 (id: 21896)

The desire for power is characteristic of pagan rulers in this world. It ought not to be a trait of those who follow the Son of Man ([18:1–5](https://ref.ly/Matt18:1-Matt18:5); [19:13–15](https://ref.ly/Matt19:13-Matt19:15); [23:1–12](https://ref.ly/Matt23:1-Matt23:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 20:25–MAT 20:28
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 20:27 (id: 21897)

The word slave is a common metaphor for the submissive relationship of a disciple to his master ([8:9](https://ref.ly/Matt8:9); [10:24–25](https://ref.ly/Matt10:24-Matt10:25); [24:45–51](https://ref.ly/Matt24:45-Matt24:51); [25:14–30](https://ref.ly/Matt25:14-Matt25:30)). Jesus’ disciples serve others, following Jesus’ example (e.g., [John 13:1–17](https://ref.ly/John13:1-John13:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 20:27
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 20:28 (id: 21898)

This expression, the Son of Man came*,* suggests Jesus’ preexistence (see [Dan 7:13–14](https://ref.ly/Dan7:13-Dan7:14)). • Jesus was describing his voluntary offering of himself as a ransom for many, to pay the debt all people owe (see [Matt 26:26–29](https://ref.ly/Matt26:26-Matt26:29); [Isa 53:10–12](https://ref.ly/Isa53:10-Isa53:12); [Rom 3:24](https://ref.ly/Rom3:24)), thereby buying them out of slavery (see [Gal 5:1](https://ref.ly/Gal5:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 20:28
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 20:29–34 (id: 21899)

The blind men’s expression of faith in the Son of David was an acknowledgment of Jesus as the Messiah (see [21:9](https://ref.ly/Matt21:9); [22:42](https://ref.ly/Matt22:42); [2 Sam 7:12–16](https://ref.ly/2Sam7:12-2Sam7:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 20:29–MAT 20:34
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:1 (id: 21909)

Bethphage (a Hebrew name meaning *house of figs*) was probably located on the eastern slope of the Mount of Olives between Bethany and Jerusalem proper.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:1
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:1–28.20 (id: 21901)

Jesus’ entry into Jerusalem initiates Matthew’s account of how the Messiah’s suffering and resurrection establish salvation.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:1–MAT 21:11
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:3 (id: 21923)

Jesus was revealing himself as the Lord who, as king of Israel, ascends to Mount Zion on a donkey ([21:5](https://ref.ly/Matt21:5); see [Zech 9:9](https://ref.ly/Zech9:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:3
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:4–5 (id: 21924)

The Old Testament fulfillment here emphasizes the Messiah’s non\-violent, humble*,* and saving work (see [11:28–30](https://ref.ly/Matt11:28-Matt11:30); [Isa 62:11](https://ref.ly/Isa62:11); [Zech 9:9–10](https://ref.ly/Zech9:9-Zech9:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:4–MAT 21:5
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:11 (id: 21902)

The crowds with Jesus understood him to be a prophet*,* empowered by God to teach and to perform miracles. • The description from Nazareth in Galilee highlights Jesus’ humble origins (see [2:23](https://ref.ly/Matt2:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:11
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:12 (id: 21904)

Buying and selling took place within the Temple complex, in the Court of the Gentiles. • Money changers profited from the exchange of money from other currencies into official Jewish currency. Jesus criticized the commercialism that profaned the holiness of the Temple (see [Mark 11:11–18](https://ref.ly/Mark11:11-Mark11:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:12
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:12–13 (id: 21903)

The close association of the Temple cleansing (see [John 2:13–16](https://ref.ly/John2:13-John2:16)) with the cursing of the fig tree ([Matt 21:18–19](https://ref.ly/Matt21:18-Matt21:19)) reveals Jesus as the Messiah who confronted Israel and warned that God judges those who reject the Messiah and his message.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:12–MAT 21:13
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:13 (id: 21905)

Jesus’ actions were justified, because God’s glory was being desecrated through financial exploitation.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:13
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:15 (id: 21906)

The Jewish leaders’ stubborn refusal to believe is contrasted with the exuberant faith and praise of little children (see [18:1–14](https://ref.ly/Matt18:1-Matt18:14); [19:13–15](https://ref.ly/Matt19:13-Matt19:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:15
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:16 (id: 21907)

Haven’t you ever read the Scriptures? Jesus put this penetrating question to opponents who did not perceive the fulfillment of messianic promises in his ministry. See also [12:3](https://ref.ly/Matt12:3), [5](https://ref.ly/Matt12:5); [19:4](https://ref.ly/Matt19:4); [21:42](https://ref.ly/Matt21:42); [22:31](https://ref.ly/Matt22:31).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:16
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:19 (id: 21908)

there were only leaves: Mark observes that “it was too early in the season for fruit” (see [Mark 11:13](https://ref.ly/Mark11:13)). It was spring (just before Passover); figs form in the spring but ripen in the fall. • immediately the fig tree withered: Matthew has apparently compressed the story (cp. [Matt 21:18–22](https://ref.ly/Matt21:18-Matt21:22); [Mark 11:13–14](https://ref.ly/Mark11:13-Mark11:14), [20–23](https://ref.ly/Mark11:20-Mark11:23)). The cursing of the fig tree is a symbolic gesture depicting God’s judgment on Israel for rejecting the Messiah (see [Matt 3:9](https://ref.ly/Matt3:9); [8:11–12](https://ref.ly/Matt8:11-Matt8:12)). Like a fig tree that shows promise but no fruit, the Israelites (especially the hypocritical leaders) did not bear the fruit of receiving the Messiah (see [21:33–46](https://ref.ly/Matt21:33-Matt21:46)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:19
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:22 (id: 21910)

Jesus was exhorting the disciples to trust in God and to pray accordingly. He was not offering God’s unconditional endorsement of all that they might desire ([1 Jn 5:14–15](https://ref.ly/1John5:14-1John5:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:22
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:23 (id: 21912)

Elders (literally *elders of the people*) were family heads from each tribe who were members of the Sanhedrin in Jerusalem (cp. [Ezra 5:5](https://ref.ly/Ezra5:5); [6:14](https://ref.ly/Ezra6:14); [10:8](https://ref.ly/Ezra10:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:23
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:23–22.46 (id: 21911)

This section focuses on the Jewish leaders’ attack on Jesus’ authority. In each case, Jesus’ wisdom revealed the leaders’ spiritual blindness. These debates also revealed Jesus’ status as Messiah and the consequences of rejecting him. Tragically, the leaders grew more resistant with each encounter and plotted to eliminate Jesus ([21:23](https://ref.ly/Matt21:23), [46](https://ref.ly/Matt21:46); [22:15–17](https://ref.ly/Matt22:15-Matt22:17), [23](https://ref.ly/Matt22:23), [34](https://ref.ly/Matt22:34), [41](https://ref.ly/Matt22:41)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:23–MAT 22:46
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:24 (id: 21913)

Jesus propounded a riddle, the solution to which answered the leaders’ question and forced them into a dilemma that revealed their hearts ([21:25–26](https://ref.ly/Matt21:25-Matt21:26)). Answering by counter\-question was typical for such debates.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:24
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:25 (id: 21914)

John’s ministry, like Jesus’ (see [3:1](https://ref.ly/Matt3:1), [5–6](https://ref.ly/Matt3:5-Matt3:6)), was controversial, especially after John’s public denouncement of the sins of Herod Antipas (see [14:4](https://ref.ly/Matt14:4)). The leaders did not want to acknowledge that John’s ministry was from God, since they had refused to believe John by repenting of their sins ([3:2](https://ref.ly/Matt3:2)) and accepting Jesus as the Messiah ([John 1:29–34](https://ref.ly/John1:29-John1:34)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:25
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:27 (id: 21915)

The leaders lacked integrity and courage to confess what they believed about John. So Jesus’ refusal to answer their original question was fair.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:27
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:28–32 (id: 21917)

This parable continues the point about John’s significance.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:28–MAT 21:32
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:28–22.14 (id: 21916)

Three parables expose the guilt of those who had rejected the Messiah and forfeited their privilege as God’s chosen people. The new people of God are only those who embrace the Messiah.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:28–MAT 22:14
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:29 (id: 21918)

I won’t go: This response must have offended Jews who were taught to show outward respect for the authority of a father (see [8:21–22](https://ref.ly/Matt8:21-Matt8:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:29
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:32 (id: 21919)

The right way to live is in conformity to God’s will ([3:15](https://ref.ly/Matt3:15); [5:20](https://ref.ly/Matt5:20); see also [Prov 8:20](https://ref.ly/Prov8:20); [12:28](https://ref.ly/Prov12:28)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:32
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:33–46 (id: 21920)

In this story Jesus draws on [Isa 5:1–7](https://ref.ly/Isa5:1-Isa5:7). The people of Israel who rejected God’s Messiah forfeited the privilege of being God’s people. The Christian community, comprised of both Jews and Gentiles, has now been called to be the people of God (cp. [Rom 9:4–8](https://ref.ly/Rom9:4-Rom9:8); [11:1–12](https://ref.ly/Rom11:1-Rom11:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:33–MAT 21:46
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:34–35 (id: 21921)

sent his servants: The prophets had spoken God’s word to Israel. The tenant farmers represented the leaders of Israel, whom Jesus held responsible for the deaths of God’s prophets ([23:29–37](https://ref.ly/Matt23:29-Matt23:37)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:34–MAT 21:35
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:37 (id: 21922)

Finally: God’s revelation climaxed in Jesus (see [13:16–17](https://ref.ly/Matt13:16-Matt13:17); [Heb 1:1–2](https://ref.ly/Heb1:1-Heb1:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:37
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:40 (id: 21925)

When the owner of the vineyard returns refers to the Lord’s coming in judgment (see [16:27](https://ref.ly/Matt16:27); [24:1–36](https://ref.ly/Matt24:1-Matt24:36)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:40
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:41 (id: 21926)

The Jewish religious leaders pronounced their own condemnation.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:41
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:42 (id: 21927)

The cornerstone was either the first stone of the foundation or the capstone (as of an arch), the last to be laid. The very stone that the builders rejected as unworthy of use was, in fact, the most important. Jesus was referring to his own role in the Kingdom of God ([21:43](https://ref.ly/Matt21:43)) and to the religious leaders’ rejection of him.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:42
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:43 (id: 21928)

taken away from you: Either the privilege of being God’s chosen nation no longer belonged to the Jews, or the religious leaders had lost the privilege of being leaders of God’s people (see [Rom 9–11](https://ref.ly/Rom9:1-Rom11:36)). • The Christian community is a nation that will produce the proper fruit—that is, a life of trust and obedience that demonstrates the inauguration of the Kingdom (see [Matt 3:8](https://ref.ly/Matt3:8); [7:15–20](https://ref.ly/Matt7:15-Matt7:20); [12:33](https://ref.ly/Matt12:33); [13:8](https://ref.ly/Matt13:8), [26](https://ref.ly/Matt13:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:43
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:44 (id: 21929)

Though in a short while the Messiah’s opponents would gain a brief victory, they would ultimately be broken and the stone would crush them because the cross became the gateway to Jesus’ vindication and triumph (see also [Dan 2:34–35](https://ref.ly/Dan2:34-Dan2:35), [44–45](https://ref.ly/Dan2:44-Dan2:45)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:44
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 21:45 (id: 21930)

This explanation fits with Matthew’s theme of God’s judgment on the Jewish leaders who misled the people of Israel (see [23:13–15](https://ref.ly/Matt23:13-Matt23:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 21:45
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:1–14 (id: 21931)

In this parable, Israel, having repeatedly rejected God’s word in the past, rejects the Messiah and is judged as a result. In Israel’s place, God raised up the church ([16:17–19](https://ref.ly/Matt16:17-Matt16:19); [21:43](https://ref.ly/Matt21:43)), of which righteousness is also expected ([Rom 11:11–24](https://ref.ly/Rom11:11-Rom11:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:1–MAT 22:14
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:2 (id: 21945)

The king represents God, whose son is Jesus ([Gal 4:4](https://ref.ly/Gal4:4); [Heb 1:1–2](https://ref.ly/Heb1:1-Heb1:2)). • The feast represents the Kingdom of the Messiah.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:2
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:3–5 (id: 21946)

Those who were invited refers to the nation of Israel, who ignored God’s servants, the prophets (see study note on Matt 21:33–46).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:3–MAT 22:5
* **Associated Articles:** Matthew 21:33-46 (ID: 21920)

## Matthew 22:7 (id: 21958)

Jesus was alluding to the coming destruction of Jerusalem in AD 70 (see [23:37–39](https://ref.ly/Matt23:37-Matt23:39); [24:2](https://ref.ly/Matt24:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:7
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:8 (id: 21959)

Those who reject God’s invitation aren’t worthy to enter his Kingdom (cp. [3:8](https://ref.ly/Matt3:8); [10:13](https://ref.ly/Matt10:13), [37–38](https://ref.ly/Matt10:37-Matt10:38)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:8
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:9 (id: 21960)

everyone you see: God’s invitation is no longer restricted to the nation of Israel (see [28:16–20](https://ref.ly/Matt28:16-Matt28:20); cp. [10:5–6](https://ref.ly/Matt10:5-Matt10:6); [15:21–28](https://ref.ly/Matt15:21-Matt15:28)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:9
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:10 (id: 21932)

good and bad alike: See [13:24–50](https://ref.ly/Matt13:24-Matt13:50).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:10
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:11 (id: 21933)

The proper clothes correspond to spiritual fruit that demonstrates real faith (see [7:13–27](https://ref.ly/Matt7:13-Matt7:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:11
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:13 (id: 21934)

Weeping and gnashing of teeth express the intense pain and sorrow that result from condemnation for sin and unbelief (see [8:12](https://ref.ly/Matt8:12); [13:42](https://ref.ly/Matt13:42), [50](https://ref.ly/Matt13:50); [24:51](https://ref.ly/Matt24:51); [25:30](https://ref.ly/Matt25:30)). • Outer darkness is a metaphor for eternal punishment.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:13
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:14 (id: 21935)

While many people are called—they hear the invitation to the Kingdom—few are actually chosen by God and respond in faithful obedience to Jesus.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:14
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:15–22 (id: 21936)

Roman taxation was a controversial issue in first\-century Palestine (see also [17:24–27](https://ref.ly/Matt17:24-Matt17:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:15–MAT 22:22
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:16 (id: 21937)

The Pharisees, strict nationalists who resented Roman rule, were normally at odds with the supporters of Herod. Here, the unlikely alliance arose from a mutual hatred of Jesus.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:16
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:17 (id: 21938)

Is it right … or not? The question was designed to trap Jesus. If he answered no, he could be arrested for rebellion against Rome. If he answered yes, he could be accused of supporting Roman oppression.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:17
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:18 (id: 21939)

You hypocrites! See study note on 23:13.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:18
* **Associated Articles:** Matthew 23:13 (ID: 21965)

## Matthew 22:20 (id: 21940)

The poll tax had to be paid using the denarius coin, which bore the picture and title of Caesar. Old Testament prohibitions against images ([Exod 20:4](https://ref.ly/Exod20:4); [Lev 26:1](https://ref.ly/Lev26:1); [Deut 4:15–24](https://ref.ly/Deut4:15-Deut4:24)) made the use of this coin controversial among Jews (see Josephus, *War* 2\.9\.2–3\). Some Roman procurators apparently produced coins without images for use in Palestine in order not to offend the Jewish conscience.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:20
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:21 (id: 21941)

Jesus outwitted his opponents by affirming the honor due to Caesar*,* while clearly differentiating it from the supreme honor and allegiance due to God. Loyalty to God does not necessarily entail disloyalty to the governing authorities. Jesus was acknowledging two dominions, Caesar’s and God’s, the latter having priority ([Acts 4:19](https://ref.ly/Acts4:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:21
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:23 (id: 21943)

The Sadducees (see [3:7](https://ref.ly/Matt3:7)) described a situation involving *levirate* marriage (see [Gen 38:6–11](https://ref.ly/Gen38:6-Gen38:11); [Deut 25:5–6](https://ref.ly/Deut25:5-Deut25:6)), which they considered proof that resurrection from the dead is not possible.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:23
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:23–33 (id: 21942)

The resurrection was an important issue of Jesus’ day, but the question was raised only to trap Jesus.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:23–MAT 22:33
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:29 (id: 21944)

The power of God most likely refers to God’s ability to raise the dead.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:29
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:30 (id: 21947)

like the angels in heaven: Jesus was not teaching genderlessness (i.e., androgyny) nor disparaging the divine order of marriage and sexuality; rather, he was affirming that people will be transformed into a glorious new existence (see [1 Cor 15:35–49](https://ref.ly/1Cor15:35-1Cor15:49); [2 Cor 5:1–5](https://ref.ly/2Cor5:1-2Cor5:5)) in which aspects of the present order, such as marriage, will not be present.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:30
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:31–32 (id: 21948)

Since God spoke of being the God of Abraham in the present tense, this proves that Abraham still lives and thus that there is a resurrection.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:31–MAT 22:32
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:36 (id: 21949)

Since many strict Jews saw all commandments as equally binding, a careless response to this question could lead to the accusation of undermining the law of God.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:36
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:37 (id: 21950)

Jesus answers from the Shema ([Deut 6:4–9](https://ref.ly/Deut6:4-Deut6:9)), one of the core statements of God’s covenant with Israel (The first Hebrew word of [Deut 6:4–9](https://ref.ly/Deut6:4-Deut6:9) is shema‘, “hear”).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:37
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:39 (id: 21951)

Love your neighbor as yourself: [Lev 19:18](https://ref.ly/Lev19:18); see also [Rom 13:9](https://ref.ly/Rom13:9); [Gal 5:6](https://ref.ly/Gal5:6), [14](https://ref.ly/Gal5:14); [Jas 2:8](https://ref.ly/Jas2:8).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:39
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:40 (id: 21952)

are based on: Jesus’ statement affirmed the unity and coherence of God’s will, as recorded in Scripture.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:40
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:41–46 (id: 21953)

Having successfully defended himself against his opponents’ traps ([21:23–22:40](https://ref.ly/Matt21:23-Matt22:40)), Jesus questioned them as to how the Messiah can be called both the son of David and, at the same time, the Lord of David ([Ps 110:1](https://ref.ly/Ps110:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:41–MAT 22:46
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:42 (id: 21954)

the son of David: See study note on Matt 9:27; see also [2 Sam 7:12–14](https://ref.ly/2Sam7:12-2Sam7:14); [Pss 2:7–9](https://ref.ly/Ps2:7-Ps2:9); [110](https://ref.ly/Ps110:1-Ps110:7); [Isa 11:1](https://ref.ly/Isa11:1), [10](https://ref.ly/Isa11:10); [Jer 23:5–6](https://ref.ly/Jer23:5-Jer23:6).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:42
* **Associated Articles:** Matthew 9:27 (ID: 22282)

## Matthew 22:44 (id: 21955)

The quotation is from [Ps 110:1](https://ref.ly/Ps110:1), which is frequently cited by New Testament authors to describe Jesus (see [Acts 2:34–35](https://ref.ly/Acts2:34-Acts2:35); [1 Cor 15:25](https://ref.ly/1Cor15:25); [Heb 1:13](https://ref.ly/Heb1:13); [2:8](https://ref.ly/Heb2:8); [10:12–13](https://ref.ly/Heb10:12-Heb10:13); [Rev 3:21](https://ref.ly/Rev3:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:44
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:45 (id: 21956)

how can the Messiah be his son? The answer is that Jesus is more than the son of David: He is the Son of God ([14:33](https://ref.ly/Matt14:33)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:45
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 22:46 (id: 21957)

No one could answer him because they had never thought the Messiah would be God as a human being in the flesh (see [John 1:1–14](https://ref.ly/John1:1-John1:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 22:46
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:1 (id: 21968)

The religious leaders had sought a reason to accuse Jesus publicly ([21:23–22:46](https://ref.ly/Matt21:23-Matt22:46)) but found none. Jesus now turned to the crowds and to his disciples to openly indict the religious leaders for their numerous failures to conform to God’s righteous standards.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:1
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:1–25.46 (id: 21961)

This final extended discourse (see study note on Matt 5:1–7:29) centers on judgment for rejecting the Messiah.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:1
* **Associated Articles:** Matthew 5:1-7.29 (ID: 22169)

## Matthew 23:2 (id: 21974)

the Pharisees are the official interpreters of the law of Moses: They transmitted the oral traditions that were associated with the law and thought to be from Moses, and they judged religious and social matters on the basis of these traditions (see [15:2](https://ref.ly/Matt15:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:2
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:3 (id: 21980)

practice and obey: This was not a blanket endorsement of all that the Pharisees teach (see [15:1–20](https://ref.ly/Matt15:1-Matt15:20); [16:5–12](https://ref.ly/Matt16:5-Matt16:12); [23:13–39](https://ref.ly/Matt23:13-Matt23:39)). It might refer only to what was in accord with the law of Moses, or it might be bitter irony or sarcasm. Jesus might also have been counseling conformity to the Pharisees’ teachings to avoid giving offense ([17:24–27](https://ref.ly/Matt17:24-Matt17:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:3
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:4 (id: 21981)

unbearable religious demands: There were 613 legal prohibitions and commands, according to the rabbis (see [11:28–30](https://ref.ly/Matt11:28-Matt11:30); [Acts 15:10](https://ref.ly/Acts15:10), [28](https://ref.ly/Acts15:28)). • never lift a finger: The religious leaders were unwilling to consider relaxing traditional legal statutes.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:4
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:5 (id: 21982)

prayer boxes: Pious Jews wore, on the head and upper left arm, a small pouch or box (phylactery) containing written copies of important Old Testament commands (see [Deut 6:6–9](https://ref.ly/Deut6:6-Deut6:9); [11:18–19](https://ref.ly/Deut11:18-Deut11:19)). • Wearing tassels was another custom associated with piety (see [Matt 9:20](https://ref.ly/Matt9:20); see also [Num 15:38–41](https://ref.ly/Num15:38-Num15:41)). Lengthening the tassels called attention to their wearer’s pious practices.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:5
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:6 (id: 21983)

The seats of honor in the synagogues were near the scrolls of the Torah and facing the congregation.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:6
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:7 (id: 21984)

Rabbi was a title of authority and respect.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:7
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:8 (id: 21986)

Rabbi: These men functioned in Judaism as mediators for dispensing knowledge about God (see [23:7](https://ref.ly/Matt23:7)). The new covenant, by contrast, has only one teacher*,* Jesus himself as Messiah (see [Jer 31:31–34](https://ref.ly/Jer31:31-Jer31:34)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:8
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:8–12 (id: 21985)

Jesus does not prohibit the use of titles (especially for one’s own father), but rather the assumption of undue honor by those who transmit knowledge about God. The community of Jesus is a group of equals, each of whom knows God (see [12:46–50](https://ref.ly/Matt12:46-Matt12:50); [18:15–20](https://ref.ly/Matt18:15-Matt18:20)). The terms Rabbi, Father, and Teacher are roughly equivalent.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:8–MAT 23:12
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:9 (id: 21987)

Writings from later Judaism provide ample evidence of revering the teachers by calling them Father (see, e.g., *Mishnah Eduyyoth* [1:4](https://ref.ly/Matt1:4)). • God … is your Father: See [6:9](https://ref.ly/Matt6:9); [Mal 2:10](https://ref.ly/Mal2:10); cp. [1 Cor 4:15](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:15).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:9
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:10 (id: 21962)

Teacher: This title denotes the function and office of leading others into knowledge about God. Jesus, not the scribes and Pharisees, is the teacher of God’s will ([5:17](https://ref.ly/Matt5:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:10
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:11–12 (id: 21963)

Jesus’ disciples should lead by serving, in stark contrast to Israel’s religious leaders (who are described in [23:5–7](https://ref.ly/Matt23:5-Matt23:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:11–MAT 23:12
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:13 (id: 21965)

What sorrow awaits you: A stark warning of judgment from God. • Hypocrites! In English, hypocrisy describes a contradiction between reality and appearance. But in biblical usage, hypocrisy is misperceiving God’s will, leading people astray, and thus incurring God’s judgment. Coupled with this is often a desire for prestige and power ([23:5–12](https://ref.ly/Matt23:5-Matt23:12)), abuse of teaching authority, false teachings on doctrine or practice ([23:13–22](https://ref.ly/Matt23:13-Matt23:22)), and preoccupation with ethical minutiae ([23:23–28](https://ref.ly/Matt23:23-Matt23:28)). An accurate English term for this combination of factors is *heresy*. The Pharisees and teachers of religious law displayed all of these characteristics. As the Christian church began to grow, these characteristics continued to appear (e.g., [1 Tim 4:1–3](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:1-1Tim4:3); [2 Pet 2:1–22](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:1-2Pet2:22)), so God’s children always need to guard against them ([Jas 4:7–10](https://ref.ly/Jas4:7-Jas4:10); [1 Pet 2:1–3](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:1-1Pet2:3)). • shut the door of the Kingdom: By their false teaching and opposition to Jesus (see [Matt 9:32–34](https://ref.ly/Matt9:32-Matt9:34); [12:22–37](https://ref.ly/Matt12:22-Matt12:37); [15:12–14](https://ref.ly/Matt15:12-Matt15:14); [21:15](https://ref.ly/Matt21:15); [John 9:13–34](https://ref.ly/John9:13-John9:34)), the teachers of religious law and Pharisees prevented others from hearing and believing the truth about the Messiah.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:13
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:13–36 (id: 21964)

Matthew collected seven statements of what sorrow awaits you (literally *woe to you*), drawing upon similar Old Testament listings ([Isa 5:8–23](https://ref.ly/Isa5:8-Isa5:23); [Hab 2:6–20](https://ref.ly/Hab2:6-Hab2:20)), and he arranged them to climax in the murder of the prophets.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:13–MAT 23:36
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:15 (id: 21966)

A convert (proselyte) made a full conversion to Judaism, performing such observances as baptism, sacrifice, and circumcision (see [Acts 13:43](https://ref.ly/Acts13:43)). A convert was thus distinct from a “God\-fearer,” who adopted certain Jewish beliefs, most notably monotheism, without fully converting to Judaism (see [Luke 7:4–5](https://ref.ly/Luke7:4-Luke7:5); [Acts 10:2](https://ref.ly/Acts10:2)). It is likely that to make one convert means to persuade God\-fearers to become full converts to Judaism by undergoing circumcision (cp. [Gal 2:3](https://ref.ly/Gal2:3),[14](https://ref.ly/Gal2:14); [5:2–12](https://ref.ly/Matt5:2-Matt5:12); [6:12–13](https://ref.ly/Matt6:12-Matt6:13)). • of hell: Greek *of Gehenna;* see study note on 5:29.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:15
* **Associated Articles:** Matthew 5:29 (ID: 22185)

## Matthew 23:16–22 (id: 21967)

The religious leaders declared certain oaths less binding in order to commit fraud. Jesus calls for honest fulfillment of commitments (see [5:33–37](https://ref.ly/Matt5:33-Matt5:37)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:16–MAT 23:22
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:23 (id: 21969)

The teachers of religious law and Pharisees thought that meticulous tithing demonstrated their zeal for the law. Without denying the validity of the tithe*,* Jesus revealed how they had utterly failed to attend to the more important aspects of the law ([Isa 1:16–17](https://ref.ly/Isa1:16-Isa1:17); [Jer 22:3](https://ref.ly/Jer22:3); [Hos 6:6](https://ref.ly/Hos6:6); [Mic 6:8](https://ref.ly/Mic6:8); [Zech 7:9](https://ref.ly/Zech7:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:23
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:24 (id: 21970)

gnat … camel: These words form a pun in Aramaic (*qalma* … *gamla*), the language Jesus probably spoke.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:24
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:26 (id: 21971)

Internal purity will result in external righteousness, but the reverse is not true ([6:19–34](https://ref.ly/Matt6:19-Matt6:34); [12:33–37](https://ref.ly/Matt12:33-Matt12:37); [15:15–20](https://ref.ly/Matt15:15-Matt15:20)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:26
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:27–28 (id: 21972)

It was a Jewish custom to coat limestone tombs (perhaps funerary urns or ossuaries) with a mixture of marble and lime to fill their porous surfaces, giving them a more pleasing appearance and helping visitors to Jerusalem to notice the graves and avoid touching them so as not to contaminate themselves. Jesus is not criticizing the adorning of tombs; rather, he points to the similarity between these whitewashed tombs and the teachers of religious law and Pharisees. Both may have looked good on the outside, but both were contaminated and impure within.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:27–MAT 23:28
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:29 (id: 21973)

By building and decorating the tombs for the prophets*,* the teachers of religious law and Pharisees showed outward solidarity with the prophets, while inwardly they were of the same sinful character as their ancestors who had murdered the prophets.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:29
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:32 (id: 21975)

finish what your ancestors started: By killing God’s Messiah, they would bring to completion Israel’s history of killing God’s messengers (see [1 Thes 2:14–16](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:14-1Thess2:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:32
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:35 (id: 21976)

The span from Abel ([Gen 4:8–11](https://ref.ly/Gen4:8-Gen4:11)) to Zechariah ([2 Chr 24:15–22](https://ref.ly/2Chr24:15-2Chr24:22)) follows the order of the Hebrew Bible, in which 2 Chronicles is the last book. The implication is that this generation will be guilty of every murder of the righteous in the Old Testament (cp. [Matt 27:25](https://ref.ly/Matt27:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:35
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:37 (id: 21977)

Despite the severe judgment Jesus had just leveled against Israel ([23:29–36](https://ref.ly/Matt23:29-Matt23:36)), he truly longed for them to repent and receive God’s grace. • as a hen: An image of protective care (see also [Deut 32:11](https://ref.ly/Deut32:11); [Ruth 2:12](https://ref.ly/Ruth2:12); [Pss 17:8](https://ref.ly/Ps17:8); [36:7](https://ref.ly/Ps36:7); [57:1](https://ref.ly/Ps57:1); [61:4](https://ref.ly/Ps61:4); [91:4](https://ref.ly/Ps91:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:37
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:38 (id: 21978)

your house is abandoned and desolate: God would withdraw his presence from the Temple ([Ezek 10:18–19](https://ref.ly/Ezek10:18-Ezek10:19); [11:22–23](https://ref.ly/Ezek11:22-Ezek11:23); cp. [Matt 1:23](https://ref.ly/Matt1:23)), and both the Temple and Jerusalem would be destroyed.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:38
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 23:39 (id: 21979)

Blessings on the one who comes in the name of the Lord: This is possibly the prediction of an end\-time conversion of the nation of Israel to the Messiah (see also [Rom 11:12–32](https://ref.ly/Rom11:12-Rom11:32)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 23:39
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:1 (id: 21994)

The architecture of the Temple was a source of pride among Jews—see study note on Mark 13:1.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:1
* **Associated Articles:** Mark 13:1 (ID: 21327)

## Matthew 24:1–31 (id: 21988)

Some believe chapter [24](https://ref.ly/Matt24:1-Matt24:51) pertains to the return of Christ at the end of history. Others view the chapter as a prediction of the events of AD 70, when Jerusalem and the Temple were destroyed by the Romans. Others believe it refers to both. See also study notes on Mark 13.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:1–MAT 24:31
* **Associated Articles:** Mark 13:1-37 (ID: 21317)

## Matthew 24:2 (id: 22004)

Not one stone: The destruction of Jerusalem and the Temple was a sign of God’s judgment (see [1 Kgs 9:7–9](https://ref.ly/1Kgs9:7-1Kgs9:9); [Jer 7:8–15](https://ref.ly/Jer7:8-Jer7:15); [9:10–12](https://ref.ly/Jer9:10-Jer9:12); [26:6](https://ref.ly/Jer26:6), [18](https://ref.ly/Jer26:18); [Mic 3:12](https://ref.ly/Mic3:12); see also [Isa 64:11](https://ref.ly/Isa64:11); [Luke 19:44](https://ref.ly/Luke19:44); [Acts 6:14](https://ref.ly/Acts6:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:2
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:3 (id: 22014)

The Greek term translated return is parousia, which can mean *coming* or *appearing*. • end of the world (or *end of the age*): This expression refers to the climax and end of an epoch in salvation history (see [13:39–40](https://ref.ly/Matt13:39-Matt13:40), [49](https://ref.ly/Matt13:49); also [Heb 9:26](https://ref.ly/Heb9:26)). Jesus’ second coming will bring normal history to a close with decisive judgment. The disciples assumed that the destruction of the Temple and the end of history were closely connected.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:3
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:4–8 (id: 22015)

Jesus warned the disciples not to be deceived by impostors or overwhelmed by catastrophes in hope of a premature end to history. Time must run its predestined course. The signs predicted in [24:4–8](https://ref.ly/Matt24:4-Matt24:8) are not necessarily at the end; rather, they are signs prior to the end.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:4–MAT 24:8
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:5 (id: 22020)

claiming, ‘I am the Messiah’: A series of false prophets and miracle workers evoked messianic images and persuaded the masses to follow them in hope of deliverance during the period between AD 30 and 70 (Josephus, *Antiquities* 18\.4\.1; 20\.5\.1; 20\.8\.6; *War* 6\.5\.2\). The earliest recorded instance of an outright claim to be the Messiah was Bar Kochba’s claim in AD 132\. It is not clear whether Jesus is referring only to impostors in the period prior to the destruction of the Temple or to false messiahs throughout the church age or perhaps during a future tribulation.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:5
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:6 (id: 22021)

these things must take place: Tumultuous times are part of God’s sovereign plan as he brings history to a close (see [24:7](https://ref.ly/Matt24:7), [29–30](https://ref.ly/Matt24:29-Matt24:30); [2 Thes 2:8–12](https://ref.ly/2Thess2:8-2Thess2:12)). • The end could refer to the close of an epoch (such as at AD 70\) or the end of human history as we now know it (cp. [Matt 24:13–14](https://ref.ly/Matt24:13-Matt24:14); see also [10:22](https://ref.ly/Matt10:22); [13:39–40](https://ref.ly/Matt13:39-Matt13:40), [49](https://ref.ly/Matt13:49)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:6
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:8 (id: 22022)

first of the birth pains: Intense anguish is expected just prior to Jesus’ second coming (see also [24:29–31](https://ref.ly/Matt24:29-Matt24:31); [Isa 13:8](https://ref.ly/Isa13:8); [26:17](https://ref.ly/Isa26:17); [Jer 4:31](https://ref.ly/Jer4:31); [6:24](https://ref.ly/Jer6:24); [Mic 4:9–10](https://ref.ly/Mic4:9-Mic4:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:8
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:9 (id: 22023)

hated (see [Acts 28:22](https://ref.ly/Acts28:22)): At the end of the first century, the Roman historian Tacitus described Christians as “the hated ones of mankind” (Tacitus, *Annals* 15\.44\). The affliction of the righteous sometimes has the purpose of inciting repentance and obedience (see [Exod 4:31](https://ref.ly/Exod4:31); [Deut 4:30](https://ref.ly/Deut4:30); [Judg 10:6–16](https://ref.ly/Judg10:6-Judg10:16); [Pss 34:19](https://ref.ly/Ps34:19); [37:39](https://ref.ly/Ps37:39); [50:15](https://ref.ly/Ps50:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:9
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:10 (id: 21989)

Persecution will lead some to abandon loyalty to Jesus ([10:25](https://ref.ly/Matt10:25); [13:21](https://ref.ly/Matt13:21); [16:24–28](https://ref.ly/Matt16:24-Matt16:28); [26:33](https://ref.ly/Matt26:33)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:10
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:12 (id: 21990)

the love of many will grow cold (see [Rev 2:4](https://ref.ly/Rev2:4)): If the love within the community of Jesus’ disciples diminishes to the point of extinction, then the community ceases to be what God has designed it to be.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:12
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:13 (id: 21991)

The one who endures maintains faithful allegiance to Jesus despite persecution. Here, the end may refer to the end of one’s own life, the judgment on Israel in AD 70, or the end of history.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:13
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:14 (id: 21992)

throughout the whole world: This anticipates the expansive Gentile mission (see [21:43](https://ref.ly/Matt21:43); [28:16–20](https://ref.ly/Matt28:16-Matt28:20)). There will be a delay prior to the end*,* however short or long, during which the Good News will spread significantly throughout the nations. • The end will be signaled by a “sacrilegious object” ([24:15](https://ref.ly/Matt24:15)), furious persecution ([24:16–28](https://ref.ly/Matt24:16-Matt24:28)), and finally the sign of the Son of Man ([24:29–31](https://ref.ly/Matt24:29-Matt24:31)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:14
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:15 (id: 21993)

* *described by the prophet Daniel*: He spoke about the desecration (or *desolation*) of the temple (see [Daniel 8:13](https://ref.ly/Dan8:13); [9:27](https://ref.ly/Dan9:27); [11:31](https://ref.ly/Dan11:31); [12:11](https://ref.ly/Dan12:11)). It would be made unclean and ruined.
* *the abomination of desolation* could be:

    1. A false priest taking over the priesthood (see Josephus, *War* 4\.3\.6–10\).
        2. Unlawful images of God or humans, or certain people who cannot be in the temple. These people would include Antiochus Epiphanes, Caligula, Vespasian, or Titus (see Josephus, *War* 4\.4\.1–4\.7\.1\).
        3. The antichrist being present in the temple (compare *1 Maccabees* 1:54–64; *2 Maccabees* 8:17\). The term "antichrist" refers to a person or teaching that opposes Jesus Christ and his work.

* *let the reader understand:* This hidden message shows a special connection between the writer and reader, based on a shared belief that these events fulfill the prophecies of [Daniel 9](https://ref.ly/Dan9:1-Dan9:27), [11](https://ref.ly/Dan11:1-Dan11:45), and [12](https://ref.ly/Dan12:1-Dan12:13).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:15
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:20 (id: 21995)

Josephus records the winter swelling of the Jordan River, which made it more difficult to cross (see Josephus, *War* 4\.7\.5\). Muddy roads also made travel difficult in winter. • Normally Jews did not travel on the Sabbath in order to rest as God had commanded (see [Gen 2:1–3](https://ref.ly/Gen2:1-Gen2:3); [Exod 20:8–11](https://ref.ly/Exod20:8-Exod20:11); [23:12](https://ref.ly/Exod23:12); [31:12–17](https://ref.ly/Exod31:12-Exod31:17); [Lev 23:3](https://ref.ly/Lev23:3); [Deut 5:12–15](https://ref.ly/Deut5:12-Deut5:15); [Jer 17:19–27](https://ref.ly/Jer17:19-Jer17:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:20
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:21 (id: 21996)

greater anguish: Similar language is found in [Neh 9:37](https://ref.ly/Neh9:37); [Jer 11:16](https://ref.ly/Jer11:16); [Dan 12:1](https://ref.ly/Dan12:1); [Joel 2:1–17](https://ref.ly/Joel2:1-Joel2:17). The blatant savagery of the times has been documented by Josephus (see *War* 5\.10\.2–3\).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:21
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:22 (id: 21997)

God’s chosen ones endure ([24:13](https://ref.ly/Matt24:13)) and remain faithful ([24:37–25:46](https://ref.ly/Matt24:37-Matt25:46); see [Isa 65:8–9](https://ref.ly/Isa65:8-Isa65:9); [Rom 11:7](https://ref.ly/Rom11:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:22
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:24 (id: 21998)

false messiahs and false prophets (see [7:15](https://ref.ly/Matt7:15); [24:4–8](https://ref.ly/Matt24:4-Matt24:8); also [Acts 13:6](https://ref.ly/Acts13:6); [2 Pet 2:1](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:1); [1 Jn 2:18](https://ref.ly/1John2:18); [4:1](https://ref.ly/1John4:1)): Revelation describes a particular false prophet (see [Rev 16:13](https://ref.ly/Rev16:13)). • signs and wonders: Not all miracles are proof of God’s approval (see [Deut 13:1–4](https://ref.ly/Deut13:1-Deut13:4); [Rev 13:13](https://ref.ly/Rev13:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:24
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:26 (id: 22000)

Some Jewish prophets persuaded the masses to follow them into the desert to see signs of deliverance (cp. [24:4–8](https://ref.ly/Matt24:4-Matt24:8)). • hiding here: This is perhaps a reference to secretive sects, such as those at Qumran, or to the small fellowship groups associated with the Pharisees.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:26
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:26–28 (id: 21999)

These verses are an expansion of [24:23](https://ref.ly/Matt24:23). The place and manner of the Messiah’s appearing was disputed among Jews. The Messiah’s glorious appearance and vindication will be unmistakable.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:26–MAT 24:28
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:27–28 (id: 22001)

Lightning may be an allusion to the astrological phenomena attending the Messiah’s coming (see [24:29–31](https://ref.ly/Matt24:29-Matt24:31); [1 Thes 4:13–18](https://ref.ly/1Thess4:13-1Thess4:18)). It is not the suddenness of lightning that is in view but rather the magnitude of its visibility. Very possibly, Jesus gave these sayings to ward off premature excitement regarding the end ([1 Thes 4:13–5:10](https://ref.ly/1Thess4:13-1Thess5:10); [2 Thes 2:1–12](https://ref.ly/2Thess2:1-2Thess2:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:27–MAT 24:28
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:29 (id: 22003)

the sun will be darkened … will be shaken: This phenomenon can be taken literally, as befitting the climactic self\-disclosure of God’s Son, or metaphorically, as for a cosmically significant event (see [Acts 2:17–21](https://ref.ly/Acts2:17-Acts2:21); [Heb 12:26–27](https://ref.ly/Heb12:26-Heb12:27); [2 Pet 3:10](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:10); [Rev 6:12–13](https://ref.ly/Rev6:12-Rev6:13)). Similar apocalyptic language is used frequently in the Old Testament for describing political disasters and the collapse of a government as cosmic judgments from God (e.g., [Isa 13:9–16](https://ref.ly/Isa13:9-Isa13:16); [Ezek 32:1–10](https://ref.ly/Ezek32:1-Ezek32:10); [Joel 2:1–17](https://ref.ly/Joel2:1-Joel2:17); [Amos 8:7–10](https://ref.ly/Amos8:7-Amos8:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:29
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:29–31 (id: 22002)

These sayings form the climax of the discourse and answer the second of the disciples’ initial questions (see [24:3](https://ref.ly/Matt24:3)). Some take [24:29–31](https://ref.ly/Matt24:29-Matt24:31) to refer to God’s judgment on the Jewish people in AD 70, using apocalyptic images and metaphors to describe it. Others see a reference to the second coming of Christ at the end of history.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:29–MAT 24:31
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:30 (id: 22005)

the sign that the Son of Man is coming (literally *the sign of the Son of Man*): The sign is probably the Son of Man himself (see [12:38–42](https://ref.ly/Matt12:38-Matt12:42); [16:4](https://ref.ly/Matt16:4)).
