His coming expresses his vindication (see [26:64](https://ref.ly/Matt26:64)) and will bring deep mourning to those who experience God’s judgment. • All the peoples of the earth could be translated *all the tribes of the land.* The term used here is not the usual Greek term for Gentile nations (ethnoi), but a term used frequently of the tribes (phulai) of Israel (*the land*), suggesting that a national disaster in Israel might be in view (see [21:43](https://ref.ly/Matt21:43); [Zech 12:10–14](https://ref.ly/Zech12:10-Zech12:14)). • the Son of Man coming on the clouds: See [Dan 7:13](https://ref.ly/Dan7:13). Many believe that this means a descent of the Son of Man from God’s presence to reside on earth as Judge and Deliverer—i.e., the second coming of Christ. Others have argued that this describes the Son of Man coming in judgment, but not necessarily the second coming of Christ (see [Matt 10:23](https://ref.ly/Matt10:23); [16:27](https://ref.ly/Matt16:27); [19:28](https://ref.ly/Matt19:28); [25:31](https://ref.ly/Matt25:31); [26:64](https://ref.ly/Matt26:64); [28:18](https://ref.ly/Matt28:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:30
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:31 (id: 22006)

Many believe that the rapture of God’s people through angels ([13:41](https://ref.ly/Matt13:41); [16:27](https://ref.ly/Matt16:27); [25:31](https://ref.ly/Matt25:31)) is predicted here. Others believe that angels (Greek *angeloi,* “messengers”) here are human messengers ([11:10](https://ref.ly/Matt11:10); [Luke 7:24](https://ref.ly/Luke7:24); [9:52](https://ref.ly/Luke9:52); [Jas 2:25](https://ref.ly/Jas2:25)) and that Jesus is describing the expansion of the Good News among Gentiles (see [Matt 21:33–46](https://ref.ly/Matt21:33-Matt21:46); [22:1–14](https://ref.ly/Matt22:1-Matt22:14); [Deut 30:1–10](https://ref.ly/Deut30:1-Deut30:10); [Isa 27:13](https://ref.ly/Isa27:13); [Zech 2:6–13](https://ref.ly/Zech2:6-Zech2:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:31
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:33 (id: 22007)

all these things: This expression, used first in [23:36](https://ref.ly/Matt23:36) (“this judgment”), refers to the events associated with the destruction of the Temple (see [24:2](https://ref.ly/Matt24:2), [8](https://ref.ly/Matt24:8)). • his return (literally *he* or *it*): It could mean Jesus’ return (see [Jas 5:9](https://ref.ly/Jas5:9); [Rev 3:20](https://ref.ly/Rev3:20)), the destruction of the Temple, or the end of history (see [Luke 21:31](https://ref.ly/Luke21:31)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:33
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:34 (id: 22008)

this generation: In Matthew, *generation* is used particularly for contemporary, unbelieving Jews, especially focusing on the leaders who have led people away from the Messiah ([11:16](https://ref.ly/Matt11:16); [12:39](https://ref.ly/Matt12:39), [41–42](https://ref.ly/Matt12:41-Matt12:42), [45](https://ref.ly/Matt12:45); [16:4](https://ref.ly/Matt16:4); [23:36](https://ref.ly/Matt23:36)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:34
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:35 (id: 22009)

Jesus’ words are as sure as God’s own (see [5:18](https://ref.ly/Matt5:18); [Isa 40:8](https://ref.ly/Isa40:8); [55:11](https://ref.ly/Isa55:11); [59:21](https://ref.ly/Isa59:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:35
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:36 (id: 22010)

The day is the day of judgment. • or the Son: Jesus’ limited knowledge is suggested also in [Acts 1:7](https://ref.ly/Acts1:7). Because the day is unknown, Jesus’ hearers should be vigilant and faithful (see [Matt 24:37–25:46](https://ref.ly/Matt24:37-Matt25:46)). This statement ought to deter those who attempt to calculate the date of our Lord’s return.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:36
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:37 (id: 22013)

When the Son of Man returns: Jesus’ second coming (see [24:3](https://ref.ly/Matt24:3); cp. [Luke 17:26](https://ref.ly/Luke17:26)). • in Noah’s day (see [Gen 6:9–22](https://ref.ly/Gen6:9-Gen6:22); [2 Pet 2:5](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:5); [3:5–6](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:5-2Pet3:6)): The comparison here does not concern the magnitude of sins, but a lack of discernment about what God is doing, accompanied by a preoccupation with life’s festivities ([Matt 6:19–34](https://ref.ly/Matt6:19-Matt6:34)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:37
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:37–41 (id: 22012)

Jesus’ second coming, like the flood ([Gen 7](https://ref.ly/Gen7:1-Gen7:24)), will come upon people unawares. The only adequate preparation is a life of consistent vigilance and obedience (cp. [Luke 17:26–27](https://ref.ly/Luke17:26-Luke17:27), [34–35](https://ref.ly/Luke17:34-Luke17:35)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:37–MAT 24:41
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:37–25.46 (id: 22011)

Jesus now applied his predictions ([24:1–36](https://ref.ly/Matt24:1-Matt24:36)) to his followers so they will be faithful and prepared for his second coming.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:37–MAT 25:46
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:40–41 (id: 22016)

The term taken most likely means taken in judgment, at AD 70 or at the end of history; left would then mean remaining to enter the new era of either the church (see [21:43](https://ref.ly/Matt21:43); [22:1–14](https://ref.ly/Matt22:1-Matt22:14)) or the Millennium.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:40–MAT 24:41
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:42 (id: 22017)

To keep watch is to maintain active, energetic, single\-minded obedience to the Lord (see [25:13](https://ref.ly/Matt25:13); [26:38–41](https://ref.ly/Matt26:38-Matt26:41)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:42
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:45 (id: 22019)

servant: It is possible that Jesus’ listeners would have thought of God’s special servants, the prophets and lawgivers; however, Jesus so frequently used *servant* figuratively that it is more likely a description of every disciple’s responsibility (see [10:24–25](https://ref.ly/Matt10:24-Matt10:25); [13:27–28](https://ref.ly/Matt13:27-Matt13:28); [18:23–35](https://ref.ly/Matt18:23-Matt18:35); [20:26](https://ref.ly/Matt20:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:45
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 24:45–51 (id: 22018)

This parable and the three that follow ([25:1–13](https://ref.ly/Matt25:1-Matt25:13), [14–30](https://ref.ly/Matt25:14-Matt25:30), [31–46](https://ref.ly/Matt25:31-Matt25:46)) each dramatize the need for faithful obedience during the delay of Jesus’ second coming.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 24:45–MAT 24:51
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:1 (id: 22027)

To meet the bridegroom is an image for the coming of the Messiah (see [Mark 2:19–20](https://ref.ly/Mark2:19-Mark2:20)). • Details of wedding customs during the period are not known. Some think that the bride was led to the home of the bridegroom, who would stay away until the time appointed for the wedding feast. The bridesmaids*,* who had already escorted the bride to the groom’s home, would then wait for news of his arrival and escort him to the feast ([Matt 25:10](https://ref.ly/Matt25:10)). Others think the groom may have come late in the night to the bride’s home, where he was announced. Then, after celebrating with the bride’s guests, the groom would take his bride under torches or lamps to his home.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:1
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:1–13 (id: 22024)

This parable reinforces the need for individuals to be watchful and to prepare for the return of Christ ([25:13](https://ref.ly/Matt25:13); see also [Luke 12:35–36](https://ref.ly/Luke12:35-Luke12:36)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:1–MAT 25:13
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:3 (id: 22037)

While some have speculated that the oil symbolizes something specific (such as the Holy Spirit), it probably merely supports the point that proper preparation for the second coming of Christ is needed.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:3
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:5 (id: 22040)

Both the prudent and the foolish bridesmaids sleep while waiting. The parable criticizes only the foolish bridesmaids’ failure to bring enough oil.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:5
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:6 (id: 22041)

The arrival of the bridegroom at midnight while the bridesmaids slept further highlights the fact that the second coming of Jesus will come suddenly, at a time that no one can anticipate ([24:42–51](https://ref.ly/Matt24:42-Matt24:51)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:6
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:14–30 (id: 22025)

This parable teaches that the Lord expects his servants to be faithful to the task given to them while waiting for his return. The delay of Christ’s return will cause some to turn to evil deeds ([24:48–49](https://ref.ly/Matt24:48-Matt24:49)), some to inactivity ([25:3](https://ref.ly/Matt25:3)), and some to fearful passivity ([25:18](https://ref.ly/Matt25:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:14–MAT 25:30
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:19 (id: 22026)

After a long time: This highlights the long delay of Christ’s return ([24:45–51](https://ref.ly/Matt24:45-Matt24:51)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:19
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:21 (id: 22028)

See [Matt 24:45–51](https://ref.ly/Matt24:45-Matt24:51); [Luke 16:10](https://ref.ly/Luke16:10). • Let’s celebrate together is a metaphor for the Father’s approval and perhaps for the messianic banquet (see [Matt 6:1](https://ref.ly/Matt6:1), [4](https://ref.ly/Matt6:4), [6](https://ref.ly/Matt6:6), [18](https://ref.ly/Matt6:18); [9:9–17](https://ref.ly/Matt9:9-Matt9:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:21
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:24 (id: 22029)

I knew you were … harsh: A false understanding of his master becomes this servant’s excuse for laziness.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:24
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:29 (id: 22030)

God gives abundant grace to those who are faithful with what they have already been given (see [13:12](https://ref.ly/Matt13:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:29
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:31 (id: 22032)

To sit upon his glorious throne is here a posture of judgment (see [19:28](https://ref.ly/Matt19:28); [22:44](https://ref.ly/Matt22:44); [Dan 7:13–14](https://ref.ly/Dan7:13-Dan7:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:31
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:31–46 (id: 22031)

This is a description of the final judgment of which Jesus had been warning (see [7:13–27](https://ref.ly/Matt7:13-Matt7:27); [8:10–12](https://ref.ly/Matt8:10-Matt8:12); [11:20–24](https://ref.ly/Matt11:20-Matt11:24); [12:38–42](https://ref.ly/Matt12:38-Matt12:42); [13:24–30](https://ref.ly/Matt13:24-Matt13:30), [36–43](https://ref.ly/Matt13:36-Matt13:43); [16:24–28](https://ref.ly/Matt16:24-Matt16:28); [24:37–25:30](https://ref.ly/Matt24:37-Matt25:30)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:31–MAT 25:46
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:33 (id: 22033)

The right hand is the place of honor ([Gen 48:13–20](https://ref.ly/Gen48:13-Gen48:20); [Ps 110:1](https://ref.ly/Ps110:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:33
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:34 (id: 22034)

prepared for you from the creation of the world: This might be a reference to God’s choosing individuals for salvation in eternity past (see [13:10–17](https://ref.ly/Matt13:10-Matt13:17); [Eph 1:4](https://ref.ly/Eph1:4); [Rev 17:8](https://ref.ly/Rev17:8)), or it might simply refer to the Kingdom itself as a place (cp. [Matt 25:41](https://ref.ly/Matt25:41)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:34
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:35–36 (id: 22035)

The deeds described here, often called “deeds of mercy,” were acts of compassion shown to the helpless (see [Isa 58:1–12](https://ref.ly/Isa58:1-Isa58:12); [Ezek 18:7](https://ref.ly/Ezek18:7); [Jas 1:26–27](https://ref.ly/Jas1:26-Jas1:27)). These good deeds are not attempts to merit God’s favor; rather, they arise from a love for Christ that results in compassion toward others (see [6:1–4](https://ref.ly/Matt6:1-Matt6:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:35–MAT 25:36
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:37 (id: 22036)

These righteous ones (see [5:6](https://ref.ly/Matt5:6), [20](https://ref.ly/Matt5:20)) are those who do God’s will as taught by Jesus, expressed most clearly in deeds of love ([7:12](https://ref.ly/Matt7:12); [9:9–13](https://ref.ly/Matt9:9-Matt9:13); [22:34–40](https://ref.ly/Matt22:34-Matt22:40); [25:35–40](https://ref.ly/Matt25:35-Matt25:40)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:37
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:40 (id: 22038)

my brothers and sisters: This expresses either Jesus’ solidarity with his disciples (see [10:42](https://ref.ly/Matt10:42); [18:1–14](https://ref.ly/Matt18:1-Matt18:14); [Gal 6:10](https://ref.ly/Gal6:10)) or Jesus’ solidarity with humanity in general, irrespective of the faith of the one being helped (see [Matt 6:1–4](https://ref.ly/Matt6:1-Matt6:4); [25:43](https://ref.ly/Matt25:43); [Prov 19:17](https://ref.ly/Prov19:17)). The use of *brothers and sisters* points to the first interpretation ([Matt 12:46–50](https://ref.ly/Matt12:46-Matt12:50); [18:15–35](https://ref.ly/Matt18:15-Matt18:35); [23:8](https://ref.ly/Matt23:8); [28:10](https://ref.ly/Matt28:10)) but does not invalidate social responsibility for other people in general (see [Luke 10:30–37](https://ref.ly/Luke10:30-Luke10:37)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:40
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 25:46 (id: 22039)

The Greek term translated eternal can mean either “lasting forever” or “lasting for an age,” in this case “the age to come” ([13:39–40](https://ref.ly/Matt13:39-Matt13:40), [49](https://ref.ly/Matt13:49); [24:3](https://ref.ly/Matt24:3); [John 17:3](https://ref.ly/John17:3); [2 Thes 1:9](https://ref.ly/2Thess1:9); [Phlm 1:15](https://ref.ly/Phlm1:15); [1 Jn 5:11](https://ref.ly/1John5:11), [13](https://ref.ly/1John5:13)). Some hold out hope that the punishment of the damned will, after “an age,” be ended by annihilation or forgiveness. The parallel between eternal life and eternal punishment suggests strongly that it means “lasting forever,” since eternal life does not end (see also [Luke 16:19–31](https://ref.ly/Luke16:19-Luke16:31); [Heb 6:2](https://ref.ly/Heb6:2); [Rev 20:10](https://ref.ly/Rev20:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 25:46
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:2 (id: 22053)

The irony is that the Son of Man, who is to judge the nations ([25:31–46](https://ref.ly/Matt25:31-Matt25:46)), must first be wrongly judged and condemned to death by evil people. Jesus’ death was the ultimate Passover sacrifice (see [John 19:31–37](https://ref.ly/John19:31-John19:37); [1 Cor 5:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:2
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:3 (id: 22063)

The residence of Caiaphas, the high priest*,* was near the Temple in Jerusalem’s Upper City. Since it was not the normal meeting place, this gathering was *ad hoc*, urgent, and probably secretive. The council chamber, the traditional meeting place for the Sanhedrin, was located either at the southern end of the Court of the Israelites in the Temple, or on the western edge of the Temple hill. • Joseph Caiaphas*,* son\-in\-law of Annas (see [John 18:13](https://ref.ly/John18:13)), was high priest from AD 18 to 36 ([John 11:49](https://ref.ly/John11:49)), the longest tenure of any high priest from the time of Herod’s rule until AD 70\. His father\-in\-law, Annas, had been deposed but continued to be called high priest as well (see [Luke 3:2](https://ref.ly/Luke3:2); [John 18:13](https://ref.ly/John18:13), [19–24](https://ref.ly/John18:19-John18:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:3
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:5 (id: 22074)

Jerusalem was flooded with pilgrims at Passover*,* and the Jewish leaders worried about having their authority taken away if they caused or allowed anything that resembled revolt against Rome (see [21:8–11](https://ref.ly/Matt21:8-Matt21:11), [14–16](https://ref.ly/Matt21:14-Matt21:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:5
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:6 (id: 22083)

Simon, a man who had previously had leprosy: Jesus’ presence in the man’s home exhibited the forgiving, healing love Jesus often showed toward outcasts (see [8:7](https://ref.ly/Matt8:7); [9:10](https://ref.ly/Matt9:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:6
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:6–13 (id: 22075)

A similar anointing took place earlier in Galilee ([Luke 7:36–50](https://ref.ly/Luke7:36-Luke7:50)). Matthew’s insertion of the episode at this point (cp. [John 12:1–8](https://ref.ly/John12:1-John12:8)) sets the Jewish leaders’ murderous plotting ([Matt 26:3–5](https://ref.ly/Matt26:3-Matt26:5)) and Judas’s betrayal ([26:14–16](https://ref.ly/Matt26:14-Matt26:16)) in sharp contrast to the woman’s praiseworthy actions.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:6–MAT 26:13
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:7 (id: 22086)

The jar of expensive perfume was a burial ointment (see [Mark 16:1](https://ref.ly/Mark16:1); [Luke 23:56–24:1](https://ref.ly/Luke23:56-Luke24:1); [John 12:1–7](https://ref.ly/John12:1-John12:7); [19:38–42](https://ref.ly/John19:38-John19:42)) made of nard, which was harvested in India. The value of this jar of perfume was nearly a year’s wages ([John 12:5](https://ref.ly/John12:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:7
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:8 (id: 22087)

The disciples were indignant: [John 12:4](https://ref.ly/John12:4) indicates that Judas Iscariot incited this reaction.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:8
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:12 (id: 22042)

to prepare my body for burial: It is not clear whether the woman fully understood the significance of her actions. In addition to preparation for burial, the anointing also speaks of Jesus as king ([1 Sam 10:1](https://ref.ly/1Sam10:1); [2 Kgs 9:6](https://ref.ly/2Kgs9:6)) and priest ([Exod 29:7](https://ref.ly/Exod29:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:12
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:14–16 (id: 22043)

Judas sold himself to the authorities (see also [John 11:57](https://ref.ly/John11:57)), concealed it ([Matt 26:25](https://ref.ly/Matt26:25)), and then took them to Jesus at the appropriate time so they could carry out their plans ([26:47–56](https://ref.ly/Matt26:47-Matt26:56); see [John 18:2](https://ref.ly/John18:2)). Later, Judas was overcome by guilt and committed suicide ([Matt 27:3–10](https://ref.ly/Matt27:3-Matt27:10); see [Acts 1:15–22](https://ref.ly/Acts1:15-Acts1:22)). Judas was apparently known for his greed ([Matt 26:14–15](https://ref.ly/Matt26:14-Matt26:15); [John 12:4–6](https://ref.ly/John12:4-John12:6); [13:29](https://ref.ly/John13:29)). It is also possible that he was motivated by disappointment over the nature of Jesus’ reign as Messiah, his own humiliation over the anointing of Jesus (see [John 12:1–8](https://ref.ly/John12:1-John12:8)), or resentment over the leadership of the Galilean apostles, Peter, James, and John. Whatever his motivation, Judas’s betrayal was a part of God’s sovereign plan ([Acts 1:16–17](https://ref.ly/Acts1:16-Acts1:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:14–MAT 26:16
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:18 (id: 22044)

My time: The Messiah would now complete the work for which he was commissioned, to die for the sins of the world.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:18
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:23 (id: 22045)

eaten from this bowl with me: It was the custom for everyone present to dip their food into a common bowl, which probably contained herbs and fruit puree. Sharing a meal was a sign of friendship and trust, making a betrayer’s presence all the more startling ([26:21](https://ref.ly/Matt26:21); but see [John 13:26](https://ref.ly/John13:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:23
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:24 (id: 22046)

as the Scriptures declared: Jesus might have been referring to [Isa 53:7–9](https://ref.ly/Isa53:7-Isa53:9) or to the broader Old Testament theme of a suffering Messiah. This verse combines God’s sovereign will with human responsibility.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:24
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:25 (id: 22047)

Judas referred to Jesus as Rabbi*,* while the other disciples call him “Lord” ([26:22](https://ref.ly/Matt26:22)). • “You have said it”: This enigmatic statement affirmed that Judas was the betrayer.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:25
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:26 (id: 22049)

The unleavened bread of the Passover ([Exod 12:18](https://ref.ly/Exod12:18)) is also described as the “bread of suffering” ([Deut 16:3](https://ref.ly/Deut16:3)), referring to hardships in Egypt. • The customary blessing over the bread in the Passover meal was “Blessed are you, O Lord our God, King of the universe, who brings forth bread from the earth.”

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:26
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:26–29 (id: 22048)

The Last Supper derives its significance in part from the Jewish Passover (see [Exod 12](https://ref.ly/Exod12:1-Exod12:51)). The phases of the Jewish liturgy for Passover are as follows: (1\) Festal blessing; (2\) first cup (see [Luke 22:17–18](https://ref.ly/Luke22:17-Luke22:18)); (3\) eating bitter herbs (see [Matt 26:23](https://ref.ly/Matt26:23) and corresponding study note); (4\) eating unleavened bread ([26:26](https://ref.ly/Matt26:26); [Mark 14:22](https://ref.ly/Mark14:22)); (5\) second cup is mixed; (6\) the Passover *haggadah* (reading) is given ([Exod 12](https://ref.ly/Exod12:1-Exod12:51)); (7\) first part of the *hallel* ([Pss 113–114](https://ref.ly/Ps113:1-Ps114:8); see study note on Pss 113–118); (8\) second cup is taken; (9\) blessing and eating of unleavened bread ([Matt 26:26](https://ref.ly/Matt26:26); [Mark 14:22](https://ref.ly/Mark14:22); [Luke 22:19](https://ref.ly/Luke22:19)); (10\) the Passover lamb is eaten; (11\) third cup ([Matt 26:27–28](https://ref.ly/Matt26:27-Matt26:28); [Mark 14:23–24](https://ref.ly/Mark14:23-Mark14:24); [Luke 22:20](https://ref.ly/Luke22:20)); (12\) fourth cup (see [Matt 26:29](https://ref.ly/Matt26:29)\[?]; [Mark 14:25](https://ref.ly/Mark14:25)\[?]); (13\) time of fellowship; (14\) second part of the *hallel* ([Pss 115–118](https://ref.ly/Ps115:1-Ps118:29); see [Matt 26:30](https://ref.ly/Matt26:30)). None of the New Testament accounts of the Last Supper includes every aspect of a typical Jewish Passover. However, the most important aspects of the Passover that gave meaning to the early Christian celebration of the Lord’s Supper are included (see [1 Cor 11:23–25](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:23-1Cor11:25)). Jesus, the Lamb of God, is the ultimate Passover lamb and the perfect sacrifice for sin. • this is my body … my blood: Ever since the Reformation, there have been three dominant interpretations of Jesus’ statements concerning the bread and the wine: (1\) that the bread and wine change into the actual body and blood of Jesus Christ (*transubstantiation*); (2\) that Christ is mysteriously present in the sacrament either spiritually (*real presence*) or “in, with, and under” the bread and wine (*consubstantiation*); (3\) that the bread and wine symbolize the body and blood of Christ, benefiting the recipient through the Spirit by faith (*symbolism*).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:26–MAT 26:29
* **Associated Articles:** Matthew 26:23 (ID: 22045); Psalms 113:1-118.29 (ID: 23856)

## Matthew 26:27 (id: 22050)

He gave thanks. The traditional blessing for the Passover cup was “Blessed are you, O Lord our God, King of the universe, who creates the fruit of the vine.” An early Christian variant is, “We give thanks to you, our Father, for the Holy Vine of David, your child, whom you made known to us through Jesus your child; glory be to you forever” (*Didache* 9\.2\). • The four cups of the Passover meal correspond to the fourfold promise of [Exod 6:6–7](https://ref.ly/Exod6:6-Exod6:7), with two for deliverance, one for redemption (see [Matt 26:27–28](https://ref.ly/Matt26:27-Matt26:28)), and one for fellowship (see [26:29](https://ref.ly/Matt26:29)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:27
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:28 (id: 22051)

the covenant: Under God’s covenant with Israel, the blood of sheep or goats ([Exod 12:5](https://ref.ly/Exod12:5), [13](https://ref.ly/Exod12:13); [24:8](https://ref.ly/Exod24:8)) was shed and placed on the two doorposts and on the lintel at Passover ([Exod 12:7](https://ref.ly/Exod12:7)). The blood of Jesus, the sinless Lamb of God, establishes a new covenant (see [Jer 31:31](https://ref.ly/Jer31:31)). The idea of the *covenant* is God’s unilateral commitment to establish salvation for mankind, fulfilling the promise to Abraham (see [Gen 12](https://ref.ly/Gen12:1-Gen12:20); [Gal 3:15–29](https://ref.ly/Gal3:15-Gal3:29); [4:12–31](https://ref.ly/Gal4:12-Gal4:31)). • to forgive the sins of many: Jesus shed his blood as a sacrifice for sin (see [Jer 31:31–34](https://ref.ly/Jer31:31-Jer31:34); [Mark 14:24](https://ref.ly/Mark14:24)). Some have understood *many* to refer only to God’s chosen people, while others have understood *many* to be an expression meaning “all” (cp. [Matt 20:28](https://ref.ly/Matt20:28)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:28
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:29 (id: 22052)

until the day: Though the Kingdom had been inaugurated in Jesus’ ministry, it awaits final consummation (see [1 Cor 15:20–28](https://ref.ly/1Cor15:20-1Cor15:28); [Rev 19–22](https://ref.ly/Rev19:1-Rev22:21)). • until the day I drink it new: The final consummation of the Kingdom is pictured as a feast like the Passover, symbolizing an eternal fellowship of love and peace.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:29
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:30 (id: 22054)

they sang a hymn: Some have suggested that the *Great Hallel* ([Ps 136](https://ref.ly/Ps136:1-Ps136:26)) was sung.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:30
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:31 (id: 22055)

God will strike: In [Zech 13:7–9](https://ref.ly/Zech13:7-Zech13:9), the Shepherd*,* God’s partner, is struck down (understood by Jesus as a prediction of his own death), and out of the scattered sheep emerge a purged, purified remnant of faithful ones ([Zech 13:8–9](https://ref.ly/Zech13:8-Zech13:9)). In the short term, the disciples would soon be scattered and deny association with Jesus ([Matt 26:34](https://ref.ly/Matt26:34), [56](https://ref.ly/Matt26:56), [69–75](https://ref.ly/Matt26:69-Matt26:75)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:31
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:32 (id: 22056)

Jesus foresaw a time of restoration for the disciples despite their imminent abandonment of him (see ch [28](https://ref.ly/Matt28:1-Matt28:20); [John 21](https://ref.ly/John21:1-John21:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:32
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:35 (id: 22057)

While Peter’s denial receives the most attention, all the other disciples denied or avoided association with Christ as well (see [26:56](https://ref.ly/Matt26:56)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:35
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:36 (id: 22059)

Gethsemane is the name of an olive orchard approximately 250 yards east of Jerusalem’s Golden Gate, overlooking the Kidron Valley on the edge of the Mount of Olives. Jesus and his disciples apparently met there often ([Luke 22:39–40](https://ref.ly/Luke22:39-Luke22:40); [John 18:1–2](https://ref.ly/John18:1-John18:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:36
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:36–46 (id: 22058)

This scene reveals the depth of Jesus’ awareness of the suffering that awaited him on the cross, as well as his utter commitment to God’s will (see [20:28](https://ref.ly/Matt20:28)). Expressions in [26:41–42](https://ref.ly/Matt26:41-Matt26:42) echo the Lord’s Prayer ([6:9–13](https://ref.ly/Matt6:9-Matt6:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:36–MAT 26:46
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:37 (id: 22060)

* *He took with Him Peter and the two sons of Zebedee:*Peter, James, and John were probably the leaders of the apostles. They received special revelation (Peter, James, and John were present at the Transfiguration, where they saw Jesus transformed on the mountain, [17:1–13](https://ref.ly/Matt17:1-Matt17:13)). They stayed with Jesus during this difficult time.
* Jesus felt *sorrow* and *distress* as he thought about the Father’s plan for him (see [27:45–46](https://ref.ly/Matt27:45-Matt27:46)). Though he had never sinned, Jesus would take on humanity’s sin so that people could become "the righteousness of God" in Jesus (2 Corinthians 5:21\).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:37
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:38 (id: 22061)

crushed with grief: See [John 12:27](https://ref.ly/John12:27); cp. [Pss 42:5–6](https://ref.ly/Ps42:5-Ps42:6), [11](https://ref.ly/Ps42:11); [43:5](https://ref.ly/Ps43:5).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:38
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:39 (id: 22062)

If it is possible: Jesus’ heart’s desire was for uninterrupted communion with the Father instead of coming under God’s wrath. • Yet I want your will to be done: His resolution to do the Father’s will was firm ([4:1–11](https://ref.ly/Matt4:1-Matt4:11); [16:23](https://ref.ly/Matt16:23); [John 6:38](https://ref.ly/John6:38)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:39
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:49 (id: 22064)

Judas … gave him the kiss: Judas’s use of a sign of affection to betray Jesus amplifies the heinousness of his betrayal.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:49
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:51 (id: 22065)

one of the men with Jesus: This was Peter ([John 18:26](https://ref.ly/John18:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:51
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:53 (id: 22066)

thousands (literally *twelve legions*): Jesus used Roman military language (a legion consisted of approximately 6,000 soldiers) to describe the aid he could receive from God. Jesus was not a helpless victim; he permitted his own arrest.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:53
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:54 (id: 22067)

For Jesus to have resisted would have impeded the fulfillment of God’s saving work (see [16:21–23](https://ref.ly/Matt16:21-Matt16:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:54
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:55 (id: 22068)

The leaders’ clandestine behavior was driven by fear of the masses who revered Jesus (see [21:26](https://ref.ly/Matt21:26), [46](https://ref.ly/Matt21:46); [26:3–5](https://ref.ly/Matt26:3-Matt26:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:55
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:56 (id: 22069)

It is not clear which of the Scriptures Jesus was alluding to—perhaps [Isa 53](https://ref.ly/Isa53:1-Isa53:12), or perhaps the Old Testament theme of a suffering Messiah in general. • As Jesus had predicted earlier that evening, all the disciples deserted him ([Matt 26:31–35](https://ref.ly/Matt26:31-Matt26:35)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:56
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:57–68 (id: 22071)

This hearing might have been little more than an unofficial preliminary hearing designed to establish consensus on the terms of the charges. The Jewish leaders were under considerable pressure to keep this incident secret, lest their actions cause a riot (see [21:26](https://ref.ly/Matt21:26), [46](https://ref.ly/Matt21:46); [26:5](https://ref.ly/Matt26:5), [55](https://ref.ly/Matt26:55); [John 11:45–53](https://ref.ly/John11:45-John11:53)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:57–MAT 26:68
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:57–27.26 (id: 22070)

The Gospels record Jesus as undergoing five hearings: (1\) an informal hearing before Annas ([John 18:13–24](https://ref.ly/John18:13-John18:24)); (2\) a night hearing before the Sanhedrin ([Matt 26:59–66](https://ref.ly/Matt26:59-Matt26:66)); (3\) a morning hearing before the Sanhedrin ([27:1–2](https://ref.ly/Matt27:1-Matt27:2)); (4\) a hearing before Herod Antipas ([Luke 23:6–12](https://ref.ly/Luke23:6-Luke23:12)); and (5\) a two\-stage trial before Pilate ([Matt 27:11–31](https://ref.ly/Matt27:11-Matt27:31); see [Luke 23:6–12](https://ref.ly/Luke23:6-Luke23:12)). It all amounts to two trials, a Jewish trial and a Roman trial.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:57–MAT 27:26
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:58 (id: 22072)

the high priest’s courtyard: This location suggests an *ad hoc* meeting of the Sanhedrin at the palace of the high priest ([26:3](https://ref.ly/Matt26:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:58
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:59 (id: 22073)

were trying to find witnesses: The verb tense suggests an extended, perhaps desperate, attempt to find any testimony that could lead to a formal accusation (see [Mark 14:55–56](https://ref.ly/Mark14:55-Mark14:56)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:59
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:60 (id: 22076)

could not use anyone’s testimony: The evidence was too insubstantial or inconsistent to meet their goal of a death sentence until two men came forward ([Deut 17:6](https://ref.ly/Deut17:6); [19:15](https://ref.ly/Deut19:15)) with testimonies that did not conflict.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:60
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:61 (id: 22077)

The charge is either a misunderstanding or a deliberate distortion of Jesus’ prediction of his death and resurrection (see [John 2:19–21](https://ref.ly/John2:19-John2:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:61
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:63 (id: 22078)

if you are the Messiah: This question from the high priest was prompted by [Zech 6:12](https://ref.ly/Zech6:12), which had predicted that the Messiah would rebuild the Temple (cp. [Matt 26:61](https://ref.ly/Matt26:61)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:63
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:64 (id: 22079)

You have said it: This purposefully enigmatic response is essentially an affirmative answer (see [26:25](https://ref.ly/Matt26:25); [27:11](https://ref.ly/Matt27:11)); Mark has “I Am” ([Mark 14:62](https://ref.ly/Mark14:62)). • you will see: By quoting [Dan 7:13](https://ref.ly/Dan7:13), Jesus affirmed that he was the Son of Man who would be vindicated and exalted by God. • seated in the place of power at God’s right hand: Literally *seated at the right hand of the power;* see [Ps 110:1](https://ref.ly/Ps110:1). Jews were reluctant to name God directly (see study note on Matt 5:4). • The expression coming on the clouds of heaven could refer either to the destruction of Jerusalem in AD 70 or to Jesus’ second coming at the end of history.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:64
* **Associated Articles:** Matthew 5:4 (ID: 22198)

## Matthew 26:65 (id: 22080)

*He has blasphemed:* Caiaphas thought Jesus had spoken against God (blasphemed) when Jesus claimed to be the Son of Man. The title "Son of Man" was very special. It described someone who shared God's glory and power ([Daniel 7:13–14](https://ref.ly/Dan7:13-Dan7:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:65
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:67–68 (id: 22081)

Such abuse fulfills [Isa 50:6](https://ref.ly/Isa50:6); [53:4–9](https://ref.ly/Isa53:4-Isa53:9) and Jesus’ own predictions ([Matt 16:21](https://ref.ly/Matt16:21); [17:22–23](https://ref.ly/Matt17:22-Matt17:23); [20:18–19](https://ref.ly/Matt20:18-Matt20:19); [26:2](https://ref.ly/Matt26:2); see also [Mark 14:65](https://ref.ly/Mark14:65)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:67–MAT 26:68
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:69–75 (id: 22082)

Peter’s denials fulfill Jesus’ prediction ([26:34](https://ref.ly/Matt26:34)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:69–MAT 26:75
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 26:73 (id: 22084)

your Galilean accent: Jews from Galilee had a distinctive accent, compared with those from Judea (cp. [4:13](https://ref.ly/Matt4:13) and corresponding study note).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:73
* **Associated Articles:** Matthew 4:13 (ID: 22154)

## Matthew 26:75 (id: 22085)

When the crowing of the rooster reminded Peter of Jesus’ prediction ([26:34](https://ref.ly/Matt26:34)), he was struck with sorrow.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 26:75
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:1 (id: 22094)

The charge of blasphemy ([26:65–66](https://ref.ly/Matt26:65-Matt26:66)), though sufficient for the death penalty among Jews, would not convince a Roman judge. Hence, the leading priests and the elders conspired together to prepare a more political charge consistent with capital offenses in Roman law (see [27:11–26](https://ref.ly/Matt27:11-Matt27:26); [Luke 23:2](https://ref.ly/Luke23:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:1
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:1–2 (id: 22088)

The Jewish leaders were ready to level charges against Jesus before Pilate so that he would order Jesus’ execution. Pilate, a Gentile, fulfills Jesus’ prediction ([20:19](https://ref.ly/Matt20:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:1–MAT 27:2
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:2 (id: 22101)

Tiberius Caesar appointed Pilate to be the governor (or *prefect*) of Judea. Pilate ruled primarily from Caesarea, not Jerusalem, from AD 26 to AD 36\. Though he had sovereign power in Judea, Pilate was ultimately responsible to the legate of Syria, the central authority in the eastern portion of the Roman Empire. Josephus records several instances where Pilate’s disregard for the sanctity of Jewish customs led to revolt.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:2
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:3 (id: 22109)

Judas was filled with remorse (Greek metamelomai), but he did not repent (Greek metanoeō), which would have changed his heart and resulted in obedience and a relationship with God based on faith.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:3
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:3–10 (id: 22102)

There are two accounts of Judas’s death—this one and [Acts 1:18–19](https://ref.ly/Acts1:18-Acts1:19). There are differences between the two: (1\) Matthew states that the priests bought the field ([Matt 27:6–7](https://ref.ly/Matt27:6-Matt27:7)), while Acts seems to suggest that Judas bought it ([Acts 1:18](https://ref.ly/Acts1:18)); (2\) Matthew reports that Judas committed suicide by hanging himself ([Matt 27:5](https://ref.ly/Matt27:5)), while Acts enigmatically refers to a fall and an abdominal rupture ([Acts 1:18](https://ref.ly/Acts1:18)); (3\) Matthew implies that the field of blood was so named because it became a place of burial ([Matt 27:7–8](https://ref.ly/Matt27:7-Matt27:8)), while Acts suggests that it was because of Judas’s violent death there ([Acts 1:19](https://ref.ly/Acts1:19)). The two accounts are compatible if one takes the account in Acts as describing the effects of the actions described in Matthew.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:3–MAT 27:10
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:4 (id: 22115)

an innocent man: Jesus’ innocence is a dominant theme in the narrative of his suffering (see [23:35](https://ref.ly/Matt23:35); [26:55–56](https://ref.ly/Matt26:55-Matt26:56), [59–60](https://ref.ly/Matt26:59-Matt26:60); [27:18–19](https://ref.ly/Matt27:18-Matt27:19), [24](https://ref.ly/Matt27:24); see also [Luke 23:47](https://ref.ly/Luke23:47)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:4
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:5 (id: 22122)

hanged himself: Judas’s suicide resulted from a guilt\-stricken, unrepentant conscience. His death satisfied Old Testament law regarding the punishment of a false witness (see [Deut 19:16–21](https://ref.ly/Deut19:16-Deut19:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:5
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:7 (id: 22124)

Foreigners were Gentiles who died in Jerusalem. An asset whose owner could not be traced was used for public charity. In this instance, unclean money was used to buy an unclean place for unclean people.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:7
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:8 (id: 22125)

Field of Blood is a way of describing a cemetery (cp. [Acts 1:18–19](https://ref.ly/Acts1:18-Acts1:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:8
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:9–10 (id: 22126)

the prophecy of Jeremiah: The citation is from [Zech 11:12–13](https://ref.ly/Zech11:12-Zech11:13). Matthew might merely have been conforming to the Jewish custom of citing books by referring to the first book in the particular scroll—the first book in the scroll containing Zechariah would have been Jeremiah. Or, Matthew might have thought of similar passages in Jeremiah ([Jer 19:1–13](https://ref.ly/Jer19:1-Jer19:13); [18:2–6](https://ref.ly/Jer18:2-Jer18:6); [32:6–15](https://ref.ly/Jer32:6-Jer32:15)) along with [Zech 11:12–13](https://ref.ly/Zech11:12-Zech11:13). • Matthew sees a striking resemblance between Zechariah’s actions and those of the leading priests. Both contexts deal with the rejection of God’s messenger who was to be king of God’s people.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:9–MAT 27:10
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:11 (id: 22090)

king of the Jews: The Sanhedrin’s original charge of blasphemy ([26:65–66](https://ref.ly/Matt26:65-Matt26:66); [27:1](https://ref.ly/Matt27:1)) held no interest to the Romans, who saw it as a Jewish religious question (cp. [Acts 25:18–20](https://ref.ly/Acts25:18-Acts25:20)). The charge was therefore changed to incriminate Jesus in Roman eyes as a political rebel (see [Luke 23:2](https://ref.ly/Luke23:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:11
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:11–26 (id: 22089)

The Roman trial included an initial hearing before Pilate ([27:11–14](https://ref.ly/Matt27:11-Matt27:14)), one before Herod Antipas ([Luke 23:6–16](https://ref.ly/Luke23:6-Luke23:16)), and a second hearing before Pilate ([Matt 27:15–26](https://ref.ly/Matt27:15-Matt27:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:11–MAT 27:26
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:15 (id: 22091)

Pilate’s custom seems out of character; he was not known for wanting to please his Jewish subjects. However, if Pilate’s position with Caesar was precarious at this point (see study note on John 19:12; see Philo, *On the Embassy to Gaius* 159–161\), then this gesture may have been to keep the peace and thus avoid negative attention from Rome.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:15
* **Associated Articles:** John 19:12 (ID: 19023)

## Matthew 27:16 (id: 22092)

notorious prisoner … named Barabbas: Elsewhere he is called a “revolutionary” ([Mark 15:7](https://ref.ly/Mark15:7); [John 18:40](https://ref.ly/John18:40)), a term that also denotes a robber or insurrectionist (see [Luke 23:19](https://ref.ly/Luke23:19)). To the zealots, Barabbas was a hero.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:16
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:19 (id: 22093)

through a terrible nightmare (cp. [1:20](https://ref.ly/Matt1:20)): It is ironic that a pagan recognizes and takes a stand for Jesus’ innocence, while the Jewish crowd does not.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:19
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:24 (id: 22095)

The responsibility is yours! The priests had said the same thing to Judas ([27:4](https://ref.ly/Matt27:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:24
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:25 (id: 22096)

all the people (see [21:43](https://ref.ly/Matt21:43)): This does not mean every living Jew. Instead, those urging Jesus’ condemnation are representative of all of unbelieving Israel, whose actions bring consequences for the nation as a whole (e.g., the destruction of Jerusalem in AD 70\). • We will take responsibility for his death—we and our children (see [23:35](https://ref.ly/Matt23:35); [2 Sam 1:16](https://ref.ly/2Sam1:16); [14:9](https://ref.ly/2Sam14:9); [Jer 51:35](https://ref.ly/Jer51:35); [Acts 5:28](https://ref.ly/Acts5:28); [18:6](https://ref.ly/Acts18:6); [20:26](https://ref.ly/Acts20:26)): Christians have at times misunderstood and misused this verse in persecution of Jews, but it is not an indictment against Jews in general.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:25
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:26 (id: 22097)

When a man was flogged*,* he was beaten with whips that had leather thongs at the end, some with sharp bone, lead*,* or rock fragments stuck to the ends of the thongs (see also [Deut 25:1–3](https://ref.ly/Deut25:1-Deut25:3); [1 Kgs 12:11](https://ref.ly/1Kgs12:11), [14](https://ref.ly/1Kgs12:14); [Acts 16:22](https://ref.ly/Acts16:22); [22:25](https://ref.ly/Acts22:25); [2 Cor 11:24–25](https://ref.ly/2Cor11:24-2Cor11:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:26
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:27 (id: 22099)

* *the governor's soldiers* were extra troops recruited from non\-Jewish residents of Palestine.
* The soldiers stayed at the governor's official building in Jerusalem. This building was called the Antonia Fortress. It stood at the northwest corner of the Temple area.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:27
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:27–31 (id: 22098)

In the Jewish trial Jesus was mocked as a prophet ([26:67–68](https://ref.ly/Matt26:67-Matt26:68)); here he is mocked as a king.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:27–MAT 27:31
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:28–29 (id: 22100)

The scarlet robe was probably the cloak of a soldier meant to emulate royal garb solely for the purpose of ridiculing Jesus. • Weaving thorn branches into a crown was a mockery of Jesus as king.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:28–MAT 27:29
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:32 (id: 22104)

Normally, the victim carried his own cross. Only the crossbeam was carried; the vertical pole would be waiting at the crucifixion site. Simon might have been forced because Jesus was weak from the effects of scourging. The act of enlisting Simon might also have been a further mockery. Jesus was treated as one who deserved a servant even though he was being marched to his death.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:32
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:32–44 (id: 22103)

Ironically, the taunts and ridicule of the crowd express the truth about Jesus: He is the Son of God and King of Israel, the Messiah.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:32–MAT 27:44
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:34 (id: 22105)

Giving Jesus wine mixed with bitter gall was probably intended for ridicule (see [Ps 69:21](https://ref.ly/Ps69:21)). It was also a sedative—Jesus probably rejected it in order to suffer fully for our sins (see [Isa 53:10](https://ref.ly/Isa53:10)). • Gall, otherwise known as wormwood, is a bitter narcotic made from the oil of Artemisia (cp. [Mark 15:23](https://ref.ly/Mark15:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:34
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:35 (id: 22106)

they … nailed him to the cross: Crucifixion, though not generally practiced by Jews, was a widespread Roman punishment for military and political offenders, particularly slaves, rebels, and insurrectionists. The sheer cruelty and the public spectacle of crucifixion worked as a powerful social deterrent. Victims were flogged and then crucified naked, adding to the humiliation. It was seen as the most painful of all possible deaths; it involved intense suffering, exposure to weather and insects, suffocation, and often a final violent thrust of a spear to end life. Further, since crucifixion was a curse from God ([Deut 21:22–23](https://ref.ly/Deut21:22-Deut21:23)), the act was particularly heinous to Jewish sensibilities. Paradoxically, what was so despicable among humans has become the instrument of our salvation. Jesus previously had instructed his disciples to take up their crosses and follow him ([Matt 16:24](https://ref.ly/Matt16:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:35
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:37 (id: 22107)

The official charge was fastened to the cross above the criminal’s head; Jesus was crucified for political sedition.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:37
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:38 (id: 22108)

Crucifying Jesus between two convicted revolutionaries added further humiliation and guilt by association.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:38
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:40 (id: 22110)

if you are the Son of God: This taunt recalls Jesus’ temptation at the very beginning of his public ministry ([4:1–11](https://ref.ly/Matt4:1-Matt4:11)), in which the devil appealed to Jesus’ privileged status in order to tempt him to avoid suffering (see also [16:21–23](https://ref.ly/Matt16:21-Matt16:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:40
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:45 (id: 22111)

Darkness symbolizes the judgment of God or, more specifically, the arrival of the day of the Lord (see [Amos 5:18](https://ref.ly/Amos5:18), [20](https://ref.ly/Amos5:20); [8:9–10](https://ref.ly/Amos8:9-Amos8:10); also [Jer 4:27–28](https://ref.ly/Jer4:27-Jer4:28); [13:16](https://ref.ly/Jer13:16); [15:9](https://ref.ly/Jer15:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:45
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:46 (id: 22112)

Eli, Eli: This cry means *My God, my God,* but the similarity in sound accounts for the people’s confusion ([27:47](https://ref.ly/Matt27:47)). • My God, my God, why have you abandoned me? Jesus was experiencing God’s wrath for the sins of humanity.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:46
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:47 (id: 22113)

It was widely believed that Elijah would return before the day of the Lord ([11:14–15](https://ref.ly/Matt11:14-Matt11:15); [17:10–13](https://ref.ly/Matt17:10-Matt17:13); [Mal 4:5](https://ref.ly/Mal4:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:47
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:48 (id: 22114)

The sour wine was vinegar. The drink was probably designed to mock Jesus (cp. [Ps 69:21](https://ref.ly/Ps69:21) with [Matt 27:34](https://ref.ly/Matt27:34)) by pretending to help assuage his thirst. Others have suggested that it was given as an act of genuine kindness.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:48
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:50 (id: 22116)

Each of the four Gospels highlights different aspects of Jesus’ last moments. • released his spirit: This emphasizes the sovereignty of Jesus in that he released himself to death (see also [John 19:30](https://ref.ly/John19:30)). • shouted out again (see [Matt 27:46](https://ref.ly/Matt27:46)): This cry was Jesus’ final prayer (see [Luke 23:46](https://ref.ly/Luke23:46)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:50
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:51 (id: 22117)

The significance of the splitting of the curtain in the Temple is that the wall dividing people from God has been torn down by the death of Jesus Christ (see also [Eph 2:11–22](https://ref.ly/Eph2:11-Eph2:22); [Heb 6:19](https://ref.ly/Heb6:19); [9:1–10:25](https://ref.ly/Heb9:1-Heb10:25)). • The earth shook, rocks split apart: These are portents of the arrival of judgment (see [Exod 19:18](https://ref.ly/Exod19:18); [Judg 5:4](https://ref.ly/Judg5:4); [Ps 18:7](https://ref.ly/Ps18:7); [Joel 3:14–17](https://ref.ly/Joel3:14-Joel3:17); [Amos 8:8–10](https://ref.ly/Amos8:8-Amos8:10)). Josephus records the appearance about AD 30 of a star resembling a sword and a spontaneous opening of the gates of the Temple (Josephus, *War* 6\.5\.3–4\).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:51
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:52–53 (id: 22118)

tombs opened: Jesus’ climactic death inaugurated the Kingdom of God by breaking the powers of death and establishing the final resurrection (see [Isa 26:19](https://ref.ly/Isa26:19); [Dan 12:2](https://ref.ly/Dan12:2); [1 Cor 15:1–58](https://ref.ly/1Cor15:1-1Cor15:58); [Col 1:18](https://ref.ly/Col1:18); [Heb 2:14–15](https://ref.ly/Heb2:14-Heb2:15)). • These godly ones either did not enter the city until after Jesus’ resurrection or they were not raised until then, with Jesus as the firstfruits (see [1 Cor 15:20](https://ref.ly/1Cor15:20), [23](https://ref.ly/1Cor15:23); [Col 1:18](https://ref.ly/Col1:18)). If that is the case, Matthew has included this episode to form a more powerful commentary on the impact of Jesus’ death.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:52–MAT 27:53
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:54 (id: 22119)

The Roman officer and the other soldiers were Gentiles. • the Son of God: This may be an unqualified affirmation that Jesus is the unique Son of God (see [14:33](https://ref.ly/Matt14:33); [16:16](https://ref.ly/Matt16:16)) or possibly a more general affirmation of Jesus’ innocence (see [Luke 23:47](https://ref.ly/Luke23:47)). They are responding to the earthquake and all that had happened as evidence of divine interest in this occasion.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:54
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:58 (id: 22120)

In Roman crucifixion, the bodies of criminals were often left to rot. [Deut 21:22–23](https://ref.ly/Deut21:22-Deut21:23) prohibits a body from remaining on a cross or a gallows overnight. Joseph’s action was in accordance with Jewish law, while his motivation was probably his loyalty to Jesus. • Pilate issued an order: Pilate was accommodating, probably because he did not believe Jesus was guilty of insurrection (see [Matt 27:24–26](https://ref.ly/Matt27:24-Matt27:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:58
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:59–60 (id: 22121)

Burial customs were important in Judaism, especially in contrast to the Greeks and Romans, who cremated their dead. Leaving a corpse unburied was the severest form of judgment ([Deut 21:22–23](https://ref.ly/Deut21:22-Deut21:23); [2 Kgs 9:37](https://ref.ly/2Kgs9:37); [Ps 79:3](https://ref.ly/Ps79:3); [Jer 16:4](https://ref.ly/Jer16:4), [6](https://ref.ly/Jer16:6); [Ezek 29:5](https://ref.ly/Ezek29:5); [Rev 11:9](https://ref.ly/Rev11:9)). Death was lamented and mourned ([Mark 5:38–39](https://ref.ly/Mark5:38-Mark5:39)); the body was washed ([Acts 9:37](https://ref.ly/Acts9:37)), anointed ([Matt 26:6–13](https://ref.ly/Matt26:6-Matt26:13); [John 12:3](https://ref.ly/John12:3), [7](https://ref.ly/John12:7); [19:39](https://ref.ly/John19:39)), and wrapped in burial cloths ([Matt 27:59](https://ref.ly/Matt27:59); see [Gen 50:2–3](https://ref.ly/Gen50:2-Gen50:3)). The body was placed in a tomb (see [Matt 23:27](https://ref.ly/Matt23:27)) that had been tunneled into a rock or carved into the side of a cave wall. The entrance to a tomb was often closed with a huge stone and sealed to prevent ceremonial uncleanness or robbery. • clean linen … new tomb: Both reflect ceremonial purity. Joseph had purchased the tomb for his own family, but it had not yet been used.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:59–MAT 27:60
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 27:62–66 (id: 22123)

This incident bolsters the truth of Jesus’ resurrection—it is inconceivable that Matthew would fabricate such a story since witnesses abounded who could have countered the claims.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 27:62–MAT 27:66
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 28:1 (id: 22134)

Mary Magdalene (see [27:56](https://ref.ly/Matt27:56)): The mention of two women as witnesses lends credibility to the historicity of the account—an inventor of tales would not have used women as witnesses, since a woman’s testimony was considered less reliable than a man’s.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 28:1
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 28:1–10 (id: 22127)

The discovery of the empty tomb and the various resurrection appearances are presented with different emphases in each of the four Gospels. Matthew focuses on the reunion in Galilee, the attempt on the part of the Jewish leaders to discredit the resurrection, and the significance of the resurrection for the salvation of the world.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 28:1–MAT 28:10
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 28:12 (id: 22128)

Such a bribe was contrary to the law (see [Exod 20:16](https://ref.ly/Exod20:16); [23:8](https://ref.ly/Exod23:8)). • elders: See study note on Matt 21:23.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 28:12
* **Associated Articles:** Matthew 21:23 (ID: 21912)

## Matthew 28:13 (id: 22129)

stole his body: Tomb robbery was a common problem in the ancient world, so such an accusation would have been entirely believable.

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 28:13
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 28:15 (id: 22130)

still tell it today: Justin Martyr wrote to Jews of his day (about AD 165\), “You have sent … men throughout all the world to proclaim, ‘A godless and lawless heresy has sprung from one Jesus, a Galilean deceiver, whom we crucified, but his disciples stole him by night from the tomb … and now \[the disciples] deceive men by asserting that he has risen from the dead and ascended into heaven’” (Justin Martyr, *Dialogue with Trypho* 108\). This misinformation probably became widespread after the disciples began to proclaim Jesus’ resurrection (see [Acts 2:22–36](https://ref.ly/Acts2:22-Acts2:36)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 28:15
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 28:17 (id: 22131)

some of them doubted: This might be a veiled reference to Thomas ([John 20:24–29](https://ref.ly/John20:24-John20:29)), but all eleven might have experienced a mixture of both worship and doubt (see also [Matt 14:31](https://ref.ly/Matt14:31); [Luke 24:10–11](https://ref.ly/Luke24:10-Luke24:11); [John 20:24–29](https://ref.ly/John20:24-John20:29)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 28:17
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 28:18 (id: 22132)

Jesus’ authority is power delegated from the Father (see [7:29](https://ref.ly/Matt7:29); [9:6–8](https://ref.ly/Matt9:6-Matt9:8); [21:23–27](https://ref.ly/Matt21:23-Matt21:27); [26:64](https://ref.ly/Matt26:64); [John 3:35](https://ref.ly/John3:35)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 28:18
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 28:19 (id: 22133)

go and: Literally *going*, a participle that supports the main imperative, make disciples. Matthew probably intended go to be understood as a separate command (as it is translated) and not as a circumstantial modifier (i.e., *while you go;* cp. the same construction in [9:6](https://ref.ly/Matt9:6); [Acts 10:20](https://ref.ly/Acts10:20)). • make disciples: A disciple is one who repents of sin, trusts in Jesus for salvation, and obeys his teachings. • all the nations: The mission to the Gentile nations formally began here (see [Matt 10:5–6](https://ref.ly/Matt10:5-Matt10:6); [15:24](https://ref.ly/Matt15:24); see also [1:1](https://ref.ly/Matt1:1); [2:1–12](https://ref.ly/Matt2:1-Matt2:12); [8:5–13](https://ref.ly/Matt8:5-Matt8:13); [21:43](https://ref.ly/Matt21:43); [24:14](https://ref.ly/Matt24:14); [26:13](https://ref.ly/Matt26:13)). • Two aspects of making disciples are baptizing and teaching ([28:20](https://ref.ly/Matt28:20)).. Baptism indicates public identification with, and surrender to, Jesus and the work he has done for salvation (see [3:13–17](https://ref.ly/Matt3:13-Matt3:17); [10:32–33](https://ref.ly/Matt10:32-Matt10:33); [20:28](https://ref.ly/Matt20:28); [26:28](https://ref.ly/Matt26:28); [Acts 2:38](https://ref.ly/Acts2:38); [Rom 6:1–11](https://ref.ly/Rom6:1-Rom6:11); [1 Pet 3:21](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:21)). • In the name of means entrance into a relationship and its benefits, which come to those who truly believe. • Father … Son … Holy Spirit: This is a formulaic expression for the nature of God as a trinity (see also [1 Cor 12:4–6](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:4-1Cor12:6); [2 Cor 13:14](https://ref.ly/2Cor13:14); [Eph 4:4–6](https://ref.ly/Eph4:4-Eph4:6); [2 Thes 2:13–14](https://ref.ly/2Thess2:13-2Thess2:14); [1 Pet 1:2](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:2); [Rev 1:4–6](https://ref.ly/Rev1:4-Rev1:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 28:19
* **Associated Articles:** 

## Matthew 28:20 (id: 22135)

Teach: The disciples’ curriculum is comprised of all the commands of Jesus (e.g., the Sermon on the Mount, chs [5–7](https://ref.ly/Matt5:1-Matt7:29)). The church is to be marked by its obedience to Jesus’ commands ([5:17–20](https://ref.ly/Matt5:17-Matt5:20); [7:13–27](https://ref.ly/Matt7:13-Matt7:27)). Jesus’ authority and presence are the basis for the disciples’ mission (see also [1:23](https://ref.ly/Matt1:23); [18:20](https://ref.ly/Matt18:20)).

* **Associated Passages:** MAT 28:20
* **Associated Articles:**
